

         英汉词汇手册

           4611条



abandon
abandon　［əˈbændən］
vt. 抛弃；放弃〈同 desert〉
例 The baby was abandoned by his teenage mother. 那个婴儿被他的未婚妈妈遗弃了。
n. 放纵〈同 unrestraint〉
例 The guests at the party danced with abandon. 聚会上的客人们尽情地跳舞。
联 abandonment n. 抛弃；放弃

abate
abate［ə'beɪt］
v. ① 减轻，降低 ② 缓和
解　① to reduce in amount, degree, or intensity; lessen ② to fall off in degree or intensity; subside
例　When the rain abated, we went outside again. 雨变小了之后，我们又出去了。
构　a (=to) + bat (=to beat) + e

abbreviate
abbreviate［ə'bri:vɪeɪt］
vt. ①缩短〈同　shorten, abridge〉
例　The President was asked to abbreviate his speech since the students crammed in the room without air-conditioning were running out of patience. 校长被要求缩短演讲时间，因为在没有空调的房间里，挤在一起的学生们正在失去耐心。
例　“Mister”is usually abbreviated as“Mr.”. Mister通常被缩写成Mr.。

abbreviate
abbreviate［ə'bri:vɪeɪt］
v. 缩写，缩短
解　to reduce in scope while retaining essential elements
例　John Paul abbreviated his name to J.P. 约翰·保罗把他的名字缩写成J.P.。
同　abbreviation n. 缩短，删节；缩写词，略语
构　ab <zad (=to) + brevi (=brief, short) + ate

abide
abide［ə'baɪd］
例　Players have to abide by the referee's decision. 参赛者必须遵守裁判的判定。
vt. 忍受〈同 endure, put up with〉
例　Many people can't abide the smell of cheap cigars. 许多人没法忍受廉价雪茄的气味。

abjure
abjure［æb'ʤʊə(r)］
v. 发誓放弃，誓绝
解　to renounce upon oath
例　Most aliens must abjure foreign citizenship before becoming an American citizen. 在成为美国公民之前，大多数外国人必须承诺放弃原来的公民身份。
构　ab (=away) + jur (=to swear) + e

ablaze
ablaze［ə'bleɪz］
adj. 着火的，燃烧的；闪耀的〈同　burning; bright〉
例　After the firewood was ablaze, he felt warm. 柴火点着之后，他才感到暖和。

abnormal
abnormal［æb'nɔ:məl］
adj. 反常的，异常的；变态的〈同 anomalous, unnatural〉
例　The warm December weather in Beijing is abnormal. 在北京，12月份还这么暖和是不正常的。

abnormal
abnormal［æb'nɔ:məl］
adj. 不正常的，变态的
解　deviating from the normal or average
例　The Elephant Man is a movie about a man who had an abnormal face. 《象人》是一部关于一个面部畸形的男人的电影。
构　ab (=from) + norm (=rule) + al

abolish
abolish［ə'bɒlɪʃ］
vt. 废除，取消〈同 eliminate〉
例　Slavery was abolished in the United States after the Civil War. 美国在南北战争以后废除了奴隶制。

abort
abort［ə'bɔ:t］
n.中止计划（或任务）〈同　failure, stop〉
例　The minister ordered a general abort in stamp production when he learned there was a mistake on the newly issued stamp. 在得知新发行的邮票上有错误后，部长命令全面中止邮票的生产。

abrasion
abrasion［ə'breɪʒən］
n.磨（擦）破；表面磨损〈同　scratch; friction〉
例　She fell and suffered an abrasion on her left hand. 她摔倒了，擦伤了左手。

abridge
abridge［ə'brɪʤ］
v. ① 删节 ② 缩短
解　① to reduce the length of (a written text); to condense ② to cut short; to curtail
例　Since the book was very long and detailed, he abridged it to make a new version. 由于这本书内容冗长、细节繁琐，他将其加以删减，形成了一个新的版本。
近　ridge n. 脊 （如屋脊、山脊等）；隆起物；bridge n. 桥；drawbridge n. 吊桥；badge n. 徽章；badger v. 不断纠缠，一再要求
构　a (=to) + bridg < brevi (=to shorten) + e

abroad
abroad　［əˈbrɔːd］
adv./adj. 在国外（的），海外（的）〈同 overseas〉
例 More people are going abroad for vacations. 越来越多的人去国外度假。

abrupt
abrupt［ə'brʌpt］
adj. ① 突然的，意外的〈同 sudden〉
例　There is a road with many abrupt turns. 那儿有一条路有很多急转弯。
例　Abrupt responses often cause hurt feelings. 无礼的回答通常会伤害别人的感情。

absenteeism
absenteeism［ˌæbsən'ti:ɪzm］
n. 旷课；旷工〈同　absence〉
例　The rate of absenteeism at this school is so high that punishments were introduced for nonattendance. 这所学校的缺勤率太高了，因此学校针对缺勤者采取了惩罚措施。

absolute
absolute［'æbsəlu:t］
adj. ①完全的〈同　total, complete〉
例　After he quit his old job a feeling of absolute freedom befell him. 辞去之前的工作之后，他有一种完全自由的感觉。
例　The captain of a ship has the absolute right to jettison cargo when necessary. 船长有绝对的权力在必要时抛弃货物。

absorb
absorb　［əbˈzɔːb］
vt. 吸收（液体、知识等）〈同 take in〉
例 Almost all living things absorb oxygen. 几乎一切有生命的东西都吸收氧气。
记 ab（离去）+sorb（吸吮）→吸收掉→吸收（液体、知识等）
联 absorption n. 吸收；absorbed adj. 全神贯注的，一心一意的；absorbent adj. 能吸收的 n. 吸收剂

abstract
abstract　［ˈæbstrækt］
vt. 摘要，提炼〈同 summarize〉
例 I abstracted the main idea of his science report. 我概括出了他的科学报告的主要观点。
n. 摘要〈同 summary〉
例 The abstract of the conference last week was distributed before the meeting to all the members. 上周会议的摘要已于开会之前分发给所有成员。
adj. 抽象的〈同 theoretical〉
例 His abstract ideas were not easily understood by many people. 许多人很难理解他抽象的想法。
联 abstraction n. 抽象概念

absurd
absurd［əb'zɜ:d］
adj. 荒谬的，可笑的〈同 foolish, ridiculous〉
例　It is absurd to wear a coat at the swimming pool. 在游泳池边穿着外套很可笑。

abundant
abundant　［əˈbʌndənt］
adj. 丰富的，充裕的；大量的〈同 plentiful〉
例 In recent years, an abundant number of complaints have disturbed the telephone company. 最近几年，大量的投诉让电话公司不堪其扰。
记 ab+und（波浪）+ant→像波浪一样起伏→丰富的；大量的
联 abundance n. 丰富，充裕；abound vi. 丰富；盛产

abuse
abuse　［əˈbjuːs］
n.（权力等的） 滥用；（物品的） 不精心使用；虐待（人）〈同 misuse〉
例 An abuse of authority by the manager led to disagreement among the members. 管理者滥用职权造成了成员之间的分歧。
记 ab（偏离）+use（使用）→偏离正常使用→滥用
联 abusive adj. 滥用的；谩骂的

abut
abut［ə'bʌt］
v. 邻接，毗邻〈同　be next to, border on〉
例　The library abuts the old museum. 图书馆毗邻老博物馆。

academic
academic　［ˌækəˈdemɪk］
adj. 学术的；学院的；理论的〈同 collegiate, scholastic〉
例 Like other academic disciplines, sociology has several major subdisciplines. 与其他学科一样，社会学有几个主要分支。
联 academician n. 学会会员；院士；学者；academy n.（高等） 专科院校；研究院；学院

accede
accede［æk'si:d］
v. 应允，同意
解　agree or express agreement
例　If I accede to his demand for blackmail, I am afraid that I will be the victim of future demands. 如果我同意了他的勒索要求，我恐怕以后会遭到更多的勒索。
构　ac (=to) + ced (=to go) + e

accelerate
accelerate　［əkˈseləreɪt］
v. 加快，加速〈同 speed up〉
例 The car accelerated as it went past me. 那辆车在经过我时加速了。
记 ac（表加强） +celer（速度） +ate（动词后缀）→加快，加速
联 acceleration n. 加速度

accent
accent［'æksənt］
n. ① 口音
例　My father was born in Germany and still speaks English with a German accent. 我的父亲出生在德国，他在说英语的时候仍带着德国口音。
例　In the word“wonderful”, the accent is on the first syllable. 单词wonderful的重音在第一个音节上。

access
access　［ˈækses］
n. ① 接触；接近（的机会）〈同 approach〉
例 Students must have access to a good teacher. 学生必须有个好老师。
例 The only access to this building is through those pipes. 进入这栋建筑的唯一通道是那些管道。
记 ac+cess（走）→走过去→通道
联 accessible adj. 可接近的，可接触的；可得到的；accessibility n. 易接近；可到达

accessible
accessible［ək'sesəbəl］
adj. ① 可接近的，易达到的 ② 可理解的
解　① capable of being reached or obtained ② capable of being read with comprehension
例　The professor was accessible for questions and discussions during his office hours. 在教授办公期间，可以向其提问或与其讨论问题。
构　ac (=to) + cess (=to go) + ible

accessory
accessory［ək'sesəri］
n. 附件，零件〈同 accompaniment〉
例　Her new car has many accessories, including air conditioning. 她的新车有许多配套设施，包括空调。

accessory
accessory［æk'sesəri］
adj. 附属的，次要的 n. 附件；附属
解　adj. relating to something that is added but is not essential n. a subordinate or supplementary item; an adjunct
例　The woman loved to go shopping for wardrobe accessories, like shoes, purses and belts. 这位女士喜欢购买服饰搭配品，比如鞋子、手提包和腰带。

accidental
accidental［ˌæksɪ'dentəl］
adj. 意外的，偶然的〈同　unexpected, unforeseen〉
例　The accidental encounter with an old friend, whom he hadn't seen for two years, made him very excited. 偶然遇到一位两年未见的老朋友，这让他非常兴奋。

acclaim
acclaim［ə'kleɪm］
n. 赞誉，赞许〈同　recognition, praise〉
例　The best-selling author's new book was greeted with great acclaim. 那位畅销书作家的新书受到了广泛称赞。
vt. 喝彩，欢呼；称赞〈同　hail; praise〉
例　Spectators acclaimed the winner of the competition. 观众们为比赛获胜者欢呼。

acclaim
acclaim［ə'kleɪm］
v. 称赞；欢呼
解　to praise vociferously; to clap one's hands or shout after performances to indicate approval
例　The mayor acclaimed the firefighters as the city's heroes for their bravery. 消防员们勇敢无畏，市长赞扬他们是这座城市的英雄。
近　acclimate v. 使适应
构　ac (=to) + claim (=to cry out)

accommodate
accommodate［ə'kɒmədeɪt］
vt. ① 容纳，为…提供空间；供应（膳宿）〈同 contain, supply〉
例　That hotel can accommodate up to one hundred guests. 那家旅馆总共可以容纳100个客人。
例　I will accommodate my scheme to yours. 我会调整我的计划以适应你的计划。

accommodation
accommodation　［əˌkɒməˈdeɪʃən］
n. 住处，膳宿〈同 lodging〉
例 I am searching for temporary accommodation in this new city. 我正在这座新城市里寻找临时住所。

accompany
accompany　［əˈkʌmpəni］
vt. 陪伴，陪同；伴奏〈同 be associated with〉
例 She was accompanied by her son. 她有自己的儿子陪着。
联 accompanying adj. 陪伴的，附随的；accompaniment n. 伴奏；伴随物

accomplish
accomplish　［əˈkʌmplɪʃ］
vt. 完成，达到，实现〈同 finish, achieve〉
例 To accomplish your plans to study abroad in England, you must first take the IELTS exam. 要实现去英国出国留学的计划，你首先必须参加雅思考试。
联 accomplished adj. 精通的，熟练的；accomplishment n. 成就

accord
accord　［əˈkɔːd］
n. 同意〈同 agreement〉
例 She was in complete accord with the verdict. 她完全服从判决。

according
according　［əˈkɔːdɪŋ］
adv. 依照（to）〈同 as stated by〉
例 She gets paid according to the number of hours she works. 她按工作的小时获得报酬。

account
account　［əˈkaʊnt］
n. ① 说明，解释〈同 description〉
例 She wrote an account of all her travels in Europe in her diary. 她在日记中记述了自己在欧洲旅行的所有见闻。
例 The new law requires a personal ID to open any accounts at a bank. 新法律要求在银行开立账户时必须出具个人身份证明。
v. 解释（for）〈同 explain〉
例 He accounted for the missing items as lost. 他解释称那些不见的物品丢失了。
联 accounting n. 会计学；记账；accountant n. 会计；会计师

accredit
accredit［ə'kredɪt］
vt. 授权〈同　authorize, commission〉
例　Diplomatic negotiations generally take place in embassies where ambassadors are accredited. 外交谈判通常在其大使被授权的大使馆进行。

accrete
accrete［æ'kri:t］
v. 自然增加（因不停地生长而增大）
解　to make larger or greater, as by increased growth
例　Over time the trees' roots accreted into one. 随着时间流逝，这些树的根长到了一起。
同　accretion n. 自然的增加；增加物
构　ac (=to) + cre (=to grow) + te

accumulate
accumulate　［əˈkjuːmjʊleɪt］
vi. 堆积，积聚；积累〈同 pile up; collect〉
例 Dust and dirt soon accumulate if a library is not cleaned daily. 如果不天天打扫图书馆，灰尘很快就会越积越多。
记 ac（一再）+cumul（堆积） +ate→一再堆积→积累
联 accumulative adj. 积聚的，累积的；accumulation n. 积聚

accuse
accuse　［əˈkjuːz］
v. 指责，归咎〈同 blame〉
例 Janet's boyfriend accused her of lying. 珍妮特的男朋友指责她撒谎。
联 accusation n. 谴责；控告

accustomed
accustomed　［əˈkʌstəmd］
adj. 习惯了的（to）
例 It took a long time for me to get accustomed to the fast food in America, but now I can't live without it！我花了很长时间才习惯了美国的快餐，可现在如果没有快餐，我都活不下去了！

acerbic
acerbic［ə'sɜ:bɪk］
adj. ① 酸的 ② 尖刻的
解　① sour or bitter in taste ② harsh or corrosive in tone
例　You should not eat the fruit if it is not ripe, since it will probably taste acerbic. 你应该等水果熟了再吃，不然可能会很酸。

achieve
achieve　［əˈtʃiːv］
vt. 完成，实现 vi. 如愿以偿〈同 win, accomplish〉
例 Kermit achieved his dream of marrying Miss Piggy. 克米特终于实现了娶佩姬小姐为妻的梦想。
联 achievement n. 成就，功绩

acid
acid［'æsɪd］
adj. ① 酸的 ② 尖刻的
解　① sharp or biting to the taste; sour ② sharp in manner or temper
例　Lemons are an acid fruit. 柠檬是一种酸味水果。

acknowledge
acknowledge　［əkˈnɒlɪʤ］
vt. 承认〈同 admit〉
例 The experts reluctantly acknowledged that their estimate of food costs was not accurate. 专家们不情愿地承认，他们对食品成本的估算并不准确。
联 acknowledgement n. 承认；确认；acknowledged adj. 公认的

acquaintance
acquaintance　［əˈkweɪntəns］
n. 熟人
例 We are acquaintances and talk frequently. 我们是熟人，经常在一起聊天。
记 ac（表强调） +quaint（知道） +ance（名词后缀）→熟人知道彼此的事情→熟人
联 acquaint vt. 使熟知；了解；（be) acquainted with 熟悉

acquiesce
acquiesce［ˌækwɪ'es］
v. 勉强同意，默许
解　to give consent silently
例　The bank manager acquiesced to the robbers so that no one would get hurt. 银行经理答应了抢劫者的要求，这样其他人就不会受到伤害。
同　acquiescence n. 默许
构　ac (=to) + quie (=to be quiet) + sce

acquire
acquire［ə'kwaɪə(r)］
v. 获得，得到
解　to come into the possession of something concrete or abstract
例　The tycoon acquired valuable assets from his many takeovers. 这个企业巨头从他的多项收购中获得了有价值的资产。

acquired
acquired［ə'kwaɪəd］
adj. 后天习得的
解　gotten through environmental forces
例　After studying for his Ph.D degree, he returned to his country to apply his newly- acquired skills to his profession. 取得博士学位后，他回到自己的祖国，把新掌握的技术应用到了自己的专业领域里。

acquisition
acquisition　［ˌækwɪˈzɪʃən］
n. 得到，获得〈同 acquirement〉
例 The stockbroker made an acquisition of the future price of the stock based on its historical growth patterns. 股票经纪人根据股票的历史增长趋势，获得股票的未来价格。
记 ac+qusit（得到）+ion→得到，获得
联 acquire vt. 获得；学到

acquisition
acquisition［ˌækwɪ'zɪʃən］
n. 获得；获得物
解　the act of acquiring; anything gained or acquired
例　The company's many acquisitions practically gave it a monopoly in the market. 这家公司收购了许多公司之后，几乎可以垄断市场。

acquisitiveness
acquisitiveness［ə'kwɪzɪtɪvnəs］
n. 贪得无厌
解　strong desire to acquire and possess
例　The money-hungry businesswoman has always had a sense of acquisitiveness ever since she was a young girl. 当她还是个年轻的女孩的时候，这个视钱如命的女商人就有了一种获取利润的意识。
构　ac (=to) + quis (=to seek) + itive + ness

acrid
acrid［'ækrɪd］
adj. ① （气味等）刺激的，辛辣的 ② 刻薄的
解　① strong and sharp ② harsh or corrosive in tone
例　Acrid coal smoke made my eyes water. 刺鼻的煤烟把我的眼睛熏得流泪。
同　acridity n. （气味等）辛辣，刺激

acrimonious
acrimonious［ˌækrɪ'məʊnjəs］
adj. 言词或语调等刻薄的，激烈的
解　bitter and caustic in temper, manner, or speech
例　An acrimonious dispute broke out between the drivers who had the accident. 一场激烈的冲突在发生事故的司机之间爆发了。
同　acrimony n. 尖刻，刻薄
近　parsimonious adj. 太节省的，小气的

acronym
acronym［'ækrənɪm］
n. 用大写字母表示的缩写词〈同　abbreviation〉
例　AIDS is an acronym for Acquired Immune Deficiency Syndrome. AIDS是“获得性免疫缺陷综合征”的缩写。

action
action［'ækʃən］
n. 行为，行动
解　the state or process of acting or doing; a deed
例　The judge told her she had to be responsible for her actions. 法官告诉她要为自己的行为负责。

activate
activate［'æktɪveɪt］
vt. 刺激，使活动〈同 mobilize〉
例　The hungry and tired child was activated when he saw the bread. 这个又饿又累的孩子一看见面包马上变得精神起来。

activate
activate［'æktɪveɪt］
vt. 刺激，激发，使活动
解　to set in motion; to make active or more active
例　The driving instructor taught her to put the key into the ignition to activate the car. 驾驶教练教她把钥匙插入点火装置来启动车辆。

active
active［'æktɪv］
adj. ① 积极的，活跃的 ② 活性的
解　① working hard or with energy; busy and energetic; lively ② working
例　The professor was very active in his lectures, throwing his hands in the air and jumping up and down. 教授在讲课过程中很活跃，挥舞双手，跳上跳下。
同　activity n. 活动；活跃，活力

actual
actual［'æktʃʊəl］
adj. 实际的，现行的〈同　real, true〉
例　Our actual expenses for food and clothes last year were much lower than we thought. 去年，我们在吃穿上的实际开支远远低于预期。
例　Realizing that she was addicted to cigarettes, Janet decided to quit. 珍妮特意识到自己吸烟上瘾了，因此决定戒烟。
例　The drug addict was required to get medical help. 那个瘾君子被要求接受药物治疗。

acumen
acumen［ə'kjʊ:mən］
n. 精明，敏锐，明智
解　shrewdness shown by keen insight
例　Sherlock Holmes' acumen helped him solve hundreds of mysteries. 夏洛克·福尔摩斯的聪明帮助他破解了数百个谜案。

acute
acute［ə'kju:t］
adj. ① 灵敏的，敏锐的〈同 keen〉
例　Acute hearing helps most animals sense the approach of thunderstorms long before people do. 大多数动物都有着灵敏的听觉，它们比人类感知雷雨到来的时间要早很多。
例　With the acceleration of industrial growth came acute urban crowding and accompanying social stress. 随着工业化的加速发展，城市里出现了严重拥挤和随之而来的社会压力。

acute
acute［ə'kjʊ:t］
adj. ① 灵敏的，敏锐的 ② （病）急性的，剧烈的
解　① quick in perceiving and responding to impressions; keen ② afflicted by a disease exhibiting a rapid onset followed by a short, severe course
例　Dogs have an acute sense of smell. 狗有着敏锐的嗅觉。
同　acuity n. 敏锐，灵敏

adapt
adapt　［əˈdæpt］
v.（使）适应，调整；改编〈同 adjust; modify〉
例 After moving to Harbin, Janet adapted to the cold weather. 珍妮特在搬到哈尔滨之后，适应了寒冷的天气。
记 ad（去） +apt（适合）→（使）适应，调整
联 adaptable adj. 能适应的，适应性强的；adaptation n. 改编，改写；适应环境；adaptive adj. 适合的；适应的

addition
addition［ə'dɪʃən］
n. 增加；加法
解　the act of adding one thing to another
例　The addition of new factories around the community would hinder the local air quality. 在社区周围建造新的工厂会影响当地的空气质量。

additional
additional［ə'dɪʃənəl］
adj. 附加的
解　added; extra; more
例　The teacher realized the test was too long and gave the students an additional ten minutes to finish it. 老师意识到测试内容太多，给了学生额外10分钟来完成。

additive
additive［'ædətɪv］
n. 添加剂〈同　addition, supplement〉
例　The scientists had to use certain additives to make the drug more powerful. 为了增强药物的药效，科学家们不得不使用特定的添加剂。

additive
additive［'ædɪtɪv］
n. 添加剂，添加物
解　something added to enhance food or gasoline or paint or medicine
例　The food from fast food restaurants has a lot of chemical additives, such as preservatives. 快餐店的食物有很多化学添加剂，比如防腐剂。
近　

adept
adept［ə'dept］
adj. 熟练的，擅长的〈同　competent, skilled〉
例　Mr. Bao is known to be an adept writer. 鲍先生是一位出色的作家。

adequate
adequate　［ˈædɪkwət］
adj. 足够的，充足的〈同 sufficient〉
例 I bought four bottles of water for our camping trip and I hope it is adequate. 我为露营买了四瓶水，希望这些已经足够了。
联 inadequate adj. 不充分的；不适当的

adequate
adequate［'ædɪkwɪt］
adj. 适当的，足够的
解　enough to meet a purpose
例　The student's work was not outstanding, but it was adequate for a passing grade. 这名学生的成绩不算优秀，但是足以及格。
同　adequacy n. 足够；inadequacy n. 不充分
构　ad (=to) + equ (=equal) + ate

adhere
adhere［əd'hɪə(r)］
vi. ① 黏附，粘牢〈同 stick〉
例　Mud adheres to your shoes. 你的鞋粘上泥了。
例　In China, many people adhere to Confucius' teaching. 在中国，有很多人遵循孔子的教育理念。

adjacent
adjacent［ə'ʤeɪsənt］
adj. 毗连的，邻近的〈同 neighboring〉
例　The house adjacent to ours has been sold, so we have a new neighbor. 我们隔壁的房子已经卖出去了，于是我们有了新的邻居。

adjudicate
adjudicate［əˌʤu:dɪ'keɪt］
v. 判决，宣判，裁定
解　to hear and settle (a case) by judicial procedure; to study and settle (a dispute or controversy)
例　The claims of the surviving victims of the crash will be adjudicated by an international commission. 坠机幸存者的索赔要求将由国际委员会裁决。
同　adjudicator n. 裁决者
构　ad (=to) + judic (=to judge) + ate

adjunct

例　I hoped that I would find the computer course a useful adjunct to my other studies. 我希望计算机课对我学习其他课程有辅助作用。

adjust
adjust［ə'ʤʌst］
vt. 调整；使适应〈同 regulate, adapt〉
例　It took Janet more than half a year to adjust to the new business after she changed her job. 珍妮特跳槽以后，花了多半年的时间来适应这份新工作。

administer

vt. 管理〈同 govern〉
例　The British administered Hong Kong until 1997. 英国对香港的管辖持续到1997年。

administration
administration　［ədˌmɪnɪˈstreɪʃən］
n. ① 管理，经营〈同 supervision〉
例 Headmasters are more involved in administration than in actual teaching. 校长大部分的工作是行政管理，而不是实际教学。
例 The school administration met to decide on a new school policy. 学校管理委员会召开会议，来确定学校的一项新政策。
联 administrative adj. 管理的；行政的；administrator n. 管理者；行政官；administer v. 管理；执行

例　Adobe is a type of brick made of clay baked in the sun. 泥砖是一种用黏土制成的、在太阳下烤晒而成形的砖。

advent

n.（尤指不寻常的人或事的）出现，到来〈同 coming into being〉
例　The advent of e-mail changed communication. 电子邮件的出现改变了通信方式。

adverse
adverse［æd'vɜ:s］
adj. 负面的，不利的；相反的〈同 unfavorable, opposite〉
例　The adverse effects from most of the medication were minimal. 大多数药物的副作用很小。
例　The International Fund for Animal Welfare was a strong advocate of the campaign to save dolphins from death. 国际爱护动物基金会是拯救海豚运动的坚决拥护者。
例　Some people advocated limiting the number of cars on the main road. 有些人倡议限制主路上的汽车数量。

例　It is not advisable for you to go to school while you are still sick. 你还在生病，不应该去学校。

例　Soda water is water that has been aerated with carbon dioxide. 苏打水是压入二氧化碳的水溶液。

affinity

例　She felt an affinity with all who suffered; their pains were her pains. 她能与所有遭受痛苦的人产生情感共鸣；他们的痛苦就是她的痛苦。
例　Many girls have a strong affinity for chocolate candy. 许多女孩特别喜欢巧克力糖。

affinity
affinity［ə'fɪnəti］
n. 亲密关系；吸引力
解　a natural attraction or feeling of kinship
例　She had a strong affinity for chocolate when she was depressed and she could not resist eating it. 当她情绪低落时，巧克力对她来说有一种强烈的吸引力，她忍不住要去吃。

例　Private cars are banned from the city on alternate days. 私家车每隔一天就被禁止入城。
例　If that business does not make what we want, we can always find an alternate one that does. 如果那项业务达不到我们想要的水平，我们随时都可以选择其他的业务来替代。
例　Her cheerfulness alternated with despair. 她的欢乐和绝望交替而来。

例 Most plants depend upon their roots to anchor themselves in the soil and to absorb water and inorganic chemicals. 大多数植物都是靠根部将自己固定在土壤中，吸收水分和无机化学物。

anesthesia

例　The anesthesia around his mouth allowed him to be unconscious when the dentist extracted his teeth. 他的嘴巴周围被麻醉，这样在医生给他拔牙时他就不会感觉疼痛。

anesthetic

animated
animated［'ænɪmeɪtɪd］
adj. 活生生的；活泼的，生动的〈同　lively〉
例　Cartoons are animated short films. 卡通是动画短片。

animated
animated［'ænɪmeɪtɪd］
adj. ① 栩栩如生的 ② 活泼的，生机勃勃的
解　① seeming to be alive ② lively; vigorous
例　The clown's animated performance made both the children and the adults laugh. 小丑栩栩如生的表演逗得孩子和大人都哈哈大笑。
同　animate v. 使有生命；animation n. 兴奋，活跃；inanimate adj. 死气沉沉的，无生命的

animosity
animosity［ˌænɪ'mɒsɪti］
n. 憎恶，仇恨
解　violent hatred; active dislike; ill will
例　The wife held a great deal of animosity towards her ex-husband for the way he had treated her. 妻子因其前夫对待她的方式很恶劣而十分憎恨他。

annex
annex［æ'neks］
vt. 兼并，附加〈同　add, attach〉
例　In 1939, Hitler succeeded in annexing various parts of Europe to Germany without firing the shot. 1939年，希特勒没有动用一枪一炮，便将欧洲许多地区并入德国领土。

annihilate
annihilate［ə'naɪəleɪt］
vt. 消灭；削减〈同　conquer, destroy〉
例　They were sent on a mission to annihilate the rebel forces. 他们被派去消灭叛军。

anniversary
anniversary［ˌænɪ'vɜ:səri］
n. 周年纪念〈同　commemoration〉
例　Our wedding anniversary is January 12th. 我们的结婚纪念日是1月12日。

announce
announce［ə'naʊns］
v. 宣告，宣布
解　to make known publicly
例　The teacher announced to the class the sad news of the national disaster. 老师在班上通报了国家遭受灾难的沉痛消息。
同　announcement n. 声明

annoy
annoy　［əˈnɔɪ］
vt. 使恼怒；打扰 vi. 令人讨厌〈同 irritate〉
例 What annoys me is the fact that he won't listen to other people's suggestions. 令我烦恼的是，他竟然不听其他人的建议。
联 annoyance n. 烦恼；annoying adj. 恼人的

annual
annual　［ˈænjʊəl］
adj. 每年的〈同 yearly〉
例 Companies publish annual reports to inform the public about the previous year's activities. 公司通过公布年报，将之前一年的经营活动告知公众。
联 annually adv. 一年一次地

anomalous
anomalous［ə'nɒmələs］
adj. 反常的，不规则的
解　deviating from the general or common order or type
例　Both geniuses and mad men usually follow anomalous patterns of behavior. 天才和疯子通常都行为异常。
同　anomaly n. 异常，反常；反常的事件

anomalous
anomalous［ə'nɒmələs］
adj. 反常的，不规则的
解　deviating from the general or common order or type
例　It would be anomalous for a principal to have no authority. 一个校长没有任何权威，这是很不正常的。
同　anomaly n. 异常，反常；反常的事件

anomaly
anomaly［ə'nɒməli］
n. 异常，不规则；异常的人或物〈同　abnormality, deviation〉
例　A dog with six legs would be an anomaly. 一条狗长有六条腿，这属于异常现象。

anonymity
anonymity［ˌænə'nɪmɪti］
n. 无名，匿名
解　state of being nameless
例　The donor of the gift asked the college not to mention him by name; and the dean readily agreed to respect his anonymity. 礼物捐赠人要求学院不要提起他的姓名，院长欣然同意尊重他的匿名请求。
构　an (=not, without) + onym (=name) + ity

anonymity
anonymity［ˌænə'nɪmɪti］
n. 无名，匿名
解　state of being nameless
例　The donor of the gift asked the college not to mention him by name, and the dean readily agreed to respect his anonymity. 礼物捐赠人要求学校不要提到他的名字，校长也毫不勉强，同意尊重他匿名的要求。

anonymous
anonymous［ə'nɒnɪməs］
adj. 匿名的〈同 unknown〉
例　Sometimes, the newspaper publishes anonymous articles in the political opinion section. 有时候，报纸在政治观点版刊登匿名文章。

antagonistic
antagonistic［ænˌtæɡə'nɪstɪk］
adj. 对立的，敌对的
解　acting against each other; opposing; hostile
例　Cats and dogs are antagonistic towards each other. 猫类和狗类互相敌视。
同　antagonism n. 对抗，敌对

antagonize
antagonize［æn'tæɡənaɪz］
v. ① 与…对抗 ② 激怒
解　① to act in opposition to ② to provoke the hostility of
例　The fly antagonized him as he sat peacefully reading a book. 在他平静地坐着看书时，一只苍蝇惹恼了他。

antarctic
antarctic［æn'tɑ:ktɪk］
adj.［常作A-］南极的，南极地带的
例　Scientists are keen to track the fortunes of Antarctic plant life over 30 million years. 科学家热衷于追踪3000万年以来南极地区植物的生长情况的宝贵信息。
n.［常作the A-］南极地区
例　The protection of the Antarctic from commercial exploitation is an important goal of environmentalists. 保护南极地区不被商业开发是环保人士重要的工作目标。

antecedent
antecedent［ˌæntɪ'si:dənt］
n. 先辈；前事 adj. 先行的
解　n. a preceding occurrence or cause or event adj. preceding in time or order
例　Scientists cannot agree on whether the egg or the chicken was the antecedent. 科学家们在“先有鸡还是先有蛋”这个问题上无法达成一致。
近　anterior adj. 较早的，以前的
构　ante (=before) + ced (=to go) + ent

anthem
anthem［'ænθəm］
n. 圣歌，赞美歌〈同　hymn〉
例　The band played the national anthem. 乐队演奏了国歌。

anthology
anthology［æn'θɒləʤi］
n. 诗集；文选〈同　collection〉
例　I love to read anthologies of science fiction stories. 我喜欢读科幻小说选集。

anthology
anthology［æn'θɒləʤi］
n. 诗集，文选；选集
解　a collection of selected literary passages
例　She used an anthology of bedtime short stories to read her children to sleep. 她通过读一本睡前短篇故事集来哄孩子们睡觉。
同　antho (=flower; collection) + logy

antibiotic
antibiotic［ˌæntibaɪ'ɒtɪk］
adj. 抗菌的，抗生的
例　Antibiotic drugs such as penicillin have saved many lives. 青霉素等抗菌药物挽救了许多人的生命。

antibiotic
antibiotic［ˌæntɪbaɪ'ɒtɪk］
n. 抗生素
解　a substance produced by a living organism, especially a bacterium or fungus, that destroys or weakens germs
例　Penicillin is an antibiotic. 青霉素是一种抗生素。
构　anti (=against) + bio (=life) + tic

antibody
antibody［'æntɪbɒdi］
n. 抗体
解　a protein substance produced in the blood or tissues in response to a specific antigen, such as a bacterium or a toxin
例　The professor explained to the biology students how our bodies create antibodies in response to foreign substances in our blood. 教授向生物系学生讲解当外来物质进入我们的血液中时，我们的身体是如何产生抗体的。
构　anti (=against) + body (=body)

antibody
antibody［'æntɪbɒdi］
n. 抗体
解　substance formed in the blood tending to inhibit or destroy harmful bacteria, etc.
例　The antibodies surrounded and killed the bacteria in his liver. 抗体包围并消灭了他肝脏里的细菌。

anticipate
anticipate　［ænˈtɪsɪpeɪt］
vt. 预料，预期〈同 expect〉
例 Columbus' discovery of America was probably anticipated by earlier explorers. 哥伦布发现美洲大陆，可能已经被之前的探险家们预见到了。
记 anti（前）+cip（落下）+ate→提前落下→预期
联 anticipation n. 期望，预料

anticlimax
anticlimax［æntɪ'klaɪmæks］
n. 高潮突降（从上升趋势突然转为令人失望的下降趋势）；虎头蛇尾
解　a disappointing decline after a previous rise
例　After all the suspense for the new movie, the actor's poor performance made the last scene an anticlimax. 这部新电影在前面设置了许多悬念，但这个男演员拙劣的表演使最后一场戏变得虎头蛇尾。

anticlimax
anticlimax［ˌæntɪ'klaɪmæks］
n. 高潮突降
解　a sudden change from an important state to a trivial state
例　The athlete's paralysis was an anticlimax to his promising career. 这位运动员的瘫痪使他正辉煌的事业突然走向了低谷。

antidote
antidote［'æntɪdəʊt］
n. 解毒剂
解　a remedy or other agent used to neutralize or counteract the effects of a poison
例　They gave the patient an antidote to reverse the course the poison had taken. 他们给病人服用解毒剂来中和毒药的毒性。
构　anti (=against) + dote (=to give)

antipathy
antipathy［æn'tɪpəθi］
n. 憎恶，反感，不相容
解　a feeling of intense dislike
例　Cats naturally have a strong antipathy towards dogs. 猫和狗天生不相容。
构　anti (=against, opposite) + path (=to feel) + y

例　The crank telephone is now thoroughly antiquated. 如今，摇柄电话已经完全过时了。

antiquated

adj. ① 陈旧的 ② 过时的
解　① extremely old as seeming to belong to an earlier period ② being out of style or fashion
例　Marine explorers discovered the remains of an antiquated city at the bottom of the ocean. 海洋探险家在海底发现了一座废弃城市的残骸。

antique
antique　［ænˈtiːk］
n. 古董〈同 relic〉
例 The clock in the room is an antique. 那个房间里的钟表是一件古董。
adj. 古时的，陈旧的〈同 old, archaic〉
例 Richard likes antique cars and always goes to auto shows on weekends. 理查德喜欢古董车，经常在周末去参加车展。
记 anti（前）+que→以前就有的→古时的

antique

解　n. something made long ago adj. of times long ago; from times long ago
例　This carved chest is a genuine antique. 这个雕花的箱子是一件真正的古董。

例　He bathed the wound with antiseptic. 他用抗菌剂冲洗伤口。

anxious
anxious　［ˈænkʃəs］
adj. ① 渴望的〈同 keen〉
例 Since it was Rob's first date, he was more nervous than he was anxious. 这是罗布的第一次约会，因此他更多感到的是紧张而不是渴望。
例 The drought has made farmers anxious about the harvest. 干旱让农民们担心起庄稼的收成。

例　The apartment in the inland city was very expensive because of its view of the lake. 由于市内有个湖，所以这个内陆城市的房价很高。

apathetic

adj. 冷漠的，无动于衷的
解　showing little or no emotion or animation
例　Many people are apathetic about social issues and are only concerned about their own self-interest. 许多人对社会事件漠不关心，而只在乎自身的利益。
构　a (=not) + path (=to feel, to suffer) + etic

apathy
apathy［'æpəθi］
n. 漠然，冷淡
解　the trait of lacking enthusiasm for or interest in things generally
例　The people's apathy towards pollution contributed to the destruction of the environment. 人们对污染的冷漠导致了对环境的破坏。
近　pithy adj. （讲话或文章）简练的
同　apathetic adj. 冷漠的，无动于衷的
构　a (=not, without) + path (=to feel) + y

例　The waitress apologized for spilling coffee on the man's lap. 女服务员因把咖啡洒到了一位男士的腿上而向他道了歉。

apology
apology［ə'pɒləʤi］
n. ① 为信仰等辩护 ② 道歉

例　He expressed his apology to his girlfriend in a love letter. 他在情书里向女朋友表达了歉意。

apophasis
apophasis［ə'pɒfəsɪs］
n. 【修辞】婉转表达法，表面否认要说或正说的话来加以暗示
解　allusion to something by denying that it will be mentioned
例　The attorney's use of apophasis aimed to discredit his rival without accusing him of anything outright. 这位律师没有直接指控对手的罪行，而是通过婉转表述来达到使其名誉扫地的目的。

apoplectic
apoplectic［ˌæpəʊ'plektɪk］
adj. ① 狂怒的；大怒的 ② 中风的，濒于中风的
解　① extremely angry; furious ② having or inclined to have apoplexy
例　Members of Congress became apoplectic about wasteful government spending. 国会成员对于政府开支的浪费感到非常愤怒。

apostasy
apostasy［ə'pɒstəsi］
n. 背教；脱党
解　a total departure from one's faith or religion
例　His statements revealed his apostasy and he was excommunicated from the church. 他的陈述透露了他的叛教，因此被逐出教会。
同　apostate n. 背教者，变节者

apostrophe
apostrophe［ə'pɒstrəfi］
n. 撇号 (')
解　the mark (') used to indicate possession as well as the omission of one or more letters from a printed word
例　The apostrophe is used to express possession. 撇号用来表达所有格。

apparatus
apparatus［ˌæpə'reɪtəs］
n. 器械，设备，仪器〈同　machinery, equipment〉
例　The doctor uses many different apparatus including X-ray machines and stethoscopes. 医生使用许多种不同的仪器，包括X光机和听诊器。

appeal
appeal　［əˈpiːl］
n. 吸引力〈同 attraction〉
例 The appeal of traveling to a sunny beach during the cold winter is very strong. 在寒冷的冬季，去阳光明媚的海滩度假非常具有吸引力。
例 The thought of going for a walk after dinner tonight appeals to me. 今天晚上饭后散步的想法引起了我的兴趣。
例 Judgments made in a criminal case can usually be appealed to a higher court, which can either overturn or uphold a lower court ruling. 刑事案件的判决通常会被上诉至上级法院，上级法院可驳回或支持下级法院的判决。
记 ap+peal（拉）→拉过去→吸引
联 appealing adj. 动人的，吸引人的

appendix
appendix［ə'pendɪks］
n. ① 附录；附属品
例　This dictionary has an appendix which lists computer terms. 这本字典有一个列举计算机术语的附录。
例　She had her appendix out last summer. 去年夏天，她做了阑尾切除手术。

appetite
appetite　［ˈæpɪtaɪt］
n. 胃口，食欲〈同 desire〉
例 Michael had no appetite, so they had to coax him to eat. 迈克尔没有食欲，所以他们不得不哄他吃饭。

applaud
applaud［ə'plɔ:d］
v.（向…）鼓掌喝彩，欢呼〈同 clap〉
例　The audience stood up and applauded at the end of the concert. 音乐会结束时，观众们起立鼓掌。

applicant
applicant　［ˈæplɪkənt］
n. 申请人〈同 candidate〉
例 The company was so popular that there were only two vacancies for one hundred applicants. 这家公司太受欢迎，只有两个职位空缺，却有一百多名应征者。
联 application n. 申请；施用，运用；appliance n. 用具，器具；apply vt. 应用，适用；vi. 申请

application

例　Mathematics has applications in science. 数学在科学领域有所应用。

appointment
appointment　［əˈpɔɪntmənt］
n. ① 约会，约定
例 Dr. Smith will not be available for any of his appointments today since he is still out of town. 史密斯医生今天无法赴约，因为他现在还没回到城里。

apportion
apportion［ə'pɔ:∫ən］
vt.（按比例或计划）分配〈同　distribute, allot〉
例　Our problem now is not to apportion blame for our failures but to find a way to achieve successes. 我们目前的问题并非追究失败的责任，而是找出获得成功的方法。

appraisal
appraisal［ə'preɪzəl］
n. 评价；估价〈同 assessment〉
例　Fifty thousand dollars would be a fair appraisal of their new house. 给他们的新房估价5万美元是客观公正的。

appreciable
appreciable［ə'pri:ʃɪəbəl］
adj.（数量或变化等）很大的；值得重视的〈同 considerable〉
例　There has been an appreciable drop in the number of the unemployed since the new government came to power. 新政府执政以后，失业人员的数量有了明显下降。

appreciate
appreciate　［əˈpriːʃɪeɪt］
vt. ① 赏识；鉴赏〈同 admire〉
例 The teacher works very hard but he can still find time to appreciate traditional Chinese painting. 那位老师工作非常努力，但仍能抽出时间欣赏中国传统国画。
例 I appreciate your advice on this important matter. 我非常感谢您为这件重要的事情所提出的建议。
联 appreciation n. 欣赏；口味，兴趣；appreciable adj. 明显的；可估计的；appreciative adj. 感谢的；赞赏的

apprehension
apprehension［ˌæprɪ'henʃən］
n. 担心，害怕；理解〈同 worry, understand〉
例　The English test caused me a lot of apprehension because I did not study hard for it. 因为我没有努力学习，英语测试让我感到很恐惧。

approach
approach　［əˈprəʊtʃ］
n. 方法〈同 method〉
例 I've just read an interesting book which has a new approach to studying Cao Xueqin. 我最近读了一本有趣的书，书中提出了一种研究曹雪芹的新方法。
v. 接近，靠近〈同 be close to, near〉
例 The time is approaching when Sharon will leave to study English in the United States. 莎伦去美国学英语的日子越来越近了。
联 approaching adj. 接近的，逼近的

approbation
approbation［ˌæprə'beɪʃən］
n. ① 称赞 ② 批准，认可
解　① approval; praise ② official recognition or approval sanction
例　Popularity polls seem to be based on the mistaken idea that the basic task of a political leader is to win immediate approbation from the people. 民意测验似乎建立在这样一种错误的观念上，即认为一个政治领袖的基本任务就是从人民那里得到直接的认可。
构　ap < ad (=to) + prob (=to try, to test) + ation

appropriate
appropriate　［əˈprəʊprɪət］
adj. 适当的，恰当的〈同 proper〉
例 I've been invited to her wedding but I haven't got anything appropriate to wear. 我受邀参加她的婚礼，但我还没有合适的衣服穿。
例 The city government appropriated a large budget for the construction of a new science museum. 市政府拨出很大一部分预算，用于建设新科技博物馆。
记 ap+propr（=proper 正确）+iate→正确的，恰当的
联 appropriation n. 拨款；inappropriate adj. 不适当的，不相称的

appropriate
appropriate［ə'prəʊprieɪt］v. ① 拨款 ② 挪用，盗用［ə'prəʊpriət］adj. 合适的
解　v. ① to set apart for a specific use ② to take for oneself or for one's own use, esp. without permission adj. suitable for a particular person or place or condition, etc.
例　The judge decided on an appropriate sentence for the crime. 法官对这一罪行作出了适当的判决。
同　appropriately adv. 得体地；appropriateness n. 适当；appropriation n. 恰当；拨款，挪用公款

approval
approval　［əˈpruːvəl］
n. 赞成，正式批准〈同 sanction〉
例 We'll buy the new computer system as soon as we have the approval of the directors. 只要获得董事们的批准，我们马上就购买新电脑系统。
联 disapproval n. 不赞成；approve v. 赞许，欣赏；批准，赞成

approval
approval［ə'pru:vəl］
n. ① 批准 ② 赞同
解　① a message expressing a favorable opinion ② acceptance as satisfactory
例　Elected officials normally check ratings of their pubic approval in order to calculate their chances for reelection. 当选官员通常都会确认他们的公共支持率，从而计算出下次当选的几率。

approximate
approximate
例 Your latest design approximates much more closely what I understood the building would be like. 你最新的设计与我想象中这栋建筑的样子非常接近。
例 The approximate time that the train will arrive at its destination is 8:00 a.m. tomorrow. 火车抵达目的地的大体时间是明天上午八点。
记 ap+proxim（接近）+ate→接近，近似
联 approximately adv. 近似地，大约；approximation n. 近似值

apt
apt［æpt］
adj. ① 恰当的，贴切的〈同 appropriate〉
例　His apt reply to the question showed that he had understood it very well. 他对这个问题做出的恰当的回答表明他已经理解得很好了。
例　A careless person is apt to make mistakes. 粗心的人容易犯错误。

aquatic
aquatic［ə'kwætɪk］
adj. 水生的，水栖的
例　Dolphins are good examples of mammals that are aquatic life forms. 海豚是水生生物中哺乳动物的很好的例子。

aqueduct
aqueduct［'ækwɪˌdʌkt］
n. 引水渠，渡槽
解　an artificial channel or large pipe for bringing water from a distance; a structure that supports such a channel or pipe
例　The inland town built an aqueduct to transport water from the river to houses. 这个内陆城镇建造了一个引水渠，用来把水从河里输送到各家各户。
近　aquatic adj. 水生的，水中的

arbitrary
arbitrary　［ˈɑːbɪtrəri］
adj. 专横的，专制的；武断的〈同 dictatorial〉
例 The manager consistently rewarded his sales team in an arbitrary manner, causing offense to the top performers of other departments, who received no pay for extra work. 那位经理总是以随意的方式奖励销售团队，这引起了其他部门优秀员工的不满，因为他们的额外工作并没有得到回报。
记 来自arbit（判断，裁决）+rary→武断的
联 arbitrarily adv. 任意地；专横地；arbitrator n. 仲裁人；arbiter n. 权威人物；仲裁人；arbitrate v. 仲裁，公断

atrophy
atrophy［'ætrəfi］
n. ① 【医】萎缩，萎缩症 ② 衰退
解　① a decrease in size of an organ caused by disease or disuse ② any weakening or degeneration (especially through lack of use)
例　Medical experts state that almost every case of muscle and tissue atrophy is the result of changes in cell nutrition, disease, or prolonged disuse. 医学专家称，几乎所有肌肉和组织萎缩都是由细胞营养的变化、疾病或长期不运动所引起的。
近　trophy n. 奖品，战利品；troupe n. 剧团；歌唱团
构　a (=not, without) + troph (=nourishment) + y

例　The members of the wedding party all wore formal attire. 参加婚宴的宾客都盛装出席。

attorney
attorney　［əˈtɜːni］
n. 代理人；辩护律师〈同 lawyer〉
例 The attorney turned down the law firm's offer of a position. 那名律师拒绝了那家律师事务所提供的职位。
记 at+torn（转）+ey→脑子转得快的人→律师

attractive　［əˈtræktɪv］

例 The Hudson River has a couple of interesting physical features that made it very attractive for settlement by the Europeans. 哈德逊河有几个非常有趣的特点，使其吸引了欧洲人来此定居。
记 at+tract（拉）+ive→把注意力拉过来的→吸引人的

attribute
attribute
例 His outstanding attribute was his kindness. 他最突出的品质是善良。
例 Her success is attributed to her hard work and a bit of luck. 她的成功归因于她的努力工作和一点点好运气。
联 attribution n. 归属，归因

audible［'ɔ:dəbəl］

例　Some insects have such a keen sense of hearing that they can hear sounds not audible to the human ear. 有些昆虫有非常敏锐的听觉，它们可以听到人耳听不到的声音。

automatic
automatic　［ˌɔːtəˈmætɪk］

baton［'bætən; (US)bə'tɒn］
n. 接力棒；指挥棒
解　a slender wooden stick or rod passed from runner to runner in a relay race or used by a conductor to direct an orchestra
例　If one of the runners in the relay race dropped the baton, the whole relay team would be disqualified. 在接力赛中，如果其中一名队员掉了接力棒，那么整个接力队将失去比赛资格。

battle
battle［'bætəl］
n. 战斗
解　a hostile meeting of opposing military forces in the course of a war
例　The general told his adversary that he may have won the battle, but not the war. 将军告诉他的敌人，他可能赢了这场战役，但赢不了整个战争。
近　belittle v. 轻视；贬低；brittle adj. 易碎的；脆弱的；bristle v. 毛发竖立，气势汹汹 n. 硬毛

bay
bay　［beɪ］
n. 海湾
例 Our favorite fishing spot is in the bay. 我们最喜欢的钓鱼地点是海湾。

bead
bead［bi:d］
n. ①珠子〈同　pearl〉
例　She wore a necklace of brightly colored wooden beads. 她戴着一条颜色鲜艳的木珠项链。
例　Beads of sweat fell from the tennis player's face. 网球运动员的脸上滴下了汗珠。

beak
beak［bi:k］
n. 鸟嘴，喙〈同　nib〉
例　Hunting birds usually have sharp beaks. 猎食鸟类通常都有锐利的喙。

beam
beam　［biːm］
n. ① 大梁〈同 rafter〉
例 One of the Olympic sports for gymnastics is to balance on two beams. 奥运会体操比赛有一个项目是要在双杠上保持平衡。
例 We could just pick out the path in the weak beam of the torch. 我们只能在火把微弱的光亮下辨认路线。

bear
bear　［bɜə(r)］
vt. ① 负担，支撑〈同 support〉
例 The camels bear their cargo across the desert without complaint. 骆驼任劳任怨地驮着货物穿越沙漠。
例 The coins bear the date and the queen's head on them. 硬币上带有日期和女王的头像。
例
联 unbearable adj. 无法忍受的，承受不住的

例　She used a beater to mix ingredients when making baked goods. 在制作烘焙食品时，她使用搅拌机把各种材料混合在一起。

n. 基础；基岩〈同　basis; foundation〉
例　The house by the beach was built on bedrock. 海边的房子建在基岩上。

例 The actor's agent accepted the award on behalf of him. 那位演员的经纪人代他领了奖。

例 The computer behaved without any problems for two months and then one day it suddenly didn't work. 这台电脑连续两个月运转都很正常，但有一天却突然出现了故障。
联 behavior n. 举止，行为

belabor

例　The rider belabored the tired horse with a stick. 骑手用棍子痛打那匹疲惫的马。

例　His coarse, hard-bitten exterior belied his innate sensitivity. 他粗俗、顽强的外表，掩饰了他与生俱来的敏感。

例　The bellicose warrior always wanted to pick a fight with someone. 这个好斗的勇士总是喜欢寻衅打架。

例　The priest gave him a benediction for his good deeds. 牧师因他所做的善事而为他祈祷。

记 bene（善，好）+fic（做）+ial（有…的）→做好事的→有益的

beneficial

例 Charity's goal is to help people in difficulty. 慈善机构的目的是帮助有困难的人。
记 分割联想：char（音似“茶”）+ity→请穷人喝茶→施舍→慈善
联 charitarian n. 慈善家；charitable adj. 仁慈的

charm
charm　［tʃɑːm］
n. 吸引力，（女人的）魅力
例 I used all of my charm to impress Bill. 我发挥自己所有的魅力来给比尔留下印象。

charter
charter　［ˈtʃɑːtə(r)］
vt. 准许（某人或某物）包租；特许〈同 license〉
例 The University of Georgia, chartered in 1785, was the first state-supported university in the United States. 1785年获得特许成立的乔治亚大学，是美国首所由州政府扶持的大学。
n. 宪章，章程
例 The Charter of the United Nation's states its activities and powers. 《联合国宪章》明确了其职能与权力。

chase
chase　［tʃeɪs］
v. 追逐〈同 run after〉
例 The dog chased the cat for nearly half a mile. 那条狗追了那只猫将近半英里。

chaste
chaste［tʃeɪst］
adj. 贞洁的；（思想、言论）朴素的〈同　virtuous; modest〉
例　The conservative woman had decided to be chaste until she got married. 那位保守的女士决定在结婚之前保持贞洁。

chat
chat　［tʃæt］
vi. 闲谈〈同 talk〉
例 Dave chatted on the telephone all evening. 戴维一晚上都在打电话聊天。

cheer
cheer　［tʃɪə(r)］
n. 欢呼〈同 applause〉
例 The crowd gave a cheer when the team scored. 当球队进球的时候，人群发出了欢呼声。
联 cheerful adj. 愉快的，高兴的

chef
chef［∫ef］
n. 厨师
例　When the restaurant hired a better chef, business improved. 餐厅聘请了一位更好的厨师之后，生意逐渐好了起来。

例　An athlete always cherishes the hope of winning a gold medal. 运动员都希望自己能拿金牌。

chew
chew　［tʃuː］
vt. 咀嚼（食物等）
例 It was difficult to chew the tough meat. 这肉太老，很难嚼。

chiefly
chiefly　［ˈtʃiːfli］
adv. 主要地，多半地〈同 mainly〉
例 The decision is chiefly up to the president to make. 决定主要取决于总裁。

childish［'tʃaɪldɪʃ］
adj. 孩子（气）的；幼稚的〈同 immature〉
例　A childish prank ended in a broken window. 窗玻璃被打碎了，孩子的恶作剧才收场。

chill
chill　［tʃɪl］
v. 使冷；变冷，冷却〈同 cool〉
例 The January winds chill everybody. 一月的风让所有人都感到寒冷。
n. 寒意，寒战〈同 coldness〉
例 The chill in the desert at night can be very bad. 沙漠晚上的寒冷会非常难熬。
联 chilly adj. 寒冷的

chip
chip　［tʃɪp］
n. 碎片；芯片
例 I stepped on a chip of stone and bruised my heel. 我踩到了一块碎石，结果擦伤了脚后跟。

chisel［'tʃɪzəl］

例　The artist chiseled a totem from the large tree. 艺术家用大树凿刻出了一个图腾。

例　The gentleman showed his chivalry when opening the door for women. 那位绅士殷勤有礼地为女士们开门。

例 Anne chopped the wood with an axe. 安妮用斧子砍木头。

例　Her parents did not let her go out with her friends until she finished her chores. 她父母不让她与朋友们一起出去，除非她做完家务。

例　The doctors were finally able to attribute his chronic headaches to the gas in his apartment. 医生最终成功诊断出，他慢性头疼的原因在于其公寓里有煤气泄漏。

chunk［tʃʌŋk］

例　Here's a chunk of wood for the fire. 这里有一大块木头可以生火。

cipher［'saɪfə(r)］
n. 密码〈同　code〉
例　Lacking his code book, the spy was unable to decode the messages sent to him in cipher. 由于没有密码本，那个间谍无法破译用密码传递给他的信息。

circuitous
circuitous［sə'kju(:)ɪtəs］
adj. 迂回的，绕圈子的
解　marked by obliqueness or indirection in speech or conduct; deviating from a straight course
例　The taxi driver took the tourists on a circuitous path to the airport. 出租车司机载着乘客绕路来到机场。
同　circuity n. 迂回，绕行

circular
circular［'sɜ:kjʊlə(r)］
adj. 圆形的
解　shaped like a ring
例　The Board always met at a circular table where everyone was equal. 董事会通常举行圆桌会议，这样人人都是平等的。

circulate
circulate　［ˈsɜːkjʊleɪt］
v.（使）循环；（使）传播〈同 circle〉
例 In times of prosperity money circulates quickly, but during a depression it circulates slowly. 货币在繁荣时期流通得很快，而在萧条时期则流通得很慢。
联 circulation n. 循环；流通；circulation desk 图书借还台

circulate
circulate［'sɜ:kjʊleɪt］
v. 流通；发行；传播；循环
解　to cause to be distributed; to flow freely, as of air or liquids
例　The boy circulated newspapers to houses throughout the neighborhood. 男孩在小区内挨家投递报纸。
近　articulate v. 发音清晰；清楚地说话；接合；immaculate adj. 洁净的，无瑕的；maculated adj. 有斑点的
同　circulation n. 流通；循环

circumference
circumference　［sɜːˈkʌmfərəns］
n. 圆周；周长〈同 perimeter〉
例 The highway was built on the circumference of the city. 高速公路绕这座城市而建。
记 circum（环绕）+fer（运载）+ence（名词后缀）→圆周；周长

circumference
circumference［sə'kʌmfərəns］
n. 圆周
解　the length of the closed curve of a circle
例　The circumference of the earth is about 25,000 miles. 地球的赤道周长大约为2.5万英里。
近　interference n. 干预
构　circum (=around) + fer (=to carry) + ence

circumlocution
circumlocution［ˌsɜ:kəmlə'kju:ʃən］
n. 迂回累赘的陈述
解　an indirect way of expressing something
例　The professor set a maximum number of 100 words for the essay so the students' circumlocution would not waste his time. 教授要求文章字数不能超过100字，这样他就不会因为学生的长篇赘述而浪费时间。
构　circum (=around) + locut (=to say) + ion

circumscribe
circumscribe［'sɜ:kəmskraɪb］
vt. 界限；限制〈同　mark the boundaries of; confine〉
例　A terrible illness circumscribed him to bed for a year. 一种严重的疾病让他卧床一年。

circumspect
circumspect［'sɜ:kəmspekt］
adj. 慎重的，仔细的
解　cautious; well-considered; prudent
例　Investigating before taking any action, she tried always to be circumspect. 她在采取行动之前总会先进行调查，努力做到万无一失。
同　circumspection n. 谨慎小心
构　circum (=around) + spect (=to look)

circumstance

例 We need to know the exact circumstances surrounding the accident. 我们需要知道事故发生地周围的具体情况。

circumvent
circumvent［ˌsɜ:kəm'vent］
vt. ① 包围，智取 ② 绕行；避开
解　① to get the better of or defeat by trickery; to outwit ② to go around

collaborate
collaborate［kə'læbəreɪt］
vi. ① 合作 ② 通敌
解　① to work together on a common enterprise or project ② to work treasonably especially with enemy forces occupying one's country
例　The world's scientific community collaborated in the immense task of deciphering the genetic makeup of human DNA. 国际科学界通力合作，一起参与到破译人类基因密码这项庞大的工程中来。
同　collaboration n. 合作；collaborator n. 合作者
构　col < con (=with) + labor (=to work) + ate

compress
compress［kəm'pres］
v. 收缩；压缩
解　to press together or into a smaller space; to squeeze out; to squeeze
例　Compress your speech until only the relevant points remain. 压缩你的演讲，只保留相关的要点。
同　compressor n. 压缩机
构　com < con (=together) + press (=to press)

comprise
comprise　［kəmˈpraɪz］
vt. 包含；由…组成〈同 consist of〉
例 The committee is comprised of seven people. 委员会由七个人组成。

compromise
compromise　［ˈkɒmprəmaɪz］
n. 妥协，折中〈同 concession〉
例 The union chief was willing to reach a compromise on wages but he was intractable when it came to working conditions. 工会主席愿意就工资问题妥协，但在涉及工作环境的问题上，他却非常强硬。
记 com+promise（保证）→相互保证→妥协

compulsory
compulsory［kəm'pʌlsəri］
adj. 必须做的，被强制的〈同 mandatory〉
例　Attending school is compulsory until age sixteen. 16岁前的教育都是义务教育。

concave
concave［'kɒnkeɪv］
adj. 凹的
例　The inside of your eye is the concave side. 你的眼睛内部是凹面。

concave
concave［kɒn'keɪv］
adj. 凹的
解　curving inward
例　The inside of his eyeglasses were concave. 他的眼镜内侧是凹的。

conceal
conceal　［kənˈsiːl］
vt. 隐藏，隐瞒〈同 hide〉
例 He tried to conceal his identity by disguising his voice. 他试图通过伪装自己的嗓音来隐藏身份。

concede
concede　［kənˈsiːd］
v. 承认〈同 acknowledge〉
例 Despite all the evidence Janet had assembled, Bob refused to concede that she was right. 虽然珍妮特收集了大量证据，但鲍勃仍不承认她是对的。

concede
concede［kən'si:d］
v. ① 让步 ② 承认
解　① to make a concession; to yield ② to admit as true; acknowledge
例　I conceded that I had made a mistake. 我承认我犯了一个错误。
同　concession n. 让步；特许，特许权
构　con (=with) + ced (=to go) + e

conceive
conceive［kən'si:v］
vt. 构思；设想〈同 design, consider〉
例　She conceived a plan to expand her company's business. 她想出了一个扩大公司业务的计划。

concentrate
concentrate　［ˈkɒnsəntreɪt］
v. 集中精力，专心〈同 centralize〉
例 The police are concentrating their search in the area where the missing child was last seen. 警方将搜查范围集中在那个失踪的孩子最后被看见的区域。
联 concentration n. 集中；专心；concentrated adj. 集中的；浓缩的

concentrate
concentrate［'kɒnsentreɪt］
v. 浓缩；集中精力 n. 浓缩液
解　v. to make dense or denser; focus one's attention on sth. n. substance or solution made by concentrating
例　The student concentrated only on his studies during the examination period. 在考试期间，这名学生把所有精力都集中在学习上。
同　concentrated adj. 集中精力的；concentration n. 集中

concentric
concentric［kən'sentrɪk］
adj. 同心的
例　The target was made of concentric circles. 靶子是由同心圆组成的。

conception
conception［kən'sepʃən］
n. 观念，认识〈同 thought〉
例　We have no real conception of what people suffered during the war, because our country was not involved in it. 我们对于在战争中人们所遭受的苦难没有真切的认识，因为我们国家没有卷入战争。

concert
concert［'kɒnsət; 'kɒnsɜ:t］
n. ① 音乐会
例　The pianist will give a concert at the music hall. 那位钢琴家将在音乐厅举办一场音乐会。
例　Two countries acted in concert with each other to stop a war. 两个国家共同行动，制止了一场战争。

concession
concession　［kənˈseʃən］
n. ① 让步，迁就
例 Mum does not allow me to play my trumpet in the house, but as a concession I'm allowed to play it in the garage. 妈妈禁止我在屋子里吹喇叭，不过作为让步，她允许我在车库里吹。
例 She owns the restaurant concession that sells food in the public park. 她拥有在公园销售食物的餐厅特许经营权。
记 由concede而来，con（一起）+cede（走，承认）→同意一起走→让步

concise
concise［kən'saɪs］
adj. 简洁的，简明的〈同 succinct〉
例　In spite of the vast number of details in the United States Constitution, the document is remarkably concise. 尽管美国宪法有许多细节，但是这部宪法还是相当简明的。

concise
concise［kən'saɪs］
adj. 简洁的
解　expressing much in few words
例　Poetry is the most concise form of literature. 诗歌是一种最为凝练的文学形式。
构　con (=intensive) + cis (=to cut) + e
同　concision n. 简明，简洁

conclude
conclude［kən'klu:d］
v. ① 得结论 ② 结束
解　① to reach a conclusion after a discussion or deliberation ② to bring to a close
例　The police investigation concluded that the prisoners had escaped the jail through the sewage pipes. 警察通过调查得出了结论：囚犯是通过排污管从监狱里逃走的。

conclusive
conclusive［kən'klu:sɪv］
adj. 最后的，决定性的〈同　decisive, final〉
例　When the stolen books turned up in John's locker, we finally had conclusive evidence of the identity of the mysterious thief. 被盗的书在约翰的柜子里被发现时，我们终于有确凿的证据确认那个神秘窃贼的身份了。

conclusive
conclusive［kən'klu:sɪv］
adj. 结论性的；（事实、证据等）确凿的
解　final and deciding
例　The conclusive evidence affirmed the defendant's guilt. 确凿的证据证实了被告的罪行。

concomitant
concomitant［kən'kɒmɪtənt］
adj. 伴随的
例　Culture is not always concomitant with wealth. 文化并非总是与财富相伴而生。

concrete
concrete　［ˈkɒnkriːt］
n. 水泥〈同 cement〉
例 Dams vary in size from small rock barriers to concrete structures hundreds of feet high. 水坝的规模大小不一，既有小型的岩石屏障，也有数百英尺高的混凝土结构的大坝。
adj. 具体的；实体的〈同 tangible〉
例 Bill prefers concrete facts to abstract ideas. 比起抽象的理念，比尔更喜欢具体的事实。
记 con（共同）+crete（=cre 制造）→共同制造的物品→实体的

concrete
concrete［'kɒnkri:t］
adj. 具体的 n. 混凝土
解　adj. not abstract or imaginary n. a strong hard building material composed of sand, gravel, cement and water
例　The student used specific examples to give a concrete image of his story. 这个学生利用多个详尽的例子，使他的故事有了一个具体的形象。

concur
concur［kən'kɜ:(r)］
v. ① 同意 ② 同时发生
解　① to be in agreement ② to be in accord
例　The directors concurred to accept a new company policy that would increase professionalism. 董事会成员同意接受一项新的公司政策，这项政策可以使公司更加专业化。
同　concurrence n. 同时发生的事
构　con (=together) + cur (=to run)

concurrent
concurrent［kən'kʌrənt］
adj. 同时发生的〈同　simultaneous, coincident〉
例　Working on two concurrent projects can be very exhausting for an author. 同时从事两个项目对于一名作家来说是非常令人疲惫的。

condemn
condemn　［kənˈdem］
vt. 谴责〈同 blame〉
例 The principal condemned smoking by students at school. 校长谴责学生在学校吸烟的行为。
记 con（共同）+demn（=damn 诅咒）→大家诅咒→谴责
联 condemnation n. 谴责

condensation
condensation［ˌkɒnden'seɪʃən］
n. 压缩，浓缩〈同 compression〉
例　This 10-page summary is a condensation of a 100-page report. 这份10页的总结是一份100页报告的浓缩。

condiment
condiment［'kɒndɪmənt］
n. 调味品〈同　seasoning, flavoring〉
例　The only condiment I like on my hamburgers is mustard. 我喜欢在汉堡包上添加的唯一一种佐料是芥末。

conducive
conducive［kən'dju:sɪv］
adj. 有助于…的
解　helpful; contributing to
例　Exercise and proper eating habits are conducive to good health. 锻炼和合理的饮食习惯有益健康。
近　seductive adj. 诱人的，有魅力的
构　con (=together) + duc (=to lead) + ive

conductor
conductor［kən'dʌktə(r)］
n. 指挥家，乐队指挥
解　the person who leads a musical group; director of an orchestra, chorus, etc.
例　The conductor waved his arms around in the air as the symphony played on. 随着交响乐开始演奏，指挥家在空中挥舞着手臂。

confederate
confederate［kən'fedəreɪt］
n. 同盟者，盟友〈同　ally, collaborator〉
例　The criminal recruited a confederate to help rob the bank. 那名罪犯招募了一名同伙，来帮助他抢劫银行。

confer
confer［kən'fɜ:(r)］
v. ① 颁给，赋予（on）〈同 bestow〉
例　The President of Harvard University conferred a doctorate on the distinguished politician. 哈佛大学校长授予这位著名的政治家博士头衔。
例　One should confer with one's elders before making a big decision. 在做重大决定之前应该和前辈商量一下。

conference
conference［'kɒnfərəns］
n. 会议；协商会，讨论会〈同 meeting, discussion〉
例　A conference was called to discuss getting a playground for the school. 为了讨论给学校建操场的事情召开了一次会议。

confess
confess　［kənˈfes］
vt. 坦白，承认 vi. 承认错误，认罪〈同 acknowledge〉
例 Janet confessed that she had told a lie. 珍妮特承认自己撒了谎。
联 confession n. 承认，招供

confidant
confidant［ˌkɒnfɪ'dænt］
n. 心腹朋友，知己
解　trusted friend
例　She had many friends but only one confidant to whom she recounted her deepest secrets. 她有许多朋友，但是只有一个知心朋友可以用来倾诉她心里最深处的秘密。
同　confidante n. 知心女友

confide
confide［kən'faɪd］
vt. 吐露（心事），倾诉〈同　disclose, reveal〉
例　When they were children, she always confided her problems to her big sister. 她们还是小孩子的时候，她总是把自己的问题说给姐姐听。

confident
confident　［ˈkɒnfɪdənt］
adj. 有信心的，自信的〈同 assured〉
例 Tom does not seem confident when he speaks in public. 汤姆在公共场合说话时，似乎不够自信。
记 con+fid（相信）+ent→相信（自己）→自信的
联 confidence n. 信心；overconfident adj. 过于自信的，自负的

confident
confident［'kɒnfɪdənt］
adj. 自信的，有信心的
解　sure of oneself
例　Willie was so confident that he had passed the exam that he did not even bother to check the answers before handing in his answer sheet. 威利对通过考试十分有把握，甚至在交答卷之前都没有检查一下。
同　confidence n. 信心；self-confident adj. 有自信的
构　con (=completely) + fid (=trust) + ent

confidential
confidential［ˌkɒnfɪ'denʃəl］
adj. 秘密的，机密的〈同 secret〉
例　Only highly trusted employees could read the confidential report. 只有非常可信的雇员才能看这份机密报告。

confidential
confidential［ˌkɒnfɪ'denʃəl］
adj. 机密的
解　told or written as a secret
例　Only highly trusted employees could look at the confidential report. 只有被高度信任的员工才能看这份机密报告。
构　con (=completely) + fid (=trust) + ential

configuration
configuration［kənˌfɪgə'reɪʃən; (US)kənˌfɪgjʊ'reɪʃən］

confine

例 Please confine your comments to the topic assigned. 请在指定的主题范围内作评论。

confine
confine［kən'faɪn］
vt. 限制，禁闭
解　to keep within limits; to restrict; to keep in; to shut in
例　The farmer confined the pigs with a fence so they wouldn' t run away. 农夫把猪关在栅栏里，这样它们就不会跑掉。
同　confinement n. 监禁

confirm
confirm　［kənˈfɜːm］
vt. 证实，使…更坚定〈同 verify, corroborate〉
例 Years of research confirmed the theory that smoking is harmful. 持续数年的研究证实了吸烟有害健康的理论。

conflict
conflict　［ˈkɒnflɪkt］
n. 争论；冲突〈同 fight〉
例 Many citizens were killed in an armed conflict with a neighboring country. 许多平民在与邻国的武装冲突中丧生。
联 conflicting adj. 相冲突的，相矛盾的

confluence
confluence［'kɒnflʊəns］
n. 汇合；聚集〈同　conflux; throng〉
例　Mighty rivers often come into being at the confluence of several small streams. 气势磅礴的河流往往是由许多小溪流汇集而成的。

confluence
confluence［'kɒnflʊəns］
n. 汇流处；合流，汇流
解　the place where two things come together; a flowing together
例　The land near the confluence of the river would often get flooded when it rained heavily. 当雨下得很大时，河流汇合点附近的这片土地经常被淹没。
构　con (=together) + flu (=to flow) + ence

conform
conform［kən'fɔ:m］
vi. 遵守，顺从；符合（to）〈同 comply with, follow〉
例　Every member must conform to the rules of our club. 每位会员必须遵守我们社团的规章制度。

conform
conform［kən'fɔ:m］
v. 使一致；遵守，顺从
解　to obey or be in accordance with established rules
例　The professor told the students blatantly that they can either conform to his rules or fail. 教授明确告诉学生，如果他们不遵从他制定的规则就会不及格。
同　conformity n. 符合，一致；遵从

conformist
conformist［kən'fɔ:mɪst］
n. 遵奉习俗者，墨守成规的人
解　someone who conforms to established standards of conduct
例　He was not a conformist and refused to follow the status quo. 他不是一个墨守成规的人，拒绝维持现状。
同　nonconformist n. 我行我素的人，不遵循社会常规的人 adj. 不遵循社会常规的

confront
confront　［kənˈfrʌnt］
vt.（使）面对，正视〈同 face〉
例 If you confront your problems honestly and openly, instead of trying to hide them, you will have a better chance of solving them. 如果你真诚地、坦率地面对问题，而不是试图隐藏它们，你就更有机会解决这些问题。
记 con（共同）+front（面，前面）→共同面对→(使）面对，正视
联 confrontation n. 对抗

confront
confront［kən'frʌnt］
v. ① 面对，面临 ② 对抗
解　① to be or come face to face with ② to be opposite to
例　If you confront your problems honestly and openly, instead of trying to hide them, you will have a better chance of solving them. 如果你诚实、坦然地面对自己的问题，而不是试图隐瞒它们，那么你解决这些问题的可能性就更大。
同　confrontation n. 对抗
构　con (=together) + front (=forehead, face)

congenial
congenial［kən'ʤi:nɪəl］
adj.（因性情、志趣等相近而）彼此合得来的；适意的〈同　compatible; agreeable〉
例　My father loved to go out for a meal with congenial companions. 我爸爸过去喜欢和意气相投的朋友一起出去吃饭。

congenial
congenial［kən'ʤi:niəl］
adj. 意气相投的
解　having similar tastes and interests; getting on well together
例　Congenial companions made the trip pleasant. 意气相投的伙伴使旅途变得愉快。

congestion

congregate

conjunction

conquer
conquer　［ˈkɒŋkə(r)］

例 Bill finally conquered his bad habit of laughing during sad movies. 比尔最终克服了在看悲剧电影时大笑的坏习惯。

conquest
conquest　［ˈkɒnkwest］
n. 征服
例 The country's wild ambition for the conquest of the world made all of its neighbors nervous. 这个国家征服世界的野心，令所有周边国家非常紧张。

conquest

n. 征服

例　The famous Mongolian warrior's military campaign had a history of countless conquests. 这个著名的蒙古勇士战功显赫，征服的地方数不胜数。

conscience
conscience　［ˈkɒnʃəns］
n. 良心，良知
例 My conscience made me help the poor old lady. 出于良知，我帮助了那位贫困的老妇人。
联 conscientious adj. 尽职尽责的

conscientious
conscientious［ˌkɒnʃɪ'enʃəs］
adj. 尽责的，一丝不苟的〈同 responsible, reliable〉
例　Conscientious work is careful and exact. 认真尽责的工作意味着细心和准确。

conscious
conscious　［ˈkɒnʃəs］
adj. ① 有意识的，神志清醒的〈同 awake〉
例 I fainted briefly but was conscious again in a few seconds. 我突然晕倒，但在几秒钟之后又恢复了意识。
例 Human should be more conscious of the influence they have on ecosystems. 人类应该更加意识到自己对于生态系统的影响。
记 con（共同）+sci（知道）+ous→知道的→有意识的
联 consciousness n. 意识，知觉；unconscious adj. 不省人事的；未发觉的，无意识的；subconscious adj. 潜意识的

consecutive
consecutive［kən'sekjʊtɪv］
adj. 连续的〈同 successive, sequential〉
例　He was reelected for four consecutive terms. 他又连着当选了四次。

consensus
consensus［kən'sensəs］
n. 意见一致〈同 agreement〉
例　The council reached a consensus on the date of the election. 委员会就选举日期达成一致。

consent
consent［kən'sent］
n./vi. 同意，赞同〈同 approval, agree〉
例　You need the principal's consent to leave campus. 你得到校长的同意才可以离开学校。

consequence
consequence　［ˈkɒnsɪkwəns; (US)ˈkɒnsəkwens］
n. 结果，后果〈同 result〉
例 I missed the bus this morning and as a consequence I was late for work. 我今天早上没有赶上公共汽车，结果上班迟到了。
联 consequent adj. 作为结果的，随之发生的；consequently adv. 从而，因此

consequence
consequence［'kɒnsɪkwəns］
n. ① 结果 ② 重要的地位
解　① a result or effect ② importance
例　The consequence of the fall was a broken leg. 这次跌倒的后果是把腿摔断了。
构　con (=with) + sequ (=to follow) + ence

consequent
consequent［'kɒnsɪkwənt］
adj. 作为结果的，随之发生的〈同 resulting〉
例　His long illness and consequent absence put him far behind in his work. 他久病请假，使他的工作落后了许多。

consequential
consequential［ˌkɒnsɪ'kwenʃəl］
adj. 重要的；产生后果的
解　having important issues or results
例　Ben Franklin was a consequential figure in the American history. 本·富兰克林是美国历史上的一个重要的人物。
构　con (=with) + sequ (=to follow) + ential

conservation　［ˌkɒnsəˈveɪʃən］
n. 保存，保持，保护〈同 preservation〉
例 The government encourages the conservation of natural gas. 政府鼓励大家节约使用天然气。
联 conservationist n. 自然资源保护论者

conservative
conservative　［kənˈsɜːvətɪv］
adj. 保守的，谨慎的；守旧的〈同 cautious〉
例 The builder's conservative estimate of the time required to remodel the kitchen was six weeks. 施工人员对改造厨房所需时间的保守估计是六周。
记 con+serv(e)（保持）+ative→保守的
联 conservatism n. 保守主义，守旧性

例　An experienced backpacker can give you many suggestions for conserving energy on a long, tough hike. 一位经验丰富的背包客可以在长途跋涉方面给你很多保存体力的建议。

联 consideration n. 体谅；考虑

consist　［kənˈsɪst］

consistent　［kənˈsɪstənt］
adj. 一致的；稳定的，变化少的〈同 regular〉

联 consistency n. 一致性，连贯性；consistently adv. 一贯地

constant
constant　［ˈkɒnstənt］
adj.（恒久）不变的，持续的；一再重复的〈同 invariable〉
例 I can't sleep because of the constant noise of the cars and trucks in the street. 我睡不着，因为大街上不断传来汽车和卡车的噪音。

contemporary　［kənˈtempərəri］

contradict

例　Janet paid a costly salary to hire an American teacher to help her improve her English. 珍妮特高薪聘请了一位美国老师来帮她提高英语水平。

costume
costume［'kɒstju:m; (US)'kɒstu:m］
n. 服装〈同 attire〉
例　The actors in the play had beautiful costumes. 剧中的演员们穿着好看的服装。

couch
couch［kaʊtʃ］
n. 长椅，长沙发〈同 sofa〉
例　A couch refers to a long seat, usually upholstered and having a back and arms. 长沙发都有长长的座位，通常装软垫，并且有靠背和扶手。
vt.（用语言）表达〈同 express〉
例　His thoughts were couched in beautiful language. 他用优美的语言表达了自己的想法。

counteract［ˌkaʊntər'ækt］

例　She tries to counteract her former rudeness by being especially polite now. 为了消除之前的粗鲁无礼（的形象），她现在特别有礼貌。

counterargument［'kaʊntəˌɑ:gjʊmənt］
n. 辩论，抗辩
解　an argument in opposition to another
例　The winning team of the debate contest had the best arguments and counterarguments. 这场辩论赛的获胜队拥有最好的论据和反论据。

counterfeit
counterfeit［'kaʊntəfɪt］
vt. 伪造，仿造〈同　forge〉
例　Advances in photocopying technology allow criminals with no printing expertise to easily counterfeit paper currency. 随着复印技术的发展，没有任何印刷专业技术的罪犯也很容易就能伪造纸币。
adj. 伪造的，假冒的〈同　bogus, fake〉
例　The bank refused to take the counterfeit money. 银行拒绝接收假币。

counterfeit
counterfeit［'kaʊntəfɪt］
v. 伪造，仿造 n. 伪造物；伪钞
解　v. to make a copy of with the intent to deceive
n. a copy that is presented as the original
例　This twenty-dollar bill looks genuine, but it is really a counterfeit. 这张20美元的钞票看起来很像真的，但其实是假钞。
近　forfeit v. 丧失，被罚没收 n. 丧失物；surfeit n. 过多，过度，过饱 v. 使吃饱
构　counter (=against) + feit (=to make)

countermand
countermand［ˌkaʊntə'mɑ:nd］
v. 取消订货；撤回（命令）
解　to withdraw or cancel (an order or command)
例　The general countermanded the air strike when it was discovered that the target had many innocent civilians. 当发现袭击地点有很多无辜的平民时，将军下令取消了空袭。
构　counter (=against) + mand (=to order)

countermand
countermand［ˌkaʊntə'mɑ:nd］
v. 取消订货；撤回（命令）
解　to withdraw or cancel (an order or command)
例　Since Greg was late for work, he countermanded his order for a steak and ate a sandwich instead. 由于上班迟到了，格雷格取消了牛排的订单，改吃三明治了。
构　counter (=against) + mand (=to order)

v. 下定义
解　to make clear the meaning of; to explain
例　An English-Chinese dictionary can define words but can not truly explain the cultural significance behind them. 英汉词典可以给单词下定义，但是无法真正解释其背后的文化意义。

definite
definite　［ˈdefɪnət］
adj. 清楚的；明确的〈同 distinct; exact〉
例 Roger needs to know the definite arrival time so he can meet his friend on time at the airport. 罗杰需要知道确切的抵达时间，以便准时到机场接朋友。
联 definitely adv. 明确地，肯定地

definite
definite［'defɪnət］
adj. 确定的
解　clear or exact; not vague
例　I expect a definite answer, either yes or no. 我期待一个确切的答案，要么是，要么不是。
同　indefinite adj. 不清楚的，模糊的；不确定的

definition
definition［ˌdefɪ'nɪʃən］
n. ① 定义 ② （轮廓等）清晰，明确
解　① a statement of the meaning of a word, phrase, or term, as in a dictionary entry ② the state of being closely outlined or determined
例　Their marriage was doomed to fail because they each had a different definition of commitment. 他们的婚姻注定要失败，因为他们各自对承诺有着不同的定义。

adj. 决定性的，最后的〈同　conclusive, ultimate〉
例　There are no definitive answers to this problem. 这个问题没有明确的答案。

definitive
definitive［dɪ'fɪnɪtɪv］
adj. 最后的，确定的，权威性的
解　supplying or being a final or conclusive settlement; conclusive
例　Carl Sandburg's Abraham Lincoln may be regarded as the definitive work on the life of the Great Emancipator. 卡尔·桑德堡所写的《亚伯拉罕·林肯》可以被认为是把这位伟大的解放者的生平诠释得最好的作品。
构　de (=intensive) + fin (=end) + itive

例 Many people lost their fortune during the Great Depression. 在大萧条期间，许多人倾家荡产。
例 I'm beginning to get over the deep depression I felt about losing my job. 我开始克服失业带来的深度抑郁。
记 来自depress：de（向下）+press（压）→压制
联 depressant n. 镇静剂；depressive adj. 郁闷的
derive　［dɪˈraɪv］
vt. 得到，获取；源于〈同 obtain〉
例 He derives a lot of pleasure from meeting new people. 他从认识新朋友当中获得许多乐趣。
记 de（分离）+rive（=river 河流）→从河里引水→获取；源于
联 derivative n. 派生的事物，派生词；derivation n. 由来，出处

deprive
deprive［dɪ'praɪv］
vt. 剥夺，使失去〈同 deny, take away〉
例　He was deprived of his sight by the accident. 那次事故使他丧失了视力。

deputy［'depjʊti］
n. 代理人，代表；副手〈同　agent; assistant, aide〉

n. 皮肤病学
解　the branch of medicine dealing with the skin and its diseases
例　He was concerned about his skin rash and visited a specialist in dermatology. 他担心自己的皮疹，于是拜访了一位皮肤病方面的专家。

n. 脱盐，去盐作用

descend
descend　［dɪˈsend］
v. ① 传下，遗传
例 The noble qualities descend to me from my father. 我的贵族气质遗传自我的父亲。
例 The bird descended quickly to capture the worm that crawled out of a hole. 那只鸟快速往下飞来捕捉那只爬出洞口的虫子。
记 de（向下）+scend（爬）→爬下→下降
联 descendant n. 后代，后裔；descent n. 下降；血统

dysfunctional
dysfunctional［dɪs'fʌnkʃənəl］
adj. 功能紊乱的；（人际关系）不良的，不和睦的
解　maladjusted; not following the normal patterns of social behaviour
例　Both parents were alcoholics and were considered dysfunctional. 这对父母都是酗酒者，关系不和睦。

dyslexia
dyslexia［dɪs'leksɪə］
n. 阅读障碍
解　impaired ability to read
例　The child suffered from dyslexia and needed a special tutor to learn how to read. 这个小孩患有阅读障碍，需要一个特殊的家庭教师来教他怎样阅读。

earnest
earnest　［ˈɜːnɪst］
adj. 认真的；热心的〈同 serious〉
例 The earnest student studied constantly. 那个认真的学生不断地学习。

earnings
earnings［'ɜ:nɪŋz］
n. 所得，收入〈同 income〉
例　My earnings for the job weren't as high as I expected. 这份工作的收入没有我期望的高。

earplug
earplug［'ɪəplʌɡ］
n. 耳塞
解　an object made of a soft, pliable material, such as cotton or rubber, and fitted into the ear canal to block the entry of water or sound
例　Don' t forget to put in your earplugs when you go swimming. 游泳的时候别忘了戴上耳塞。

earring
earring［'ɪərɪŋ］
n. 耳环，耳饰
解　jewelry to ornament the ear, usually clipped to the earlobe or fastened through a hole in the lobe
例　On the day she got her ears pierced, her mother bought her a pair of diamond earrings. 在她打耳洞的那天，她母亲给她买了一对钻石耳环。

earshot
earshot［'ɪəʃɒt］
n. 听力范围
解　distance at which a sound can be heard; range of hearing
例　We shouted, but he was already out of earshot and could not hear us. 我们大声地叫喊，可是他离得太远，已经听不到了。

earsplitting
earsplitting［'ɪəspli:tɪŋ］
adj. 震耳欲聋的
解　loud and shrill enough to hurt the ears
例　The music that the rock band played was not only horrible; it was also earsplitting. 这个摇滚乐队演奏的音乐不仅糟糕透顶，简直到了震耳欲聋的地步。

ease
ease［i:z］
n. 安逸；悠闲〈同 easiness, leisure〉
例　The reporter writes with great ease, because he is good at writing and did a lot of research on this topic. 因为这位记者十分擅长写作，并且对这个选题做了很多研究，所以他写起来很轻松。

eavesdropper
eavesdropper［'i:vzˌdrɒpə(r)］
n. 偷听者
解　a secret listener to private conversations
例　The eavesdropper was an undercover police detective trying to overhear a conversation to get clues to a crime. 偷听者是一位卧底警探，他试着从对话中听出犯罪案件的线索。

eccentric
eccentric［ɪk'sentrɪk］
adj./n. 古怪的（人），异常的（人）〈同 strange, odd〉
例　If you go to the palace in tennis shoes, they'll think you're rather eccentric. 如果你穿着网球鞋去王宫，他们会觉得你十分古怪。

eccentric
eccentric［ɪk'sentrɪk］
n. 古怪的人 adj. 古怪的，反常的
解　n. a person with an unusual or odd personality adj. conspicuously or grossly unconventional or unusual
例　The new science fiction park attracted many eccentrics who liked to wear alien costumes. 这个新的科幻公园吸引了许多喜欢穿着奇装异服的古怪的人。
同　eccentricity n. 古怪，怪癖；反常
构　ec (=out) + centr (=center) + ic

echo
echo　［ˈekəʊ］
v. 发出回声；反射
例 The hills echoed his shout. 大山传来他叫喊的回声。
n. 回声，回音
例 An echo bounced off the bluff . 从悬崖上传回一阵回音。

eclectic
eclectic［ɪ'klektɪk］
adj. 折中的，综合性的
解　selecting what seems best of various styles or ideas
例　His style of interior decoration was eclectic: bits and pieces of furnishings from widely divergent periods, strikingly juxtaposed to create a unique decor. 他的室内装修风格不拘一格，属于多个不同时期的各式家具醒目地摆放在一起，形成了一种独特的风格。
同　eclecticism n. 折中主义
构　ec < ex (=out) + lect (=to choose) + ic

eclecticism
eclecticism［ɪ'klektɪsɪzəm］
n. 折中主义
例　Eclecticism is the practice of mixing elements dissimilar in style in a single work of art. 折中主义是将风格迥异的元素混合在一件艺术作品中的做法。

eclipse
eclipse［ɪ'klɪps］
n. 日食，月食
例　There will be a lunar eclipse tonight. 今晚会有月食。
vt. 盖过，使失色；遮蔽〈同 shadow〉
例　She is completely eclipsed by her sister, who is cleverer, prettier and more amusing. 她在她妹妹面前黯然失色。她的妹妹比她更聪明、更漂亮、更迷人。

ecology
ecology［ɪ'kɒləʤi］
n. 生态（学）；生态平衡
例　The oil spill caused terrible damage to the fragile ecology of the coastline. 石油泄漏给脆弱的沿海生态环境造成了严重的破坏。

economical
economical　［ˌiːkəˈnɒmɪkəl］
adj. 经济的；节俭的〈同 thrifty, saving〉
例 Comparing prices is an economical way to shop for groceries. 购买食品杂货时，比较价格是一种省钱的方式。
记 economic（节约的）+al→节俭的
联 economics n. 经济学

economize
economize［ɪ'kɒnəmaɪz］
vi. 节约，节省〈同　save, be thrifty〉
例　We must economize on scarce resources. 我们必须节省稀缺资源。

edge
edge［eʤ］
n. 边缘〈同 brink〉
例　John is at the edge of death. 约翰处于死亡的边缘。

edible
edible［'edəbəl］
adj. 可食用的〈同 eatable〉
例　Laurels are valued for their aromatic oils and spices, edible fruits and timber. 月桂树的价值在于能提供芳香油、香料、可食用的果实以及木料。

edifice
edifice［'edɪfɪs］
n. 宏伟的建筑物〈同　skyscraper〉
例　The huge edifice is a tribute to modern architecture. 这座宏伟的建筑是对现代建筑的致敬。

edit
edit　［ˈedɪt］
vt. 编辑，校订
例 You must edit this video before it goes on television. 这段视频在电视上播放之前，你必须对其进行编辑。
联 edition n. 版本，版；editor n. 编辑，编者；editorial n. 社论

educate
educate［'edju(:)keɪt］
v. 教育
解　to develop in knowledge or skill by teaching, training, or study; to teach
例　The parents educated their children in proper etiquette. 这对父母教孩子形成了良好的礼节。
同　educated adj. 受过教育的；education n. 教育；educator n. 教师

educated
educated［'edju:keɪtɪd］
adj. 受过教育的，有教养的〈同　informed, learned〉
例　Educated men never stop learning. 受过教育的人永远不会停止学习。

efface
efface［ɪ'feɪs］
v. 擦掉，抹去
解　to obliterate by rubbing out
例　Even one hundred years would never efface her memory of his abuse. 即使过去一百年，她被他虐待的记忆也无法被抹去。
构　ef < ex (=out) + fac (=face) + e

effective
effective［ɪ'fektɪv］
adj. 有效的；生效的〈同 efficient, productive〉
例　Sharing corporate stocks with employees can be an effective way to promote harmony, efficiency and equitability in the workplace. 让员工入股可以有效地提高职场的和谐、效率和公平的程度。

effervescent
effervescent［ˌefə'vesnt］
adj. ① 冒泡的 ② 兴奋的
解　① giving off bubbles of gas; bubbling ② lively and gay
例　He had forgotten to close the soda bottle yesterday and the soda was no longer effervescent. 他昨天忘记将苏打水的瓶盖拧上，今天苏打水已经没有气泡了。

efficient
efficient　［ɪˈfɪʃənt］
adj. 生效的；能干的，有效率的〈同 effective〉
例 The financial analyst found efficient ways for the company to save money. 财务分析师发现了帮公司省钱的有效途径。
记 ef+fici（效果，效率）+ent→有效率的
联 efficiency n. 效率，功效

effluent
effluent［'eflʊənt］
n. 流出物
例　It would be terrible if effluent from the metal factory reached the river. 如果金属加工厂的废水流入河中，后果会非常糟糕。

effortless
effortless［'efətləs］
adj. 不费力的
解　requiring or showing little or no effort; easy
例　The cat pounced on the mouse with an effortless leap. 猫轻轻一跳，扑过去抓住了老鼠。

effrontery
effrontery［e'frʌntəri］
n. 厚颜无耻；无礼
解　impudence; shameless, boldness
例　She had the effrontery to insult the guest. 她竟敢厚颜无耻地辱骂客人。
构　ef < ex (=out) + front (=forehead) + ery

effusive
effusive［ɪ'fju:sɪv］
adj. ① 过分表达感情的 ② 流出的
解　① showing too much feeling too demonstrative and emotional ② overflowing
例　Every visitor noticed that her effusive welcome was not sincere. 每个来访者都注意到，她过分表现出来的欢迎并不是真诚的。
构　ef < ex (=out) + fus (=to pour) + ive

egocentric
egocentric［ˌi:ɡəʊ'sentrɪk］
adj. 自我中心的，利己主义的
解　limited to or caring only about yourself and your own needs
例　During medieval times, many men held the egocentric belief that the sun revolved around the earth. 在中世纪，许多人信奉以自我为中心的观念，认为太阳围绕地球旋转。
同　egotist n. 自我主义者

egress
egress［'i:ɡres］
n. 出口，出去 v. 外出
解　n. a place or means of going out v. to go out
例　The egress in case of a fire is on either side of the hallway and down the stairs. 发生火灾时的紧急出口位于走廊的两侧和楼梯的下面。
构　e (=out) + gress (=to walk)

eject
eject［ɪ'ʤekt］
vt. ① 逐出，驱逐〈同 expel〉
例　The hooligans were ejected from the restaurant. 小流氓被赶出了餐厅。
例　Ants eject formic acid when another insect tries to attack them. 当被其他昆虫攻击的时候，蚂蚁就会释放出蚁酸。

elaborate
elaborate
例 The judge wrote an elaborate proposal for a new law. 法官撰写了一个详细的新法律提案。
例 I understand the basic idea, but could you elaborate on that？我理解基本意思，但你能详细说明一下吗？
记 e（出）+labor（劳动）+ate→（努力）劳动做出来的→精细的
联 elaborately adv. 精心地，精细地；elaboration n. 精心计划，精巧

elaborate
elaborate［ɪ'læbərət］adj. 复杂的，精致的［ɪ'læbəreɪt］v. 详尽地说明，阐明；精工细做
解　adj. developed or executed with care and in minute v. to talk or write in great detail; work out with great care
例　The president's spokesperson was asked to elaborate on his answer after he had given a short answer to a controversial question. 在针对一个有争议的问题作出简单的回答之后，总统的发言人被要求作出详细说明。

elapse
elapse［ɪ'læps］
vi.（时间）过去，消逝〈同 slip away, pass〉
例　Many hours elapsed while I slept. 我睡了好多个小时。

elastic
elastic　［ɪˈlæstɪk］
adj. 有弹性的〈同 pliant〉
例 Rubber can be made so elastic that it will stretch more than nine times its normal length. 塑料可以做得非常有弹性，甚至可以拉伸到正常长度的九倍以上。
记 e+last（延长）+ic→可延长出去的→有弹性的
联 elasticity n. 弹力，弹性；inelastic adj. 无弹性的

elderly
elderly［'eldəli］
adj. 过了中年的；近老年的；稍老的〈同 old〉
例　The elderly woman lives with her grandson. 老妇人和她的孙子一起生活。

election

例　How many people voted in the last election? 在上一次选举中，有多少人参加了投票？

election
election［ɪ'lekʃən］
n. 选举
解　a choosing or selecting for an office by vote
例　In our city we have an election for mayor every four years. 我们的城市每隔四年选举一次市长。

elective
elective［ɪ'lektɪv］
adj. 随意选择的
解　open to choice; not required
例　The university curriculum mandates a number of requisite courses, but allows students to pick a few elective courses. 大学的课程指定了许多必修课，但是也允许学生选择几门选修课。

elegant
elegant　［ˈelɪɡənt］

elevate
elevate［'elɪveɪt］
vt. 举起；抬高；使上升〈同 raise〉
例　The marchers elevated the flag as they passed the president. 从总统身边走过的时候，游行者举起了旗帜。

elevate
elevate［'elɪveɪt］
v. 提高，抬升
解　to raise from a lower to a higher position
例　Bruce sprained his ankle, so he had to elevate his leg and put ice on it. 布鲁斯扭伤了脚踝，因此他不得不将腿抬起来，并且在脚踝处敷上冰块。

elevation
elevation［elɪ'veɪʃən］
n. 海拔
解　height above sea level
例　The high elevation of the mountain made it difficult to breathe. 山的海拔很高，让人觉得呼吸困难。

elevator
elevator［'elɪveɪtə(r)］
n. 电梯
解　a moving platform or cage to carry people and things up and down in a building, mine, etc.
例　Some people have the inefficient habit of trying to get into an elevator before the people inside leave. 有些人在乘坐电梯时有种不良的习惯，总是在里面的人还没出来时就抢着要进去。

elicit
elicit［ɪ'lɪsɪt］
vt. 得出；引出〈同 draw forth〉
例　The comedian's joke elicited laughter from the audience. 喜剧演员的笑话逗得观众哈哈大笑。

eligible
eligible［'elɪʤəbəl］
adj. 合格的，有资格的〈同 qualified〉
例　Only native-born citizens are eligible for the office of President. 只有本国公民才有资格当总统。

eliminate
eliminate　［ɪˈlɪmɪneɪt］
vt. 排除，剔除〈同 eradicate，remove〉
例 The teacher eliminated mistakes from the student's essay. 老师挑出了学生论文中的错误。
记 e+limin（门槛）+ate→扔出门槛→剔除
联 elimination n. 排除，除去；eliminable adj. 可消除的

elite
elite［eɪ'li:t］
n. 精英，中坚分子
例　Only the elites attended the reception for the visiting queen. 只有社会精英们参加了女王访问招待会。

elixir
elixir［ɪ'lɪksə(r)］
n. 长生不老药，仙丹妙药〈同　cure-all〉
例　The elixir which can cure all diseases does not exist. 能治愈所有疾病的万能药是不存在的。

elliptical
elliptical［ɪ'lɪptɪkəl］

例　The Earth's orbit is elliptical. 地球的轨道是椭圆形的。
例　An elliptical remark baffles because it is not perfectly clear. 晦涩的言辞让人困惑，因为它不够清楚。

elongate
elongate［'i:lɒŋgeɪt; (US)ɪ'lɒŋ-］
vt. 延长，伸长〈同　lengthen, extend〉
例　The dog pulled on the sweater and elongated the sleeve. 那条狗拽着毛衣，把袖子都拉长了。

eloquent
eloquent［'eləkwənt］
adj. 善于表达的，有口才的，雄辩的〈同 persuasive〉
例　Janet is an eloquent speaker and good at business negotiation. 珍妮特口才很好，擅长商业谈判。

eloquent
eloquent［'eləkwənt］
n. ① 雄辩的，有口才的 ② 动人的
解　① having the ability to express emotion or feeling in lofty and impassioned speech ② very expressive
例　The graduation speaker was very eloquent in his speech. 这位演讲者在毕业典礼上的演说十分精彩。
同　eloquence n. 雄辩；口才

elsewhere

例 My house keys are not where I thought I left them last night. I will have to search elsewhere to find them. 我家的钥匙不在我印象中昨晚上放的地方。我得去别处找找。

elucidate

例　Since there were many questions in class, the professor elucidated on the topic. 由于同学们对这一话题有很多问题，教授对它进行了阐明。

elude
elude［ɪ'lu:d］
v. （机敏地）躲避，避开；记不起来
解　to escape, either physically or mentally
例　The student knew the response to the question but it somehow eluded his tongue at the most critical moment. 这名学生知道这个问题的答案，但是不知何故在关键时候却怎么也想不起来。
构　e < ex (=out) + lud (=to play) + e

elusive
elusive［ɪ'lu:sɪv］

例　Although he possesses great wealth, he finds happiness quite elusive. 虽然他拥有大量财富，但他却发现幸福非常令人难以捉摸。

elusive
elusive［ɪ'lu:sɪv］
adj. 难懂的，难捉摸的
解　difficult to detect or grasp by the mind
例　The elusive fox got away. 狡猾的狐狸逃走了。
构　e < ex ( =out) + lus (=to play) + ive

emancipate
emancipate［ɪ'mænsɪpeɪt］
vt. 解放，释放〈同　liberate, free〉
例　Abraham Lincoln emancipated four million African slaves. 亚伯拉罕·林肯使四百万非洲奴隶重获自由。

emancipate
emancipate［ɪ'mænsɪpeɪt］
vt. 释放，解除
解　to set free from slavery or restraint; to release
例　American slaves were emancipated during the Civil War. 美国奴隶在内战期间得到解放。
构　e < ex (=out) + man < manu (=hand) + cip < cap (=to take) + ate

embark
embark［ɪm'bɑ:k］
v. ①（使）上船（或飞机）〈同 board〉
例　The ship will leave soon and all passengers must embark in ten minutes. 船马上就要起航了，所有乘客务必在十分钟内登船。
例　After leaving college, Janet embarked upon a business career. 离开大学之后，珍妮特开始了商业生涯。

embarrass

vt. 使尴尬，使困窘〈同 humiliate〉
例 I was embarrassed by his comments about my poor clothes. 他说我的衣服非常破旧，这话让我非常尴尬。
联 embarrassment n. 困窘；阻碍

embassy

例　While traveling abroad we had to go to the Chinese embassy to resolve the emergency. 在境外旅行遇到紧急情况时，我们不得不去中国大使馆寻求帮助。

embed
embed［ɪm'bed］
vt. 插入；镶嵌〈同 encase〉
例　Small stones were embedded in the ice. 小石子嵌入了冰块里。

vt. 装饰，修饰〈同　adorn, beautify〉
例　Anne embellished the shirt collar with lace. 安妮用蕾丝装饰衬衫的领子。

emblem

例　Mace is the emblem of the authority of the king. 权杖是国王权威的象征。

embody
embody［ɪm'bɒdi］

例　My grandmother embodies all the qualities of her generation. 我的祖母体现了她这一代人所具有的所有素质。

例　The printer embossed my company's name on my business cards. 印刷公司为我的名片上的公司名称做了浮雕工艺。

embrace
embrace　［ɪmˈbreɪs］
vt. ① 包含 〈同 include〉
例 This course embraces several different aspects of psychology. 这门课包含了心理学的几个不同方面。
例 You'd be a fool not to embrace an opportunity as good as that. 如果你不抓住这么好的机会，那你就是个傻瓜。
记 em（=in 进）+brace（胳膊）→搂进胳膊里→拥抱

vt. 刺绣，镶边；装饰〈同　decorate, adorn〉

记 e（出）+merge（吞没）→被吞没的东西又露出来了→出现，浮现
联 emergence n. 出现，形成

例　He was so firmly entrenched as the political leader of the district that efforts to displace him proved completely futile. 他作为这个地区政治领袖的地位非常稳固，任何试图取代他的努力都被证明完全是徒劳的。

excessive［ɪk'sesɪv］
adj. 过度的，过分的，过多的〈同 extreme, too much〉
例　You must curb your excessive spending, or you will become penniless. 你必须控制你的过度消费，否则你会变得身无分文。

excessive
excessive［ɪk'sesɪv］
adj. 过度的，过分的，过多的
解　beyond normal limits
例　The policeman was accused of using excessive force when he punched the innocent man. 这名警察拳击了这位无罪的男子，被指控为滥用武力。
同　excess n. 过多
构　ex (=beyond) + cess (=to go) + ive

exchange
exchange　［ɪksˈtʃeɪnʤ］
n./vt. 兑换，交换〈同 substitute〉
例 Most Americans exchange gifts at Christmas. 大多数美国人在圣诞节的时候会交换礼物。

excise
excise［ek'saɪz］
v. 切除；删去
解　to remove by erasing or crossing out
例　The doctor excised some scar tissue after the burn was healed. 烧伤痊愈之后，医生切除了一些瘢痕组织。
近　exercise n./v. 练习；运动，锻炼
构　ex (=out) + cis (=to cut) + e

excited
excited［ɪk'saɪtɪd］
adj. 激动的
解　marked by uncontrolled excitement or emotion
例　The office staff was excited about the upcoming new year holidays. 职员对即将到来的新年假期感到兴奋。
同　exciting adj. 令人兴奋的；excitement n. 兴奋，激动

exclaim
exclaim　［ɪkˈskleɪm］
vt. 呼喊；惊叫
例 When interrupted, David exclaimed that he wanted to be left alone. 在被打扰的时候，汤姆大声喊着说自己想要单独待一会儿。
联 exclamation n. 惊呼，感叹

exclaim
exclaim［ɪk'skleɪm］
v. 大喊大叫
解　to utter aloud, often with surprise, horror, or joy
例　The children exclaimed with delight at the sight of the Christmas presents. 看到圣诞礼物，孩子们高兴地欢呼起来。
同　exclamation n. 尖叫

exclude
exclude　［ɪkˈskluːd; ekˈskluːd］
vt. 把…排除在外，排斥（from）〈同 leave...out of〉
例 Excluding grain from your diet will be detrimental to your health. 吃饭时不吃谷物将对你的健康有害。
记 ex（出）+clude（关闭）→关出去→排斥
联 exclusion n. 排除，逐出；exclusive adj. 排他的，单一的

exclusive
exclusive［ɪk'sklu:sɪv］
adj. 单独的，唯一的，排外的〈同 single, sole〉
例　A patent gives inventors exclusive rights to their inventions for a fixed period of time. 专利赋予发明人在特定的时期内对该项发明的独占权。

exclusively
exclusively　［ɪkˈskluːsɪvli］
adv. 完全地，仅仅地〈同 only〉
例 Monopoly refers to the fact that a commercial product or service is exclusively controlled or nearly so. 垄断是指一种产品或服务被独家控制或几乎被独家控制。

excursion
excursion　［ɪkˈskɜːʃən; (US)ɪkˈskɜːrʒən］
n. 远足，游览〈同 trip〉
例 We took an excursion to Alaska on a cruise ship. 我们乘坐游轮去阿拉斯加旅行。
记 ex（出）+curs（跑）+ion→跑出去→远足
联 excurse vi. 远足，短程旅行

excursive
excursive［ɪk'skɜ:sɪv］
adj. 离题的，散漫的
解　 (of e. g. speech and writing) tending to depart from the main point or cover a wide range of subjects
例　Politicians often give excursive answers to sensitive questions that they do not want to answer. 对于不愿回答的敏感问题，政客们总是不作正面回答。

execute
execute　［ˈeksɪkjuːt］
vt. 完成，实施，执行〈同 carry out〉
例 The workers executed the foreman's orders and finished the job quickly. 工人们执行工头的命令，很快就完成了工作。

execution
execution［ˌeksɪ'kju:ʃən］
n. 实施，执行；完成〈同 putting into practice〉
例　The committee is planning carefully for the execution of the project. 委员会仔细地为执行该项计划而进行规划。

executive
executive　［ɪɡˈzekjutɪv］
adj. 行政的〈同 administrative〉
例 In the United States, the President is the executive head of the nation. 在美国，总统是国家的行政首领。
n. 执行者；经理，主管人员
例 The chief executive called a meeting of the company's board of directors. 首席执行官召开了一次公司董事会会议。
记 ex（出来）+ecut（跟随）+ive→跟着命令做出来→执行者

exemplary
exemplary［ɪg'zempləri］
adj. 模范的，典范的；可仿效的〈同　paradigmatic〉
例　The headmaster rewarded Susan for her exemplary performance in school. 校长为苏珊在学校内的模范行为奖励了她。

exemplify
exemplify［ɪg'zemplɪfaɪ］
vt. 例证；作为…的例子〈同 illustrate〉
例　This building exemplifies the architect's dedication and hard work. 这座建筑是建筑师无私奉献和辛苦工作的例证。

exempt
exempt［ɪg'zempt］
vt. 使免除，豁免（from）〈同 immune〉
例　His lame leg exempted him from military service. 他因为瘸腿而被免除兵役。

exert
exert　［ɪɡˈzɜːt］
vt. 运用，行使，施加〈同 apply〉
例 The chairman exerted more influence on the committee than anyone else did. 主席对委员会施加的影响要超过其他任何人。
记 ex（出）+ert（力量）→出力→施加
联 exertion n. 尽力，努力

exhale
exhale［ɪks'heɪl］
vt. 呼出，呼气〈同　breathe out〉
例　Bill inhaled the cigarette smoke and then exhaled deeply. 比尔吸了一口烟，然后大口吐了出来。

exhaust
exhaust　［ɪɡˈzɔːst］
vt. 用尽，耗尽，使精疲力竭〈同 use up〉
例 The long climb to the top of the mountain exhausted our strength. 经过长时间才爬到山顶，我们都精疲力竭。
n. 排气，排气装置
例 Car exhaust fumes are the cause of much pollution. 汽车尾气是造成许多污染的原因。
联 exhausting adj. 用尽的，令人疲乏不堪的；exhaustive adj. 耗尽的，彻底的；exhausted adj. 耗尽的，疲惫的

exhausted
exhausted［ɪg'zɔ:stɪd］
adj. 精疲力竭的〈同　depleted, tired〉
例　The runners were exhausted after the marathon. 运动员们跑完马拉松之后，都已经筋疲力尽。

exhilarating
exhilarating［ɪg'zɪləreɪtɪŋ］
adj. 爽快的，使人愉快的〈同　stimulating〉
例　We came back from an exhilarating walk in the mountains. 我们在山区进行了一次令人愉快的徒步旅行后返回。

exigent
exigent［'eksɪʤənt］
adj. ① 紧急的 ② 苛求的
解　① needing quick action or help ② requiring precise accuracy
例　The driver in the car accident needed exigent medical attention and was driven to a hospital. 遭遇车祸的司机迫切需要医疗护理，随即被开车送往了医院。
构　ex (=out) + ig (=to drive) + ent

exile
exile［'eksaɪl; 'egsaɪl］
vt. 放逐，流放〈同 expel〉
例　The deposed leaders were exiled to a neighboring country. 这几位被罢免的首领被流放到邻国。

exile
exile［'eksaɪl; 'eɡz-］
n./v. 驱逐出，放逐
解　to expel from a country
例　The dictator was overthrown and lived in exile until he died. 独裁者被打倒后，一生过着流亡的生活。

exit
exit［'eksɪt; -zɪt］
v. 出去 n. 出口
解　v. leave, go n. outlet
例　Everyone exited the building when the fire alarm went off. 火警响起的时候，所有人都跑出了大楼。

exodus
exodus［'eksədəs］
n. 大批离去，成群外出
解　a departure of a large number of people or animals
例　The forest fire saw a mass exodus of wildlife leaving the woods. 森林大火使大批野生动物离开了森林。
构　ex (=out) + od < hod (=way) + us

exorbitant
exorbitant［ɪg'zɔ:bɪtənt］
adj.（指价格、索价等）过高的，过分的〈同　expensive, excessive〉
例　Meals at the new restaurant are exorbitant; a simple meal costs seventy-five dollars. 那家新餐馆的饭菜价格太高了；很简单的一顿饭竟然要75美元。

exotic
exotic［ɪg'zɒtɪk］
adj. 异国的，外来的；奇异的〈同 foreign, unusual〉
例　We saw many exotic plants at the flower show; some of them were seen for the first time by the local people. 我们在花展上看到了很多外来植物，有些是本地人第一次看到的。

expand
expand　［ɪkˈspænd］
v. 扩大，膨胀；扩张〈同 dilate〉
例 Heat causes air to expand. 加热会导致空气膨胀。
