expanse
expanse［ɪk'spæns］

例　Pictures of the Moon show vast expanses of crater and rock. 月亮的照片上显示出一望无际的环形山和岩石。

expedition
expedition［ˌekspɪ'dɪʃən］
n. 远征；探险队〈同 journey〉
例　The explorers started on a year-long expedition down the Nile. 探险家们沿尼罗河而下，开始了为期一年的探险。

expel
expel［ɪk'spel］
vt. 驱逐，开除；排出〈同 oust, discharge〉
例　When we exhale we expel air from our lungs. 当我们呼气的时候，肺将空气排出体外。

expend
expend［ɪk'spend］
vt. 花费；用光（精力、时间、体力等）〈同 spend〉
例　He expended thought, work and money on this big project. 这个重要工程使他费尽心思、精力和金钱。

expend
expend［ɪk'spend］
v. 花费；用光
解　to consume; to use up
例　The bad manager expended the company's annual budget in one month. 这个不称职的经理在一个月内就花光了公司一年的预算。

expenditure
expenditure［ɪk'spendɪtʃə(r); ek-］
n. 花费，消耗，支出
解　money paid out; the act of consuming something or spending money for goods or services
例　When they realized the expenditures were greater than the profits, they knew it wasn't worthwhile. 当他们意识到支出要远远超过收益时，他们知道这很不值得。

expensive
expensive［ɪk'spensɪv］
adj. 昂贵的
例　Fresh strawberries are expensive in the winter. 在冬天，新鲜的草莓价格很高。

expertise
expertise［ˌekspɜ:'ti:z］

例　Because of his expertise in analysis, John was hired as a consultant. 由于约翰有分析的专门技术，他被聘为顾问。

expire
expire［ɪk'spaɪə(r)］
vi. ① 期满，到期〈同 end〉
例　My driver's license will expire next month and I have to renew it. 我的驾照下个月就要到期了，我必须更新。
例　Air is expired from the lungs. 空气从肺部排出来。

explicit
explicit［ɪk'splɪsɪt］

例　Your remarks are explicit; no one can misinterpret them. 你的评论很清楚，没人会误解。

explode
explode　［ɪkˈspləʊd］

例 The red balloon exploded when I popped it with a pin. 我用大头针一扎，那个红气球就爆炸了。
联 explosion n. 爆发，爆炸

exploit
exploit　［ɪkˈsplɔɪt］
vt. 开拓；开采，开发〈同 open up〉
例 We need to make sure that we exploit our talents as fully as possible. 我们要保证尽量充分地开发我们的才能。

联 exploitation n. 开发，开采；exploitable adj. 可开发的，可利用的；exploiter n. 剥削者

exploit
exploit［ɪk'splɔɪt］
v. 开发利用；剥削
解　to make use of; to make unfair or selfish use of
例　A mine is exploited for its minerals. 矿山被用来开采矿物。

explore
explore　［ɪkˈsplɔː(r)］
vt. ① 探险，勘探〈同 investigate〉
例 The adventurer explored a dangerous underground cave. 探险家探索了一个危险的地下岩洞。
例 Frank explored several science reports for answers to his homework. 弗兰克仔细查阅了几份科学报告，来寻找家庭作业的答案。
记 ex（出）+plore（流出）→使隐藏的流出来→探险，勘探
联 explorer n. 探险家，探测者；exploration n. 勘察；探究

explosive
explosive　［ɪkˈspləʊsɪv］
adj. 爆炸的；易爆发的
例 Dynamite is highly explosive. 炸药极易爆炸。
n. 炸药
例 The explosives in the car luckily did not explode and everyone was safe. 幸运的是汽车里的爆炸物并未爆炸，所有人都很安全。

exponential
exponential［ˌekspə'nen∫əl］
adj. 指数的，幂数的
例　There has been an exponential increase in world population this century. 全球人口在本世纪出现了指数增长。

expose
expose［ɪk'spəʊz］
v. 曝光；暴露
解　to allow light to act on; to make visible or make known; to reveal
例　His back was badly burnt because he exposed it to the sun for too long. 由于暴露在阳光下的时间太长，他的背部被严重灼伤了。
同　exposure n. 暴露；曝光

exposition
exposition［ˌekspə'zɪʃən］
n. 博览会，展览会〈同 exhibition〉
例　A world's fair with exhibits from many countries is an exposition. 展品来自世界各国的展览称为博览会。

exposition
exposition［ˌekspə'zɪʃən］
n. ① 说明，阐释 ② 博览会
解　① an interpretation of the meaning of sth. ② a collection of things for public display
例　The art exposition in New York displayed some of the world's finest works. 纽约举行的这场艺术展展出了一些世界顶级的作品。

expressive
expressive［ɪk'spresɪv］
adj. 有表现力的，富有表情的，生动的〈同　indicative, demonstrative〉
例　The expressive speech by the President inspired the crowd with patriotic emotions. 总统富有表现力的演讲，激起了人们的爱国情感。

expressly
expressly［ɪk'spresli］

例　These boots are made expressly for rock climbing. 这些靴子是专门为攀岩制作的。

exquisite
exquisite［ɪk'skwɪzɪt］

例　I've just bought an exquisite piece of china. 我刚买了一件精美的瓷器。

extemporaneous
extemporaneous［ɪkˌstempə'reɪnjəs］
adj. ① 即席的，即兴的 ② 临时的，权宜的
解　① carried out or performed with little or no preparation; impromptu ② provided, made, or adapted as an expedient; makeshift
例　He was surprised to have spoken so eloquently in the extemporaneous speech. 他惊讶地发现自己在作即兴演讲时竟然如此地富有表现力。

extemporize
extemporize［ɪk'stempəraɪz］
v. 即兴（发言、创作、演奏或演说）
解　to perform without preparation; provide something roughly for an immediate need
例　He is the kind of speaker who is more effective when he extemporizes than when he reads from a prepared script. 他是那种作即兴演说比照着事先准备好的演说稿念有感染力的演讲者。

extend
extend　［ɪkˈstend］

例　Your script has some excellent ideas, but it will need extensive revision if it is to be used as the class play. 你的剧本中有一些非常棒的点子，但是如果要把它用做班级戏剧的剧本，你还需要作大量的修改。

exterior　［ɪkˈstɪərɪə(r)］

exterminate
exterminate［ɪk'stɜ:mɪneɪt］

external
external　［ɪkˈstɜːnəl; ekˈstɜːnəl］
adj. 外部的；表面的 〈同 exterior〉

external
external［ek'stɜ:nəl］
adj. 外部的

extinct
extinct［ɪk'stɪŋkt］
adj.（动物）灭绝的；（火山）不再活跃的，熄灭的〈同 nonexistent, vanished〉
例　Dinosaurs may have become extinct when a meteor struck Earth. 恐龙可能在陨石撞击地球的时候灭绝了。

extinguish
extinguish［ɪk'stɪŋgwɪʃ］
vt. 熄灭；消灭，压制〈同 put out, destroy〉
例　Water extinguished the fire. 水浇灭了火。
例　Vanilla extract is a common ingredient in candies. 香草提取物是糖果的常用配料。
例　The doctor extracted the snake's poison from the bite. 医生把蛇毒从蛇咬的伤口处吸了出来。

extol
extol［ɪk'stəʊl］
vt. 赞美〈同　praise, exalt〉
例　They wrote a song to extol their dead leader. 他们写了一首歌，来赞颂逝去的领袖。

extort
extort［ɪk'stɔ:t］
v. 勒索，强索

例　Blackmailers try to extort money from their victims. 勒索者试图从受害者手中强索钱财。
同　extortionist n. 敲诈勒索者

extract
extract［ɪk'strækt］
v. 提炼；拔出；提取

例　The dentist extracted all four of her wisdom teeth. 牙医把她的四颗智齿全拔掉了。
同　extraction n. 血统；拔出，提取

extradition
extradition［ˌekstrə'dɪʃən］
n. 引渡逃犯
解　surrender of a fugitive or prisoner by one state, nation, or authority to another
例　The lawyers opposed the extradition of their client on the grounds that for more than five years he had been a model citizen. 律师反对引渡其委托人，理由是五年多以来他一直是模范公民。

extravagant
extravagant［ɪk'strævəgənt］

例　His extravagant buying habits will have to stop. 他花钱大手大脚的习惯得改掉。

extremity
extremity［ɪks'treməti］

例　Alaska is the northern extremity of the United States. 阿拉斯加是美国的最北端。

extricate
extricate［'ekstrɪkeɪt］
v. 拯救，救出
解　to set free from entanglements, difficulties, embarrassing situations, etc.; to release
例　Jim tried to extricate himself from the heated argument by saying he had to go to the bathroom. 为了从激烈的争吵中脱身，吉姆借口说要去趟卫生间。

exuberant
exuberant［ɪg'zju:bərənt; (US)-zu:-］
adj. ①充满活力的〈同　high-spirited, lively〉
例　His speeches were famous for his exuberant language and vivid imagery. 他的演讲以充满活力的语言和生动的比喻而著名。
例　The path was blocked by the exuberant growth of wild blackberry bushes. 这条路被茂盛的野生黑莓灌木丛挡住了。

eyewitness
eyewitness［'aɪwɪtnəs］
n. 目击者〈同　witness〉
例　The police protected the eyewitness of the murder in case there were any attempts on her life. 警方对凶杀案的目击证人进行了保护，以免出现任何威胁她生命的情况。

fable
fable［'feɪbəl］
n. 寓言，神话〈同 tale, myth〉
例　My favorite fable is the one about the tortoise and the hare. 我最喜欢的一个寓言是关于乌龟和兔子的。

fabric
fabric　［ˈfæbrɪk］
n. ① 织物，布〈同 cloth〉
例 The sofa is covered with a soft cotton fabric. 沙发上盖着一块柔软的棉布。
例 It is necessary to protect the fabric of civilized society. 保护文明社会的结构是非常有必要的。

fabricate
fabricate［'fæbrɪkeɪt］
vt. ① 制作，构成〈同 make, assemble〉
例　Automobiles are fabricated from parts made in different factories. 汽车由不同工厂生产出来的配件组装而成。
例　The clerk fabricated an excuse to avoid questioning. 这个职员编造了一个理由，以免被质询。

facade
facade［fə'sɑ:d］
n. 正面，表面〈同　face; appearance〉
例　Our bedroom window is on the southern facade of the building, enabling us to enjoy plenty of sunshine. 我们卧室的窗户在楼的南面，这样我们享受到充足的阳光。

facade
facade［fə'sɑ:d］
n. 建筑物的正面，外表
解　the face or front of a building
例　The facade of the church had often been photographed by tourists because it was more interesting than the rear. 游客经常对教堂的正面拍照，因为它比背面更有意思。

facet
facet［'fæsɪt］
n. 面；（问题等的）方面〈同 side, aspect〉
例　The problem that we face now has many legal and financial facets. 我们现在面临的问题有很多法律和金融方面的问题。

facetious
facetious［fə'si:ʃəs］
adj. 轻浮的，好开玩笑的
解　cleverly amusing in tone, joking inappropriately
例　Your facetious remarks are not appropriate at this serious moment. 在这个严肃的时刻，你的诙谐言论不合时宜。

例　Modern technology has facilitated the production process. 现代科技促进了生产力的发展。

例　After their leader died, the members broke up into factions. 领导人死后，成员们分裂成了许多派系。

adj. 事实的，实际的〈同　real, actual〉

genealogy［ˌʤi:nɪ'æləʤi］
n. 家谱；族谱学
解　successive generations of kin
例　The family owned a book that recorded the genealogy of their ancestry. 这个家庭有一本记载祖先家谱的小册子。

联 generative adj. 有生殖力的；regenerate adj. 新生的 v.（使）再生

generator［'ʤenəreɪtə(r)］
n. 发电机
解　a machine that changes mechanical energy into electrical energy and produces either direct or alternating current
例　Our family bought a power generator for our house so that when a rainstorm cuts off our electricity next time, we can go along as though nothing had happened. 我们家买了一台发电机，这样当下次因风暴而断电的时候，我们就可以照常生活，不受任何影响。
近　progenitor n. 祖先，始祖

grind　［ɡraɪnd］
vt. 磨碎，碾碎 〈同 crush〉
例 Because the diamond is the hardest naturally occurring substance, it is used in industry for cutting, grinding, and boring other hard materials. 由于钻石是天然生成的最坚硬的物质，因此在工业上常用来对其他坚硬材料进行切割、磨削和钻孔。

例　The wounded men groaned in agony as the stretcher-bearers tried to move them. 抬担架的人试着去挪动伤员时，伤员们发出了痛苦的呻吟。

hypothesis

imitate　［ˈɪmɪteɪt］
vt. 仿效，模仿〈同 mimic，emulate〉
例 Decide what you want to do; don't just imitate others. 决定自己想要做什么，不要一味地模仿其他人。
联 imitation n. 模仿；仿制品

imitate
imitate［'ɪmɪteɪt］
vt. 模仿；仿效
解　to try to be like or act like; to follow the example of
例　I hate it when she imitates my actions. 我讨厌她模仿我的动作。

imitation
imitation［ˌɪmɪ'teɪʃən］
n. 模仿；仿制品〈同 mimicry, copy〉
例　In imitation of older girls, the ten-year-old girls have started wearing make-up. 为了模仿大姑娘，这些十岁的小女孩们已经开始化妆了。

immemorial
immemorial［ˌɪmɪ'mɔ:rɪəl］
adj. 太古的，极古的
解　long past; beyond the limits of memory or tradition or recorded history
例　The archeologist found the fossils of a three-headed creature that had been buried from time immemorial. 考古学家发现了一种三头生物的化石，它在远古时期就被埋葬了。

immense
immense　［ɪˈmens］
adj. 巨大的；无边的〈同 enormous〉
例 The square is dominated by an immense statue of the President. 一尊巨大的总统雕像屹立在广场上。
记 im（不）+mense（=measure 测量）→大得无法测量的→巨大的
联 immensity n. 无限；巨大

immerse
immerse［ɪ'mɜ:s］
vt. 浸入；使全神贯注于，使沉浸于〈同 submerge, engross〉
例　The hippopotamus immersed itself in the cool river. 河马把身体浸在凉爽的河水中。

immerse
immerse［ɪ'mɜ:s］
v. ① 浸入 ② 沉浸于
解　① to enclose or envelop completely, as if by swallowing ② to absorb deeply, to engross
例　The student immersed himself in research in order to complete his thesis. 为了完成论文，这名学生沉浸在了研究中。
同　immersion n. 沉入，浸入
构　im < in (=into) + mers < merg (=to dip, to sink) + e

immigrant
immigrant　［ˈɪmɪɡrənt］
n.（自外国移入之）移民〈同 alien〉
例 Illegal immigrants are sent back across the border if they are caught. 非法移民如果被抓住，会被从边境遣送回国。

imminent
imminent［'ɪmɪnənt］
adj. 即将发生的，逼近的
解　close in time, about to occur
例　When the outbreak of the war seemed imminent, the tourists rushed home. 战争似乎一触即发，游客们都纷纷回家。
构　im < in (=upon, over) + min (=to project) + ent

immobile
immobile［ɪ'məʊbaɪl; (US)ɪ'məʊbəl］
adj. 固定的，不动的〈同　stationary, fixed〉
例　Nothing in nature is truly immobile; even the mountains are in constant movement and change. 本质上而言，没有任何物体是绝对静止不动的；即便山脉也在持续地移动和变化。

immune
immune［ɪ'mju:n］
adj.（对…）免疫的，不受影响的〈同 exempt〉
例　This vaccine will make you immune to this disease for two years. 接种这种疫苗可使你对这种疾病有两年的免疫力。

impact
impact　［ˈɪmpækt］
n. ① 影响〈同 influence〉
例 Your lectures have had a powerful impact on my thinking. 您的课对我的思想产生了重要的影响。
例 The car crumpled upon impact against the solid brick wall. 那辆汽车撞上硬砖墙后变得不成样子了。
记 im（起强调作用）+pact（压）→使劲压→撞击，冲击

impair
impair［ɪm'peə(r)］
vt. 损害，削弱〈同 hurt〉
例　His misdeeds greatly impaired our friendship. 他的罪行严重伤害了我们的友谊。

impart
impart［ɪm'pɑ:t］
vt. 给予，传授；传递，传达〈同 deliver, convey〉
例　Schools impart education. 学校提供教育。

impart
impart［ɪm'pɑ:t］
v. 告知；透露
解　to make known; to disclose
例　The teacher imparted some final advice to the students at their graduation. 在学生们毕业之际，老师给了他们一些最后的忠告。
近　parlance n. 谈话，说法；pariah n. 贱民；被社会遗弃者

impartial
impartial［ɪm'pɑ:∫əl］
adj. 公正的，无偏见的〈同　unbiased, fair〉
例　A judge has the responsibility of being impartial if he is to give a fair decision on a case. 如果一名法官要对一个案件进行公平的判决，他便有责任做到公平公正。

impartial
impartial［ɪm'pɑ:ʃəl］
adj. 公平的，无私的
解　showing no more favor to one side than to the other; fair; just
例　A judge should be impartial. 法官应该公正无私。
同　impartiality n. 公正，客观；无私
构　im < in (=not) + part (=part) + ial

impassable
impassable［ɪm'pɑ:səbəl］
adj. 不能通行的，无路可通的
解　impossible to pass, cross, or overcome
例　The Great Wall made the hills almost impassable for any army. 长城使得任何军队几乎都无法进入山里。

impasse
impasse［'æmpɑ:s; 'ɪm-］
n. ① 死路 ② 僵局
解　① a road or passage having no exit ② a situation that is so difficult that no progress can be made
例　The jury members reached an impasse and couldn't unanimously agree on the verdict. 陪审团成员间陷入僵局，无法对裁决达成一致意见。

impassioned
impassioned［ɪm'pæʃənd］
adj. 充满激情的
解　characterized by intense emotion
例　Charlie gave an impassioned performance that earned him a standing ovation at the end of the play. 在演出的尾声，查理充满激情的表演赢得了观众的喝彩。

impassive
impassive［ɪm'pæsɪv］
adj. 无动于衷的，冷漠的
解　having or revealing little emotion or sensibility
例　It's not that he doesn't care about what you said. It's just his impassive personality. 他并不是不在乎你所说的话；他只是性格比较冷淡。
构　im < in (=not) + pass (=to feel, to suffer) + ive

impede
impede［ɪm'pi:d］
vt. 妨碍，阻碍〈同　hinder, hamper〉
例　The scheme was impeded by lack of funds. 由于缺乏资金，计划受到了阻碍。

impending
impending［ɪm'pendɪŋ］
adj. 行将发生的，逼近的〈同　approaching, imminent〉
例　People out at sea had been warned of the impending storms. 海上的人们已经收到了暴风雨即将来临的警告。

imperative
imperative［ɪm'perətɪv］
adj. 必要的；强制的〈同 necessary〉
例　Mutual respect and understanding among all racial and ethnic groups have become imperative in the life of this nation. 所有种族和民族之间互相尊重、互相理解已经成为这个国家生存的必需因素。
n. 命令；需要；必要的事〈同 command, order〉
例　It is an imperative that you take calculus before you start to study advanced economics. 在你学习高级经济学之前，你需要学习微积分。

imperial
imperial［ɪm'pɪərɪəl］
adj. 帝王的；威严的，至高无上的〈同 royal〉
例　The palace was decorated with imperial splendor. 宫殿装修得很有皇室风范。

impersonal
impersonal［ɪm'pɜ:sənəl］

例　He conceals his feelings behind a rather impersonal manner. 他用一种冷漠的态度掩盖自己的感情。

impersonate
impersonate［ɪm'pɜ:səneɪt］

例　My cousin impersonates many well-known film stars. 我堂弟能模仿许多著名的电影明星。

impetus

例　Janet's longing for another kind of life is a major impetus for working hard. 珍妮特对另外一种生活的渴望成为了她努力工作的主要动力。

implacable
implacable［ɪm'plækəbəl］
adj. 难以抚慰的，难平息的；难以满足的
解　unable to be appeased; refusing to be reconciled
例　The new nation was constantly threatened by its implacable enemies. 由于敌人很难和解，这个新成立的国家一直处于其带来的威胁之中。

近　impeccable adj. 无缺点的；无瑕疵的

implement
implement
例 In your training course for dental assistant, you will become familiar with many of the implements that dentists use. 在牙科助理的培训课程中，你会熟悉牙科医生所用的许多工具。
例 I am unwilling to implement this plan until I have assurances that it has the full approval of officials. 我不愿意执行这个计划，除非我确信这个计划已经得到官方的完全批准。

implication

例　She did not actually refuse, but the way that she frowned was an implication of her unwillingness. 她实际上并没有拒绝，但她皱眉头暗示了她的不情愿。
例　This guy is suspected of implication in a number of robberies. 那个家伙被怀疑参与了数起抢劫。

implicit
implicit［ɪm'plɪsɪt］

例　My boss's surly facial expression was an implicit message that we did something wrong. 老板阴沉沉的表情暗示着我们犯了错误。

impose
impose　［ɪmˈpəʊz］

impose
impose［ɪm'pəʊz］

例　President Bush was highly criticized for imposing new taxes after his election campaign. 在竞选活动之后，人们强烈谴责布什总统征收新税。

imposing

例　The pyramids of Egypt are imposing structures. 埃及的金字塔是非常雄伟的建筑。
例　The grandeur of the Great Wall left an imprint upon me. 长城的宏伟令我印象深刻。
例　The accident imprinted the fear of death on his mind. 这次事故在他的心中留下了对死亡的恐惧。

impress

impress

impulse

例　She was so hot that she had the impulse to jump into the pool even with her clothes on. 她实在是太热了，有一股不脱衣服就想跳到池塘里的冲动。

inanimate

例　A fable is usually a short tale featuring animals or inanimate objects that can talk and think like humans. 寓言通常是一则短小的故事，其中的主角是能够像人一样说话和思考的动物或没有生命的物体。

incense

例　The waitress was incensed when her picky customer refused to tip her. 当那位挑剔的顾客拒绝付小费的时候，那名女服务员被激怒了。

incisive

incompatible

例　Any new video system that is incompatible with existing ones has little chance of success. 对于任何与现有系统不兼容的新视频系统，其成功的机会都微乎其微。

incredible

例 On stage Aretha Franklin sings with incredible energy, zest, and strength. 艾瑞莎•富兰克林在舞台上唱歌时，充满了惊人的能量、热情和力量。

incriminate
incriminate［ɪn'krɪmɪneɪt］
v. 归罪于，控告；牵连
解　to accuse of a crime; to show to be guilty
例　The robber's confession incriminated two others who helped to rob the bank. 盗贼的供词牵连出了其他两名协助抢劫银行的同伙。
同　incrimination n. 连累，控告
构　in + crimin (=guilty) + ate

incur
incur［ɪn'kɜ:(r)］
vt. 招致，引起〈同 cause〉
例　Janet incurred her boyfriend's anger for telling a lie. 珍妮特因为说谎而惹怒了男朋友。

例　The incursion of the foreign army on the island was an act of war. 外国军队侵入岛屿是一种战争行为。

indifferent　［ɪnˈdɪfrənt］

infection

联 inspiring adj. 使人振奋的，鼓舞的；inspiration n. 灵感

例　The leather lash cut the side of the horse. 皮鞭把马的身体一侧抽开了一道口子。
v. 抽打，鞭打〈同　strike, hit〉
例　The rider lashes the horse to make it go faster. 骑手用皮鞭抽打马，好让它跑得更快。

lasting
lasting　［ˈlɑːstɪŋ］
adj. 持久的；永恒的；耐用的〈同 forever; enduring〉
例 Kennedy left a lasting impression on the people who heard his inaugural address. 肯尼迪给那些听过他就职演说的人们留下了不可磨灭的印象。

latent
latent［'leɪtənt］
adj. 潜伏的，隐藏的〈同 dormant〉
例　Some people believe that telepathy is a latent power of the mind. 有的人认为心灵感应是思维的潜在能力。

lateral
lateral［'lætərəl］
adj. 侧面的，旁边的
例　In order to get good plant growth, the gardener must pinch off all lateral shoots. 为了让植物更好地生长，园艺师必须修剪掉所有侧枝。

latitude
latitude［'lætɪtju:d; (US)'lætɪtu:d］
n. ① 纬度，范围〈同 scope〉
例　The average annual solar radiation received by the atmosphere varies strongly with latitude. 一年当中大气层吸收的太阳辐射平均量随着纬度的不同而表现出明显的差异。
例　The teacher gave her students a lot of latitude in choosing their science projects. 老师给予学生足够的自由来选择科学课题。

launch
launch　［lɔːntʃ］
vt. 发动〈同 begin〉
例 When he was stopped, the old man launched a verbal attack at the policeman. 那个老人被拦住以后，便开始对警察破口大骂。
n./v. 发射，(使）升空〈同 send off〉
例 The satellite was launched into orbit. 卫星被发射到运行轨道。

laundry
laundry　［ˈlɔːndri］
n. 洗衣店；待洗的衣服〈同 washing〉
例 I placed the clean laundry on the table and started folding it. 我把干净衣服放到桌子上，然后开始叠衣服。

laurels［'lɒrəlz］

例　Don't rest on your laurels: follow up your success and start looking for new markets now. 不要不思进取：借着成功的东风，马上开始寻找新市场。

lava［'lɑ:və］

例　The lava flowed down the volcano and burned many houses down. 岩浆流下火山，烧毁了许多房屋。

例　She gives lavish parties with wonderful food, flowers, and music. 她经常举办奢华的聚会，聚会上有精美的食物、鲜花和音乐。

lawsuit［'lɔ:sju:t］
n. 诉讼〈同　litigation, case〉
例　The attorney was representing clients in five lawsuits this week. 本周，这位律师代理了五起诉讼的委托人。

lax
lax［læks］

解　careless; not strict or tense
例　The lax teacher wore casual clothes and called his students by their first names. 这位散漫的老师穿衣服很随意，连上课点名也只叫学生的姓。

laxative［'læksətɪv］

解　n. something causing the bowels to empty easily adj. causing looseness or relaxation, especially of the bowels
例　The doctor recommended he take laxatives for his constipation. 医生建议他服用泻药来治疗便秘。

layer　［ˈleɪə(r)］

例 There was a thin layer of oil on the surface of the water. 在水面上有薄薄的一层油。

例　The informer leaked the secret to the press. 告密者把这个秘密泄露给了媒体。

lease
lease　［liːs］

vt. 出租，租借〈同 rent〉
例 We have leased an apartment for one year. 我们出租了一套公寓，租期为一年。
记 分割记忆：l+ease（安心）→有了租约才安心→租约

例　The legendary deeds of Sherlock Holmes are so well-known that many people think he really lived. 夏洛克·福尔摩斯的传奇故事可谓无人不知，以至于许多人都认为他是真实存在的。

例　Her handwriting is so bad that it is barely legible. 她的书法太糟糕了，几乎无法辨认。

legislation

例 The government mandates that the states are to comply with federal legislation. 政府规定，各州应遵守联邦法律。

legislation
legislation［leʤɪs'leɪʃən］

例　The president's power to veto is a control over the legislation passed by Congress. 总统的否决权是对国会通过立法的一种控制。

例　Enter the new information in the log. 在日志里填入新的信息。

logic［'lɒʤɪk］
n. ① 逻辑学 ② 逻辑
解　① the branch of philosophy that analyzes inference ② reasoned and reasonable judgment
例　His argument had no logic and he was quickly proven wrong. 他的论据没有逻辑，很快就被证明是错误的。

logical
logical　［ˈlɒʤɪkəl］
adj. 合乎逻辑的；合理的〈同 coherent〉
例 An upset stomach is a logical result of overeating. 胃不舒服是暴饮暴食的必然结果。
联 logic n. 逻辑，逻辑学

logical
logical［'lɒʤɪkəl］
adj. （指行为、事情等）合乎情理的，合乎常理的
解　in accordance with the rules of logic; able to reason correctly
例　There are times in life when you should be guided more by your feelings, without trying to be strictly logical about everything. 人生有的时候更需要跟着自己的感觉走，而不用事事都合乎常理。
同　illogically adv. 不合逻辑地
构　log (=speech) + ical

margin
margin　［ˈmɑːʤɪn］
n. ① 边缘〈同 edge〉
例 Miss Bao always writes her corrections in the margins of her students' papers. 鲍老师总是在学生试卷的空白处写上她做的修改。
例 We allow a margin of 15 minutes in catching a train. 我们只剩15分钟来赶火车。
联 marginal adj. 记在页边的；边缘的

marine
marine　［məˈriːn］
adj. 海的；航海的；海产的〈同 sea-dwelling; maritime〉
例 Whales and dolphins are marine mammals. 鲸和海豚都是海洋哺乳动物。
记 mar（海）+ine→海的
联 mariner n. 水手

maritime
maritime［'mærɪtaɪm］
adj. 海上的，海事的〈同　marine, oceanic〉
例　The fishermen lived in a maritime village. 渔民们住在一个海边的村子里。

marsh
marsh［mɑ:ʃ］
n. 湿地，沼泽〈同 swamp〉
例　A marsh is a critical component of wildlife habitat. 湿地是野生动物栖息地的重要组成部分。

marshal
marshal［'mɑ:ʃəl］
v. 排列；整理，汇集〈同 arrange, collect〉
例　The statistician marshaled his facts before making his presentation. 统计学家先把论据整理好，然后开始做陈述。
n. 元帅，最高指挥官
例　Marshal of the Royal Air Force is the highest rank in the British Air Force. 皇家空军的元帅是英国空军里最高的军衔。

marvelous
marvelous　［ˈmɑːvələs］
adj. 不可思议的；了不起的〈同 wonderful〉
例 The weather was marvelous for an afternoon walk in the park. 天气非常适合下午去公园散步。

masculine
masculine［'mæskjʊlɪn］
adj. 男性的；男子气概的〈同 manly〉
例　In some languages, there are masculine pronouns and feminine pronouns. 在有些语言里，有阳性代词和阴性代词之分。

mason
mason［'meɪsən］
n. 泥瓦匠〈同　bricklayer〉
例　The number of masons who once worked on the Great Wall was countless. 曾经在长城上干活的泥瓦匠数不胜数。

massive
massive　［ˈmæsɪv］
adj. 大而重的，庞大的；可观的〈同 enormous, colossal〉
例 If the drought continues, deaths will occur on a massive scale. 如果干旱继续，将会发生大规模死亡。
记 mass（体积）+ive→体积大的→巨大的

masterpiece
masterpiece［'mɑ:stəpi:s］
n. 杰作，名著〈同 great work〉
例　The novelist's lifelong dream was to write a masterpiece. 这位小说家一生的梦想是创作一部经典作品。

match
match　［mætʃ］
n. 相配的人（或物)
例 We talked about their love and hopes, and we all agreed that it was a good match. 我们谈论了他们的爱与希望，大家都认为他们俩很相配。
v.（使）匹配〈同 go well together〉
例 I've been unable to match this coat with any of my dresses. 我一直没法把这件外套与我的其他裙子进行搭配。
联 matching adj.（尤指颜色或外表）相配的，一致的；matchless adj. 无敌的；无比的

mate
mate　［meɪt］
v.（使）结伴，（使）成配偶〈同 breed〉
例 The zoo bought a new male gorilla to mate with the female one. 动物园新买了一只雄性大猩猩，与雌性大猩猩配成一对。
n. 配偶〈同 spouse〉
例 A male goose has only one mate until he dies. 公鹅一生只有一个伴侣。
联 mateless adj. 无配偶的，无伴的

materialism
materialism［mə'tɪərɪəlɪzəm］
n. 实利主义，物质主义；唯物主义
例　Materialism had become such a part of her life that she was always talking about what she was planning to buy next. 物质主义已经成为她生活的一部分，她总是谈论自己接下来计划买什么。

mature
mature　［məˈtjʊə（r); (US)məˈtʊər］
adj.（智力或体力）成熟的
例 Young girls are often more mature than young boys. 小女孩通常比小男孩更成熟。
记 mat（成熟）+ure→成熟的
联 maturity n. 成熟；immature adj. 不成熟的，未完全发展的；premature adj. 早熟的

maverick
maverick［'mævərɪk］
adj. 独行的；不遵守传统的〈同　independent〉
例　The maverick pilot would not obey orders and was expelled from the Air Force. 那名特立独行的飞行员不遵守命令，被开除出空军。
n. 持异议者，自行其是者〈同　nonconformist〉
例　That scientist is a maverick who doesn't care about what others think. 那名科学家是个自行其是的人，根本不关心别人怎么想。

maximal
maximal［'mæksɪməl］
adj. 最大的
解　of, relating to, or consisting of a maximum; being the greatest or highest possible
例　The coach required his players to exert their maximal effort during the game otherwise they would be substituted. 教练要求运动员在比赛时全力以赴，否则他们就会被替换下来。

maximum
maximum　［ˈmæksɪməm］
n./adj. 最大量（的），最大限度（的)〈同 greatest〉
例 The maximum amount of time I can give you is 2 weeks. 我最多能给你两周时间。

meadow
meadow［'medəʊ］
n. 草地，牧场〈同 grassland〉
例　The meadows are covered with wildflowers at this time of year. 每年的这个时候，草地上都长满了野花。

meager
meager［'mi:gə(r)］
adj. 缺乏的，不足的〈同　scanty, poor〉
例　Without a job, he could only afford meager dinners. 没有工作，他只能负担得起寒酸的晚餐。

mean
mean　［miːn］
adj. ① 卑鄙的；吝啬的〈同 not generous〉
例 She's very mean and never shares her sweets. 她非常小气，从不跟其他人分享她的糖果。
例 Six is the mean number between three and nine. 六是三和九的平均数。

meaningful
meaningful［'mi:nɪŋfʊl］
adj. 意味深长的〈同　significant, important〉
例　His hours of study before the exam were meaningful and he got a high score. 他在考试之前几个小时的学习非常有意义，他考试得到了高分。

means
means［mi:nz］
n. 手段，方法〈同 methods〉
例　He used unfair means to get through the examination. 他用不公平的手段通过了考试。

mechanism
mechanism　［ˈmekənɪzəm］
n. 机械（装置）；机理; 运作机制〈同 device〉
例 An automobile engine is a complicated mechanism. 汽车引擎是一种非常复杂的机械装置。
记 mechan（机械）+ism→机械（装置）
联 mechanics n. 机械学，力学；mechanize v. 机械化；mechanical adj. 机械的

medal
medal［'medəl］
n. 奖章，勋章，纪念章〈同 award〉
例　The swimmer received two bronze medals at the Olympics. 在奥运会上，这位游泳选手获得了两块铜牌。

media
media　［ˈmiːdɪə］
n. 媒体
例 The media are interested in focusing on controversial matters. 媒体有兴趣关注争议性事件。

mediate
mediate［'mi:dɪeɪt］
v. 斡旋，调停，调解〈同 arbitrate〉
例　He mediated in the family dispute. 他调解家庭纠纷。

medieval
medieval［ˌmedɪ'i:vəl; (US)ˌmi:d'i:vəl］
adj. 中世纪的
例　Castles were a common sight in medieval times. 城堡在中世纪很常见。

medium
medium　［ˈmiːdɪəm］
n. 媒体；媒介；方法〈同 way〉
例 Television is an important medium for advertising. 电视是一种重要的广告媒介。

mellifluous
mellifluous［mə'lɪflʊəs］
adj. （声音、音乐等）流畅的，甜美的
解　sweetly or smoothly flowing
例　The poet always attracted a large audience to her public readings not really because of the quality of her poetry, but because of her mellifluous voice. 这位诗人总是能吸引大量的观众去参加她的公开读书会，这不是因为她的诗歌质量很高，而是因为她的嗓音甜美。

melodious
melodious［mɪ'ləʊdɪəs］
adj. 旋律优美的，悦耳的〈同　harmonious, euphonic〉
例　I sang a melodious lullaby to my baby. 我给宝宝唱了一首旋律优美的摇篮曲。

melodrama
melodrama［'melədrɑ:mə］
n. 音乐剧；情节剧
例　Their house is like a melodrama; there is always an interesting crisis happening. 他们的房子就像一出情节剧一样；经常会发生有趣的危机。

melody
melody［'melədi］
n. 旋律，曲调〈同 tune〉
例　Ellington was a composer concerned not only with melody, but with harmony, rhythm and instrumentation too. 埃林顿是一个作曲家，他不仅注重曲调，而且注重协调性、旋律和乐器。

membrane
membrane［'membreɪn］
n. 膜，薄膜
例　Our body's vital organs are covered and protected by special membranes. 人身体中的重要器官有特殊的膜覆盖和保护。

memorable
memorable［'memərəbəl］
adj. 值得记住的
解　worth remembering; not to be forgotten; notable
例　Chuck's 21st birthday party with all his friends and relatives was a memorable occasion for all. 查克的21岁生日派对和他所有的亲朋好友一起度过，对大家来说都很难忘。

memorandum
memorandum［ˌmemə'rændəm］
n. 备忘录，便笺〈同 memo〉
例　Make a memorandum of the things we'll need for the trip. 把我们旅行需要准备的东西写张条儿吧。

memorial
memorial　［məˈmɔːrɪəl］
n. 纪念物〈同 monument〉
例 Mary has a rose garden as a memorial to her dead child. 玛丽有一座玫瑰花园，作为对她死去孩子的纪念。
adj. 用以纪念的
例 Hundreds of friends and former students came to Professor Conner's memorial activities. 数百位好友和从前的学生都来参加康纳教授的纪念活动。
联 memorialize v. 纪念

memorial
memorial［mə'mɔ:rɪəl］
n. 纪念物；纪念碑 adj. 纪念性的
解　n. a structure erected to commemorate persons or events adj. helping people to remember some person, thing, or event
例　The memorial service was naturally a sad occasion, but the people tried to remember the good times they had with their deceased friend. 追悼会本该是一个悲伤的场合，但是人们总是努力回忆和已故的朋友在一起的开心时刻。

menace
menace［'menəs］
n. 危险物〈同 danger〉
例　The Third World War would be a menace to world peace. 若有第三次世界大战，那将会威胁世界和平。
vt. 威吓；胁迫〈同 threaten〉
例　The school bully menaced many of the students. 这个学校恶霸威胁过很多学生。

mend
mend［mend］
vt. 修补；改进〈同 repair, improve〉
例　He asked his mother to mend the hole in the pocket of his jeans. 他让母亲为他缝补好牛仔裤口袋上的破洞。

mental
mental［'mentəl］
adj. 精神的；智力的〈同 cerebral, intellectual〉
例　His mental development is ahead of most other children's in his class. 他的智力发展要比班级里的大多数孩子超前。

mentor
mentor［'mentɔ:(r); 'mentə(r)］
n. 导师
解　teacher
例　Doug learned from his mentor both professional skills and personal ethics, two values needed to succeed in life. 道格从他的导师那里学到了专业技能和个人道德，这正是成功的人生所需要的两种价值观念。
近　menthol n. 薄荷醇

mercantile
mercantile［'mɜ:kəntaɪl］
adj. 贸易的，商业的
解　of or relating to or characteristic of trade or traders
例　Silk Street is the best place to find cheap mercantile goods. 秀水街是找到便宜商品的最佳去处。

mercenary
mercenary［'mɜ:sɪnəri］
adj. 唯利是图的 n. 雇佣兵
解　working only for money or other reward; inspired by love of money n. a person hired to fight in another country merely for wages
例　Mercenaries do not normally have any sense of loyalty; their only incentive is money. 雇佣兵通常都没有忠诚感；钱是他们唯一的动机。

merchandise
merchandise［'mɜ:tʃəndaɪs; 'mɜ:tʃəndaɪz］
n. 商品〈同 goods〉
例　There was a sale on all merchandise in the store. 这个商店里的所有商品都在大减价。

merchandise
merchandise［'mɜ:tʃəndaɪs］
n. 商品；货品
解　commodities offered for sale
例　The newspaper advertisement pictured the merchandise that was on sale. 报纸广告刊登了廉价出售的商品的图片。

merchant
merchant　［ˈmɜːtʃənt］
n. 商人
例 They worked illegally as arms merchants. 他们从事非法倒卖军火的生意。
联 mercantile adj. 商业的，贸易的；merchandise n. 商品，货物

merchant
merchant［'mɜ:tʃənt］
n. 商人
解　a businessperson engaged in retail trade
例　The merchant sold fruit and vegetables from a portable cart on the street. 商人在停靠街边的轻便货车上售卖水果和蔬菜。

mercury
mercury　［ˈmɜːkjʊri］
n. ① 水银
例 Mercury is an element, and its symbol is Hg. 汞是一种元素，它的符号是Hg。
例 Mercury revolves around the sun once every 88 days. 水星每88天围绕太阳转一圈。
记 Mercury n.【罗马神话】墨丘利（众神的信使）

merge
merge［mɜ:ʤ］
v.（使）合并，（使）融合〈同 combine, unite〉
例　The corporation merged two of its divisions. 这个公司合并了两个部门。

merit
merit　［ˈmerɪt］
n. 优点，价值〈同 virtue〉
例 This film is entertaining but has little artistic merit. 这部电影非常有趣，但没多少艺术价值。

mesmerize

vt. 施催眠术；使入迷，迷住〈同　hypnotize; fascinate〉
例　The exciting move mesmerized everyone in the theater. 这一激动人心的举动令剧院内的所有人陶醉。

mess

messenger
messenger［'mesɪnʤə(r)］

例　In big cities bicycle messengers deliver packages between office buildings. 在大城市，骑自行车的快递员在一座一座的办公大楼之间投递包裹。

metabolism
metabolism［me'tæbəlɪzəm］
n. 新陈代谢
例　He had such a high metabolism that he would eat and eat but not gain any weight. 他有极高的新陈代谢能力，因此他可以不停地吃，却不会增重。

metaphor
metaphor［'metəfə(r)］
n. 隐喻，暗喻〈同　parable〉
例　“He soared like an eagle”is an example of a simile;“He is an eagle in flight”is a metaphor.“他像鹰一样翱翔”是明喻的例子；“他是一只翱翔的雄鹰”则是暗喻。

metaphysics
metaphysics［ˌmetə'fɪzɪks］
n. 形而上学，玄学
解　branch of philosophy dealing with the nature of existence, truth, and know-ledge
例　Metaphysics is the branch of philosophy that examines the nature of reality, including the relationship between mind and matter, substance and attribute, fact and value. 形而上学是哲学的分支，主要研究现实的本质，包括意识和物质、物质和属性以及事实和价值之间的关系。

meteor
meteor［'mi:tɪə(r)］
n. 流星
例　Most meteors burn up when they enter the Earth's atmosphere. 大多数流星在进入地球大气层后都会被燃烧殆尽。

meteorology
meteorology［ˌmi:tjə'rɒləʤi］
n. 气象学
解　science dealing with phenomena of the atmosphere, especially weather processes and weather forecasting
例　The weatherman based his daily forecasts on calculated meteorology rather than lucky guesses. 气象员依靠经过测算的气象数据进行每日预报，而不是依靠侥幸猜测。

methodology
methodology［ˌmeθə'dɒləʤi］
n. 方法论，方法学
例　The scientist was well-known for his creative methodology in laboratory experiments. 这位科学家以其在实验室实验方面的创造性方法而闻名．

meticulous
meticulous［mə'tɪkjʊləs］
adj. 一丝不苟的，过细的〈同　scrupulous, factidious〉
例　She was meticulous when she cleaned her room and left nothing dirty. 她在打扫自己房间的时候非常细致，不留下任何脏东西。

metric
metric　［ˈmetrɪk］
adj. 米制的，公制的
例 A yard is about 1 meter in the metric system. 一码大约相当于公制的一米。

metropolitan
metropolitan［ˌmetrə'pɒlɪtən］
adj. 主要都市的，大城市的〈同 large city〉
例　Vermont has the lowest percentage of metropolitan residents of any state in the United States. 佛蒙特州是美国城市人口比例最低的一个州。

microbe
microbe［'maɪkrəʊb］
n. 细菌，微生物〈同　germ, bacteria〉
例　The disease is attributed to a microbe. 这种疾病归因于一种细菌。

microbe
microbe［'maɪkrəʊb］
n. 微生物
解　a minute life form (especially a disease-causing bacterium)
例　Town officials warned people against swimming in the local river because of the water pollution and the number of microbes floating around. 小镇的政府官员警告人们不要在当地的河里游泳，因为河水已被污染，并且水里有很多游离的微生物。
构　micro (=small) + be < bio (=life)

microorganism
microorganism［ˌmaɪkrəʊ'ɔ:ɡənɪz(ə)m］
n. 微生物
解　any organism (animal or plant) of microscopic size
例　The invention of the microscope helped scientists understand the function and appearance of certain microorganisms. 显微镜的发明帮助科学家了解了某些微生物的功能和外表特征。
构　micro (=minute) + organ (=instrument) + ism

microphone
microphone［'maɪkrəfəʊn］
n. 麦克风
解　a device for converting sound waves into electrical energy
例　His voice was so loud and resonant that he did not need a microphone to speak to the crowd. 他的声音大而洪亮，对人群讲话时都不需要拿麦克风。

microphone
microphone［'maɪkrəfəʊn］
n. 麦克风
解　a device for converting sound waves into electrical energy
例　She requested a cordless microphone for her lecture so she could walk around the audience. 她要求在演讲的时候使用无线麦克风，这样她就可以在听众面前走动。

microscope
microscope［'maɪkrəskəʊp］
n. 显微镜
解　instrument with a lens or combination of lenses for making small things look larger
例　Bacteria, blood cells, and other objects not visible to the naked eye are clearly visible through a microscope. 细菌、血细胞以及其他肉眼看不见的东西在显微镜下都可以清楚地看到。
同　microscopic adj. 极小的；显微镜的

mighty

例　The hero in the book was mighty and he fought dragons and tigers. 书中的主人公非常强大，他能斗蛟龙、战猛虎。

migrant

migrate

例　Pioneers from New England migrated to all parts of the United States. 从新英格兰来的开拓者移居到了美国的各个地方。

例　Man's first step on the Moon was a milestone in science. 人类在月球上迈出的第一步，是科学领域的里程碑。

milieu

例　It is incongruous to find an abstemious person in a milieu of affluence. 一个节俭的人处在一个富裕的社会环境里，是非常不协调的。

millennia

例　Many millennia have passed since China's history began to be recorded. 自中国历史有记载以来，已经过去了数千年。

millionaire
millionaire［ˌmɪljə'neə(r)］
n. 百万富翁

mime
mime［maɪm］
vt. 模拟，模仿〈同　mimic, imitate〉
例　Some insects will mime a twig when in danger. 有一些昆虫在遇到危险的情况下会模仿树枝。

mime
mime［maɪm］
n. 哑剧 v. 模拟，通过手势和身体的动作来表达
解　n. a performance using gestures and body movements without words v. to imitate; to mimic
例　The theatrical mime we saw last night was very interesting because the only sound we heard was the reaction of the audience. 我们昨晚在剧场看的哑剧十分有趣，现场唯一能听到的声音就是观众的反应。

mimic
mimic［'mɪmɪk］
n. 模仿者（模仿他人言行的人）v. ① 模仿 ② 戏弄
解　n. person or thing that imitates v. ① to copy closely; to imitate ② to copy or imitate so as to ridicule; mock
例　A parrot can mimic a person's voice. 鹦鹉能模仿人的声音。
近　inimical adj. 为敌的，不友善的
构　mim (=to imitate) + ic

mimicry
mimicry［'mɪmɪkri］
n.【生物】拟态；模仿
例　Mimicry is a biological phenomenon characterized by the superficial resemblance of two or more organisms that are not closely related. 拟态是一种生物学现象，其特点是没有密切关系的两个或多个生物体外表相似。

mimicry
mimicry［'mɪmɪkri］
n. 模仿，（动物等的）拟态伪装
解　imitation
例　The mimicry of insects to look like leaves is a survival mechanism. 昆虫通过模仿伪装成树叶的样子是一种生存机制。

mingle
mingle［'mɪŋgəl］
v.（使）混合；（使）结合〈同 mix〉
例　Water and oil do not mingle. 油和水不相融。

miniature
miniature［'mɪnətʃə(r); (US)'mɪnətʃʊər］
n. 缩小的模型，缩图，缩影
例　This model car is a miniature of a real one. 这个汽车模型是真车的缩小版。
adj. 微型的，缩小的〈同 tiny〉
例　Instead of buying a massive dog, Teddy got a miniature poodle. 泰迪买了一只迷你玩具贵宾犬，而没有买真的大贵宾犬。

miniature
miniature［'mɪnətʃə(r)］
adj. 小型的，缩影的 n. 小画像；缩影
解　being on a very small scale n. a copy or model that represents or reproduces something in a greatly reduced size
例　His favorite hobby was collecting miniature models of cars. 他的爱好是收集汽车模型。

minimal
minimal［'mɪnɪməl］
adj. 最小的，最小限度的
解　least possible; very small
例　Eric was so lazy that he only exerted the minimal effort to pass his courses. 埃里克太懒了，他只付出了最小的努力来通过各科的考试。

minimize
minimize［'mɪnɪmaɪz］
v.（使）最小化，（使）减到最小〈同 diminish〉
例　The businesswoman tried to minimize her losses when the stock market collapsed. 股市崩盘之后，女商人尽量把她的损失降低到最少。

minimize
minimize［'mɪnɪmaɪz］
v. 低估；把…减到最小
解　to reduce to the smallest possible amount or degree
例　The company directors met to talk about ways to minimize risks and increase profits. 公司主管聚集在一起，讨论降低风险和提高利润的方法。

minimum
minimum　［ˈmɪnɪməm］
adj. 最小的，最低的〈同 smallest〉
例 The minimum age for leaving school is 16. 离校的最小年龄是16岁。
n. 最小值
例 You ought to eat a minimum of 1,000 calories a day. 你每天摄入的热量至少要达到1,000卡路里。
联 minimize v. 减到最低程度

minority
minority　［maɪˈnɒrəti; (US)maɪˈnɔːrəti］
n. 少数；少数民族
例 Only a minority of his wages was spent on feeding his family. 他的工资只有一小部分用来养家糊口。

minority
minority［maɪ'nɒrɪti; mɪ-］
n. ① 少数 ② 少数民族
解　① the smaller number or part; less than half ② a group within a country, state, etc., that differs in race, religion, national origin, etc., from the larger part of the population
例　A minority of the voters wanted a tax increase, but the majority defeated it. 少数选民希望增加税收，但是大多数选民都不同意。

minus
minus　［ˈmaɪnəs］
adj. 负的
例 Minus six plus minus two equals minus eight. 负6加负2等于负8。
prep. 减去
例 Fifteen minus four equals eleven. 15减4等于11。

minuscule
minuscule［'mɪnəskju:l］
adj. 极小的〈同　tiny, very small〉
例　The students used a microscope to look at a minuscule organism. 学生们用显微镜来观察微小的有机体。

minuscule
minuscule［'mɪnəskju:l］
adj. ① 极小的，微小的 ② 小写的
解　① very small ② of, relating to, or written in a lowercase letter
例　The microbiologist used an electron microscope to examine minuscule objects. 微生物学家使用电子显微镜来检测微小的物体。

minute
minute　［maɪˈnjuːt］
adj. ① 极小的，极少的〈同 tiny〉
例 The baby mice were minute when they were born. 老鼠幼崽在刚出生时非常小。
例 Please report this event in minute detail. 请详细报道此事件。
记 minu（小）+te→极小的
联 minutia n. 细节，琐事

minutia
minutia［maɪ'nju:ʃɪə］
n. 微枝末节，细节
解　details, trivia
例　The media gives us more minutiae about movie stars than we really need to know. 媒体向我们报导很多关于电影明星的细节资料，比我们真正想知道的多得多。

miracle
miracle　［ˈmɪrəkəl］
n. 奇迹，奇事〈同 marvel〉
例 It's a miracle of nature that life can grow on plants that look dead all winter. 那些在整个冬天看起来像是死掉的植物竟然能恢复生机，真是大自然的奇迹。
联 miraculous adj. 奇迹的，不可思议的

mirage
mirage［'mɪrɑ:ʒ］
n. 海市蜃楼，幻景〈同　illusion, delusion〉
例　Thirsty people walking in the desert are likely to see a mirage of a pond. 口渴的人在沙漠里行走，很可能会看到池塘的海市蜃楼。

mirror
mirror　［ˈmɪrə(r)］
vt. 反映，映出〈同 reflect〉
例 The strength of the economy is mirrored in improved living standards. 经济的力量反映在生活水平的提高上。

misbehave
misbehave［mɪs'bɪheɪv］
v. 行为不端，举止不当
解　to behave (oneself) in an inappropriate way
例　Although she was the brightest student in the class, she was not nominated to receive the “Model Student Award” because she misbehaved. 她是班里最聪明的学生，但是由于行为不端，她没有获得“模范学生奖”的提名。

mischief
mischief［'mɪstʃɪf］
n. 恶作剧，淘气
例　The dog's mischief made a mess of the house when the owners were gone. 当主人不在家的时候，顽皮的狗把整个屋子弄得一团糟。

misconduct
misconduct［mɪs'kɒndʌkt］
n. 行为不端
解　bad behavior
例　The boy's misconduct in class led to his punishment. 男孩因为在班里行为不端而受到了惩罚。

miscreant
miscreant［'mɪskrɪənt］
n. 恶棍，歹徒
解　wretch; villain
例　The miscreant became a lawless criminal when he grew up. 这个恶棍长大以后变成了一个违法犯罪的罪犯。

misdeed
misdeed［ˌmɪs'di:d］
n. 恶行
解　a bad act; wicked deed
例　The president's misdeed became a controversial scandal. 总统的恶劣行为变成了一个引起争议的丑闻。

misdemeanor
misdemeanor［ˌmɪsdɪ'mi:nə(r)］
n. 【律】轻罪；不良行为
解　an offence less serious than a felony; minor crime
例　Since Brad was only charged with a misdemeanor, not a felony, he received a light sentence. 由于布拉德只是被指控为品行不端，而非刑事重罪，因此他被从轻判决。

miserable
miserable　［ˈmɪzərəbəl］
adj. 痛苦的，悲惨的，可怜的〈同 unhappy〉
例 She's been so miserable since her dog died. 自从她的狗死了之后，她便一直非常痛苦。

misery
misery［'mɪzəri］
n. 悲惨，不幸〈同 pain〉
例　I was in great misery when I broke my leg. 我的腿断了，十分痛苦。

misfortune
misfortune［mɪs'fɔ:tʃu:n］
n. 不幸，灾祸〈同 disaster〉
例　It was a misfortune that you lost your money so early in the trip. 旅行才刚开始你就把钱丢了，真不幸。

mishap
mishap［'mɪshæp］
n. 不幸，坏运气
解　an instance of misfortune; mischance
例　When his basketball broke the window, Bruce immediately apologized and paid for the mishap. 布鲁斯的篮球把窗玻璃打碎了，他立即道歉并赔偿了损失。

mislead
mislead［mɪs'li:d］
vt. 使误入歧途，误导；欺骗〈同 misguide, deceive〉
例　It is against the law to post an advertisement that misleads the public. 张贴误导公众的广告是违法的。

misplace
misplace［ˌmɪs'pleɪs］
v. 错误放置（口语中也指忘记放在什么地方）
解　to put into a wrong place
例　He was late because he had misplaced his car keys and couldn't find them. 由于他忘了把车钥匙放在哪儿了，怎么也找不到，因此迟到了。

missile
missile　［ˈmɪsaɪl］
n. 导弹，发射物
例 There are enough atomic missiles to destroy the whole world several times. 原子弹的数量已经足以将整个世界毁灭许多次。

mission
mission　［ˈmɪʃən］
n. 使命；任务〈同 task〉
例 Their mission was to find a way to the top of the mountain. 他们的任务是找到一条通往山顶的路。

missionary
missionary［'mɪʃənəri; (US)'mɪʃəneri］
n. 传教士〈同 preacher〉
例　He spent 20 years in Africa as a missionary. 他在非洲从事了20年的传教工作。

mist
mist　［mɪst］
n. 薄雾；喷雾
例 The gardener sprayed the plants with mist. 园艺师给植物洒喷雾。

mistrust
mistrust［mɪs'trʌst］
vt. 不信任，不相信，怀疑〈同　distrust, suspect〉
例　She mistrusted her husband's excuse for coming home late and asked him repeatedly what he had been doing. 她不相信丈夫所说的回家晚的理由，因此一遍遍地问他都做了什么。

mitigate
mitigate［'mɪtɪgeɪt］
vt. 使减轻，使缓和〈同　alleviate, relieve〉
例　A bouquet of roses should mitigate your wife's anger. 一束玫瑰花应该能缓和您妻子的怒气。

mnemonics
mnemonics［ni:'mɒnɪks］
n. 记忆法，记忆术
解　a system to develop or improve the memory
例　After his course in mnemonics, he could remember all the names of the people he met. 在学完记忆法的课程之后，他能记住所有见过面的人的名字。

mnemonics
mnemonics［ni:'mɒnɪks］
n. 记忆法，记忆规则
解　a system to develop or improve the memory
例　Jerry practised mnemonics in order to get better grades on his exams and succeed in life. 为了在考试时取得更好的成绩并且获得成功的人生，杰里努力练习记忆法。

moan
moan［məʊn］
n. 呻吟〈同　groan, sob〉
例　I could hear the moans of the patient in the next room. 我能听到隔壁房间那名患者的呻吟声。
v. 发出呻吟声；抱怨〈同　lament〉
例　She moaned all night when her pet fish died. 她的宠物鱼死后，她哀叹了一整夜。

moat
moat［məʊt］
n. 护城河，壕沟〈同　trench〉
例　The moat around the castle was ten feet deep. 城堡周围的护城河有十英尺深。

mobile
mobile　［ˈməʊbaɪl］
adj. ① 可移动的〈同 moveable〉
例 The mobile blood bank operated by the Red Cross visited our neighborhood today. 由红十字会管理的移动血库今天来到了我们社区。
例 Her face is so mobile—one minute she seems to be laughing, the next crying! 她的面部表情真丰富——前一分钟看起来还在笑，后一分钟就变成哭了！
联 mobility n. 流动性；灵活性；immobile adj. 稳定的

mobilize
mobilize［'məʊbɪlaɪz］
v. 动员
例　The senator mobilized all her supporters for her reelection campaign. 在连任竞选时，参议员动员了她所有的支持者。

mock
mock［mɒk］
v. 尤指以（模仿性）嘲笑〈同 ridicule〉
例　Don't mock him just because he keeps falling off his bike. 不要仅仅因为他总是从自行车上摔下来就嘲笑他。

mode
mode　［məʊd］
n. 方式，模式〈同 manner〉
例 Our mode of doing business is to treat the customer like royalty. 我们做生意的方式是把客户当作王室成员一样对待。

moderate
moderate
例 Unlike moderate antislavery advocates, abolitionists demanded an immediate end to slavery. 与温和的反对奴隶制的主张不同，废奴主义者要求立即废除奴隶制。
例 Cool breezes will moderate the high temperatures of the last two days. 凉风将使过去两天的高温有所缓解。
记 moder（=mod 风度）+ate→做事有风度→适度的
联 immoderate adj. 无节制的；moderation n. 适度

modest
modest　［ˈmɒdɪst］
adj. 谦虚的；适度的〈同 humble; moderate〉
例 Bernie won many awards as a translator but he is always modest when he speaks about it. 作为一名翻译，伯尼获得过许多奖项，但他在谈论这些荣誉的时候却始终非常谦虚。
记 mod（方式，风度）+est→做事有风度→谦虚的；适度的
联 immodest adj. 不谦虚的

modest
modest［'mɒdɪst］
adj. ① 谦虚的，谦让的 ② 适度的
解　① not thinking too highly of oneself; not vain; humble ② not too great; not asking too much
例　In spite of many honors, the scientist remained a modest person. 虽然获得了很多荣誉，这位科学家依然很谦虚。
同　modesty n. 谦虚；节制

modify
modify　［ˈmɒdɪfaɪ］
vt. 修改，变更〈同 alter〉
例 I modified my travel plans by staying an extra night in Rome. 我修改了我的旅行计划，决定在罗马多住一晚。
记 mod（=mode 方式）+ ify→改变方式→修改
联 modification n. 修改，修饰；modifiable adj. 可更改的；modifier n. 改造者；修饰语

modify
modify［'mɒdɪfaɪ］
v. 修改，变更
解　to change something a little
例　He asked the mechanic to modify his car to include his preferences, such as a new sunroof and tinted windows. 他要求机械师按照他的偏好来改装汽车，比如换个天窗、换个深色的车窗玻璃。
同　modification n. 修饰，修改

modish
modish［'məʊdɪʃ］
adj. 时髦的
解　fashionable
例　She always discarded all garments which were no longer modish. 她通常会把所有过时的衣服都扔掉。

moisture
moisture　［ˈmɔɪstʃə］
n. 潮湿，湿气；湿度〈同 wetness〉
例 I could feel the moisture in the air on the muggy day. 在闷热的桑拿天里，我能感觉到空气中的潮湿。

mold
mold［məʊld］
vt. 塑造〈同　shape, model〉
例　The sculptor molded the clay into a flowerpot. 雕刻家用模子把黏土做成花盆。
n. ①模子；铸型〈同　die, frame〉
例　She makes candles by pouring wax into copper molds. 她通过把蜡倒入铜模具中来制作蜡烛。
例　I threw out the bread because of the mold spotting its surface. 我把那块面包扔了，因为面包表面都长霉菌了。

molecule
molecule　［ˈmɒlɪkjuːl］
n. 分子
例 One molecule of water equals two atoms of hydrogen and one atom of oxygen. 一个水分子等于两个氢原子和一个氧原子。
联 molecular adj. 分子的

molten
molten［'məʊltən］
adj. 熔融的，熔化的〈同　melted, fused〉
例　The city of Pompeii was destroyed by volcanic ash rather than by molten lava flowing from Mount Vesuvius. 摧毁庞贝古城的是火山灰，而不是维苏威火山喷出的熔岩。

momentary
momentary［'məʊməntəri］

例　The sight of the shooting star was only momentary. 看到流星只是一瞬间的事。

monarch

例　Prince William may become the next English monarch. 威廉王子或许将成为下一任英国国王。

monarch

解　the ruler of a nation
例　Queen Victoria was Great Britain's monarch from 1837 to 1901. 从1837年到1901年，维多利亚女王是大不列颠的君主。

monetary
monetary［'mʌnɪtri］

例　In response to the bad economy, the President will announce a national policy for monetary reforms. 为了应对糟糕的经济状况，总统将宣布一项货币改革的国家政策。

monitor

例 The doctor monitored the patient's heartbeat every minute. 医生监控患者每分钟的心跳。

monochromatic
monochromatic［ˌmɒnəʊkrə'mætɪk］

monocle
monocle［'mɒnɒkəl］
n. 单片眼镜
解　a lens for correcting defective vision in one eye
例　The professor used a monocle since one of his eyes was blind. 自从一只眼睛失明之后，教授一直使用单片眼镜。

monolithic
monolithic［ˌmɒnə'lɪθɪk］
adj. ① 整体式的 ② 完整的；坚定的；庞大的
解　① constituting or acting as a single, often rigid, uniform whole ② uniform, solid, and massive
例　Nothing could bend the monolithic will of the people. 没有什么能使人民坚定的意愿屈服。

monologue
monologue［'mɒnəlɒɡ］

解　① speech you make to yourself ② a (usually long) dramatic speech by a single actor
例　She entertained the audience with a witty autobiographical monologue. 她使用机智诙谐的自传式独白愉悦观众。

monopolize
monopolize［mə'nɒpəlaɪz］
vt. 独占，垄断〈同　dominate, occupy〉
例　The three leading companies entered into a secret agreement in order to monopolize the entire industry. 为了垄断整个行业，三家领先的公司达成了一项秘密协议。

monopoly
monopoly［mə'nɒpəli］
n. 垄断，独占
例　The company once had a monopoly on the telecom industry. 这家公司曾经垄断了电信行业。

monopoly
monopoly［mə'nɒpəli］
n. 垄断，专利权
解　exclusive control or possession of something
例　The government refused to allow the two corporations to merge into one for fear that they would create a monopoly and charge customers any price they wanted. 政府不允许这两家公司合并成一家，因为担心这样会形成垄断，会导致他们向消费者任意要价。
同　monopolization n. 垄断

monotonous
monotonous［mə'nɒtənəs］
adj. 单调乏味的；无变化的〈同　boring; repetitive〉
例　My professor's monotonous voice puts me to sleep. 我的教授单调的嗓音让我昏昏欲睡。

monotony
monotony［mə'nɒtəni］
n. 单调
解　sameness leading to boredom
例　The monotony in the professor's voice made many students doze off during class. 教授单调的声音使很多学生在课堂上打起了瞌睡。
同　monotonous adj. 单调的，无聊的

morale
morale［mə'rɑ:l; (US)'mɜ:ræl］
n. 士气〈同　confidence, spirit〉
例　With no food or water, the soldiers' morale waned. 由于没有食物和水，士兵们士气低落。

morality
morality［mɒ'ræləti］
n. 道德〈同 righteousness〉
例　I have to question the morality of forcing poor people to pay for their medical treatment. 强迫穷人为医疗护理埋单，我不得不质疑这种行为的道德性。

morphology
morphology［mɔ:'fɒləʤi］
n. 形态学，形态论
例　The biology class on morphology used a dead cat as a lab specimen. 讲授形态学的生物课用一只死猫作为实验样品。

mortal
mortal［'mɔ:təl］
adj. 必死的；致命的〈同 fatal〉
例　The soldier received a mortal wound in battle. 这名士兵在战场上受了致命伤。

mortar
mortar［'mɔ:tə(r)］
n. 灰泥；臼，研钵
例　The mason used a mortar of cement when building a brick house. 泥瓦匠在盖砖房的时候，使用了混有水泥的砂浆。

mortgage
mortgage［'mɔ:gɪʤ］
n. 抵押贷款
例　If you fail to repay the mortgage, the bank will repossess your house. 如果你无法偿还贷款，银行将收回你的房子。

mosaic
mosaic［mə'zeɪɪk］
n./adj. 镶嵌图案（的）
例　She made a mosaic out of broken glass from different colored bottles. 她用把不同颜色的瓶子打碎后的玻璃做了一个镶嵌画。

mosquito
mosquito　［məˈskiːtəʊ］
n. 蚊子
例 I became sick after I was bitten by a mosquito. 我被一只蚊子叮了之后就病了。

motif
motif［məʊ'ti:f］
n.（作品的）主题，主旨〈同　theme, subject〉
例　Seeing how animals lived was a motif that the children enjoyed. 亲眼见证动物们如何生活是孩子们喜欢的一个主题。

motility
motility［məʊ'tɪlɪtɪ］
n. 能动性
解　ability to move spontaneously
例　The motility of frogs comes from the propulsion of their leg muscles. 青蛙之所以能跳动，是由于它的腿部肌肉具有推进力。

motivate
motivate　［ˈməʊtɪveɪt］
vt. 激发，刺激〈同 prompt〉
例 The energetic teacher motivates her students by praising them for good work. 那位精力充沛的老师通过对学生的良好表现进行表扬来激励他们。
记 motiv（动机）+ate→有动机→激发
联 motivation n. 动机；刺激

motivate
motivate［'məʊtɪveɪt］
v. 促使，激发
解　to give a motive or incentive to
例　The coach motivated his players to play the best game of their lives. 教练激励运动员们打一场生平最好的比赛。
同　motivation n. 动机，目的；motivational adj. 激发积极性的

motive
motive［'məʊtɪv］
n. 动机，目的
解　the reason for the action
例　The student had only one motive in college—to make good grades and find a good job after graduation. 这个学生上大学只有一个目的，那就是拿高分，然后在毕业后找一份好工作。

mount
mount　［maʊnt］
v. ① 增长〈同 increase〉
例 Rent mounts month by month. 租金每月都在上涨。
例 He mounted a horse and rode off in a cloud of dust. 他骑上马，在飞扬的尘土中疾驰而去。

mournful
mournful［'mɔ:nfʊl］
adj. 悲痛的，悲哀的〈同 sorrowful〉
例　We heard the mournful cry of a wolf. 我们听见了一只狼的哀鸣。

muddy
muddy［'mʌdi］
adj. 多泥的，泥泞的
例　The dog played in the rain and when it came back, it left muddy footprints on the floor. 小狗在雨里玩耍过，当它回到家，地板上留下了带着泥巴的足印。

mulberry
mulberry［'mʌlbəri; (US)'mʌlberi］
n. 桑树
例　The larva silkworm feeds on mulberry leaves. 蚕的幼虫以桑叶为食。

multicellular
multicellular［ˌmʌltɪ'seljʊlə(r)］
adj. 多细胞的
例　Humans are multicellular organisms. 人是多细胞生物。

multifaceted
multifaceted［ˌmʌltɪ'fæsɪtɪd］
adj. 多方面的；多才多艺的〈同　complex; versatile〉
例　It's a multifaceted business, offering a range of services. 这是一家综合性公司，可以提供各种服务。

multiple
multiple［'mʌltɪpəl］
adj. 多样的，多重的
例　When selecting your answer from among several in a multiple choice test, always seek the word that is nearest or most appropriate. 在做选择题的时候，要选出那个意思最接近或者最恰当的单词。

multiply
multiply　［ˈmʌltɪplaɪ］
v. ① 繁殖，增加〈同 proliferate, increase〉
例 The world population is multiplying fast. 世界人口在迅速增加。
例 Two multiplied by four is eight. 2乘以4等于8。

multitude
multitude［'mʌltɪtju:d; (US)'mʌltɪtu:d］
n. 大量，多数〈同 a great number〉
例　The book will find a multitude of readers. 那本书将拥有众多的读者。

mundane
mundane［'mʌndeɪn］
adj. ①平常的，普通的〈同　ordinary, everyday〉
例　Sally was tired of her mundane homework and wanted something more challenging. 萨莉厌倦了单调的家庭作业，希望来一些更具挑战性的东西。
例　He devoted himself to the spiritual needs of his followers, and left to his aides such mundane tasks as providing food and shelter. 他毕生致力于满足其追随者的精神需求，而把一些世俗的任务留给了他的助手，比如提供食物和住所等。

municipal
municipal［mju:'nɪsɪpəl］
adj. 市的，市政的〈同 civic〉
例　Municipal planners deal chiefly with the new layout of communities. 市政设计者主要负责社区新布局。

mural
mural［'mjʊərəl］
n. 壁画，壁饰〈同　wall painting〉
例　The museum painted murals on the hallway to the main exhibit. 博物馆在通往主展厅的走廊上绘制了壁画。

murmur
murmur［'mɜ:mə(r)］
v. 低声说，低语
例　The shy child murmured her thanks. 害羞的小女孩喃喃地道谢。

muscular
muscular［'mʌskjʊlə(r)］
adj. 强壮的，肌肉发达的〈同 brawny〉
例　He wished he was more muscular and didn't have such skinny arms. 他希望自己能更结实一点，而不是有这样皮包骨头的臂膀。

mushroom
mushroom　［ˈmʌʃrʊm］
n. 蘑菇
例 Thousands of mushrooms covered the dark forest floor. 成千上万的蘑菇覆盖着森林里不见阳光的地表。
v. 迅速生长
例 Since the government began offering easy loans, small businesses have mushroomed. 由于政府开始提供宽松的贷款，因此小企业如雨后春笋般迅速增加。

mute
mute［mju:t］
adj. 哑的；无声的，沉默的〈同 unable to speak, silent〉
例　The little girl stood mute with astonishment. 小女孩惊呆了，默默地站着。

mutual
mutual　［ˈmjuːtjʊəl］
adj. 相互的；共有的〈同 interactive〉
例 Although Bob and his father do not agree on the issues, they have a mutual respect for each other's opinions. 虽然鲍勃和他父亲在这几个问题上没有达成一致，但他们都相互尊重彼此的意见。
联 mutually adv. 互相地

myriad
myriad［'mɪrɪəd］
n. 许多，无数
例　A country sky on a clear night is filled with a myriad of stars. 在晴朗的夜晚，乡村的夜空中缀满了无数的星辰。
adj. 无数的〈同　many, countless〉
例　The geese flew south in a myriad flock. 无数群大雁向南飞。

mysterious
mysterious［mɪ'stɪərɪəs］
adj. 神秘的，不可思议的〈同 unexplainable, enigmatic〉
例　The appearance of UFOs has always been mysterious. UFO是什么样子一直都是个迷。

myth
myth　［mɪθ］
n. 神话，神话故事〈同 legend〉
例 When I was a child, my grandmother told me the myths that she had heard from her grandmother. 当我还是个孩子的时候，奶奶把她从她奶奶那里听到的神话故事讲给我听。
联 mythical adj. 神话的，虚构的；mythology n. [总称]神话

mythology
mythology［mɪ'θɒləʤi］
n. 神话学；神话
解　the study of myths
例　The mythology of many ancient societies saw the sun as a deity. 在很多古代社会的神话故事中，太阳都被看做神。

naive
naive［nɑ:'i:v］
adj. 天真的；幼稚的，容易上当的〈同 unsophisticated, innocent〉
例　Young, naive and trusting as I was, I believed every word he said. 那时的我年轻、幼稚，容易相信人，所以我相信他说的每句话。

naked
naked　［ˈneɪkɪd］
adj. 裸体的，无遮盖的〈同 nude〉
例 Due to the refraction of light rays, it is impossible for the naked eye to determine the exact location of a star close to the horizon. 由于光线会发生折射，因此用肉眼无法确定一颗接近地平线的星星的确切位置。

namely
namely［'neɪmli］
adv. 即，也就是
例　I like science subjects at school, namely mathematics, physics, chemistry and biology. 在学校里，我喜欢理科科目，也就是数学、物理、化学和生物。

nap
nap［næp］
n.（白天）小睡，打盹〈同 doze〉
例　People usually feel sleepy after lunch. It is beneficial for them to take a nap. 人们通常在午餐后容易犯困。对他们来说打个盹是很有益的。

narrate
narrate［nə'reɪt］
v. 讲述〈同 tell〉
例　The speaker presented slides and narrated the story behind them. 演讲者播放幻灯片，讲述它们背后的故事。

nasty
nasty［'nɑ:sti; (US)'næsti］
adj. ① 令人不愉快的，讨厌的〈同 unpleasant〉
例　The nasty weather ruined our plans for a picnic. 糟糕的天气毁掉了我们去野餐的计划。
例　Several nasty people threw rocks at the birds on the lake. 几个素质低下的人向湖里的鸟儿扔石头。

naturalist
naturalist［'nætʃərəlɪst］
n. 自然主义者；博物学家
例　Many of the people who work at the zoo are naturalists. 许多在动物园工作的人都是自然主义者。

naughty
naughty［'nɔ:ti］
adj. 顽皮的，淘气的〈同　disobedient, mischievous〉
例　The boy was very nanghty and would not listen to his mother. 那个男孩非常调皮，根本不听他妈妈的话。

naval
naval［'neɪvəl］
adj. 海军的；军舰的〈同　maritime〉
例　England was well-known for its naval power. 英格兰以其海军力量而闻名。

neat
neat［ni:t］
adj. 整洁的；整齐的〈同　tidy, clean〉
例　His mom cleaned his room and left it looking neat. 他妈妈给他打扫了房间，让房间看起来非常整洁。

necessitate
necessitate［nɪ'sesɪteɪt］
vt. 使成为必需，需要〈同 make necessary〉
例　Her broken leg necessitated an operation. 他的腿部骨折了，需要做手术。

needy
needy［'ni:di］
adj. 贫穷的，生活艰苦的〈同　poor, indigent〉
例　The money from the charity event will go to the needy. 慈善活动募集的钱将捐给贫困者。

negative
negative　［ˈneɡətɪv］
adj. ① 否定的；负的〈同 adverse〉
例 We got a negative answer to our request. 我们的请求被拒绝了。
例 If you're so negative, you'll never get the job. 如果你总是这么消极，你就永远找不到工作。
记 neg（否认，否定）+ ative→否定的
联 negate v. 否定，打消

neglect
neglect　［nɪˈɡlekt］
n./vt. 疏忽；忘记〈同 disregard; ignore〉
例 He works so hard that he neglects his family. 他工作太卖力了，把家人都忽视了。
联 negligent adj. 疏忽的，粗心大意的；negligible adj. 可忽略的，无关紧要的

negligible
negligible［'neglɪʤəbəl］
adj. 可忽略的，无关紧要的〈同 insignificant, tiny〉
例　The loss of ten cents is negligible. 十美分的损失微不足道。

negotiate
negotiate　［nɪˈɡəʊʃɪeɪt］
v. 谈判，交涉；议定〈同 discuss〉
例 The two parties are negotiating the contract. 双方正在就合同进行磋商。
联 negotiation n. 商议，谈判

neurology
neurology［njʊə'rɒləʤi］
n. 神经病学
解　the branch of medical science that deals with the nervous system and its disorders
例　She visited several experts in neurology to get a comparative diagnosis of her nervous system disorder. 为了对自己的神经系统紊乱进行比较诊断，她拜访了好几位神经学专家。

neutral
neutral　［ˈnjuːtrəl］
adj. 中性的；中立的〈同 impartial〉
例 A neutral political viewpoint is neither conservative nor liberal. 中立的政治观点既不属于保守派，也不属于自由派。
记 neutr（中间）+al→中立的
联 neutralize v. 使中立化；使无效；neutron n. 【核物理学】中子

neutralize
neutralize［'nju:trəlaɪz; (US)'nu:-］
vt. 抵消，中和〈同　offset, counterbalance〉
例　I neutralized the acid in my stomach by taking an antacid. 我吃了一片抗酸剂，来中和胃酸。

nevertheless
nevertheless　［ˌnevəðəˈles］
adv. 仍然，不过〈同 even so, still〉
例 I don't want to come; nevertheless I shall because I feel I have to. 我不想来；但我还是会来，因为我感觉我不得不来。

niche
niche［ni:∫; nɪtʃ］
n. ①壁龛〈同　alcove, recess〉
例　The status stood in a niche. 雕像立在壁龛中。
例　After trying several career paths, he finally found his niche in engineering. 尝试过多种职业之后，他最终在工程学行业找到了适合自己的位置。

nicotine
nicotine［'nɪkəti:n］
n. 尼古丁
例　The smoker had yellow nicotine stains on his teeth and fingers. 吸烟者的牙齿和手指上会有黄色的尼古丁污渍。

nightmare
nightmare　［ˈnaɪtmɛə(r)］
n. 噩梦〈同 frightening dream〉
例 The girl had a nightmare about jumping off a burning train. 那个女孩做了一个噩梦，梦见自己从一辆着火的列车上跳了下来。
记 组合词：night（夜晚）+mare（恶魔）→夜晚梦见恶魔→噩梦

nocturnal
nocturnal［nɒk'tɜ:nəl］
adj. 夜的；夜曲的〈同　nightly〉
例　A nocturnal animal is one that is active primarily during the night. 夜行动物是主要在夜间活动的动物。

nomadic
nomadic［nəʊ'mædɪk］
adj. 游牧的，流浪的〈同　wandering, itinerant〉
例　Many Native Americans were nomadic people who lived in portable homes called teepees. 许多美洲印第安人都是游牧民族，住在一种可移动的锥形帐篷里。

nominal
nominal［'nɒmɪnəl］
adj. ① 名义上的，不实的〈同 not real〉
例　The president is the nominal head of our club, but the secretary really runs things. 在我们社团，会长只是名义上的领导，书记才是办事的人。
例　We paid our friend a nominal rent for the apartment—$5 a month. 我们住这间公寓，象征性地付点房租给朋友——每个月5美元。

nominal
nominal［'nɒmɪnəl］
adj. 名义上的，有名无实的
解　existing in name only; not real
例　The president is the nominal head of our club, but the secretary really runs things. 我们社团在名义上的领导是会长，但真正处理事务的是书记。
构　nomin (=name) + al (=nature of)

nominate
nominate［'nɒmɪneɪt］
vt. 提名；任命〈同 designate〉
例　In ominated Mary for the office of treasurer. 我认命玛丽为办公室财务主管。

nominate
nominate［'nɒmɪneɪt］
v. 提名
解　to propose as a candidate for some honor
例　The Democrats and the Republicans each nominate one candidate for the presidential election. 民主党和共和党分别推荐了一名候选人来竞选总统。

nonconformist
nonconformist［ˌnɒnkən'fɔ:mɪst］
adj./n. 不遵照传统生活的（人）〈同　unconventional; rebel〉
例　Nonconformists do not easily follow the crowd or take orders. 不墨守成规的人不会轻易从众或接受命令。

nonprofessional
nonprofessional［ˌnɔnprə'fe∫ənəl］
adj. 非专业的；无专长的〈同　amateur〉
例　The Olympics only allowed nonprofessional athletes to compete in the games. 奥运会只允许非职业运动员参加比赛。

nonsense
nonsense［'nɒnsəns; (US)-sens］
n. 胡说，废话〈同　silliness, rubbish〉
例　The city's newspapers proclaimed that the referee's decision was nonsense and their team should have won. 这座城市的报纸宣布，裁判的判决是荒谬的，他们的队伍应该赢得比赛。

nontraditional
nontraditional［ˌnɒntrə'dɪ∫ənəl］
adj. 不遵照传统生活的〈同　liberal〉
例　Nontraditional thinking most always meets initial resistence from the public and takes time to become accepted. 打破传统的思维开始通常都会遇到来自公众的阻力，需要花时间才能被接受。

norm
norm［nɔ:m］
n. 准则，规范〈同 convention, standard〉
例　You must adapt to the norms of the school. 你必须适应学校的行为准则。

normal
normal［'nɔ:məl］
adj. 正常的，一般的
解　according to what is expected, usual, or average
例　The scorching heat is normal weather during the summer in Beijing. 在北京的夏天，高温天气很正常。

normalization
normalization［ˌnɔ:məlaɪ'zeɪʃən］
n. 标准化
解　the imposition of a standard
例　The quality control department assured the normalization of production processes, resulting in quality products for the company. 质量控制部门确保生产过程的标准化，从而使公司生产出质量合格的产品。

normally
normally　［ˈnɔːməli］
adv. 正常地，通常地〈同 commonly, typically〉
例 It is normally quite hot at this time of the year in Beijing. 北京每年的这个时候通常都很热。
联 normalize v. 规格化；normalization n. 正常化，标准化

nostalgia
nostalgia［nɒs'tælʤɪə］
n. 思家病，怀旧〈同　homesickness, reminiscence〉
例　After living far away from his hometown for almost twenty years, a feeling of nostalgia often came over him. 在远离家乡生活了近二十年之后，他心中经常涌起一股乡愁。

nostalgia
nostalgia［nɒs'tælʤɪə］
n. ① 思乡病 ② 怀旧之情
解　① homesickness ② longing for the past
例　Looking at her childhood pictures brought her a sense of nostalgia. 看着小时候的照片，她产生了一种怀旧之情。
同　nostalgic adj. 怀旧的，思乡的

notable
notable［'nəʊtəbəl］
adj. 著名的；显要的〈同 noteworthy〉
例　She has made notable contributions to the field of biology. 她在生物领域做出了卓越贡献。
n. 名人，要人
例　It was hard to realize that the small, rather ordinary-looking person standing before us was a world-famous notable. 很难意识到这位站在我们面前的个子矮小、长相普通的人是一位世界知名人士。

notation
notation［nəʊ'teɪʃən］
n. 符号
例　In arithmetic we use Arabic notation（1，2，3，4，etc.）and sometimes Roman notation（Ⅰ，Ⅱ，Ⅲ，Ⅳ，etc.）. 在算术里，我们使用阿拉伯符号（1、2、3、4、等），有时候也使用罗马符号（Ⅰ、Ⅱ、Ⅲ、Ⅳ、等）。

notch
notch［nɒtʃ］
n. 刻痕
例　Scores of games used to be counted by notches on sticks. 过去经常是在木棍上刻出印痕来计算比赛的分数。

noteworthy
noteworthy［'nəʊtwɜ:ði］
adj. 值得注目的，显著的〈同　notable, remarkable〉
例　The first flight across the Atlantic was a noteworthy achievement. 穿越大西洋的第一次飞行是非常显著的成就。

notify
notify［'nəʊtɪfaɪ］
v. 通知〈同 inform〉
例　Our teacher notified us that there would be a test on Monday. 老师通知我们周一会有测试。

notorious
notorious［nəʊ'tɔ:rɪəs］
adj. 臭名昭著的，声名狼藉的〈同 disreputable〉
例　No one wanted to play poker with Tom, because he was a notorious cheater. 没人愿意和汤姆打扑克，因为他是一个臭名昭著的骗子。

nourish
nourish［'nʌrɪʃ; 'nɜ:rɪʃ］
vt. 养育；滋养〈同 feed, nurture〉
例　After the operation, the doctor plans to nourish the patient with vitamins and good food. 手术之后，医生计划用维生素和有营养的食物为病人补充营养。

novelty

记 novel（新的）+ty→新颖

optimistic
optimistic　［ˌɒptɪˈmɪstɪk］
adj. 乐观的〈同 hopeful〉
例 She is optimistic about her chances of winning a gold medal. 她乐观地相信自己有赢得金牌的机会。
联 optimism n. 乐观主义，乐观

optimum
optimum［'ɒptɪməm］
adj. 最适宜的〈同 ideal, best〉
例　If you wait for the optimum moment to act, you may never begin your project. 如果你在等待最合适的时刻启动项目，那你可能永远也不会启动。

option
option［'ɒpʃən］
n. 选项；选择权〈同 alternative, choice〉
例　Pupils in our school have the option of taking Spanish, French or German. 我们学校的学生可以选择上西班牙语课、法语课或者德语课。

optional
optional　［ˈɒpʃənəl］
adj. 可自由选择的〈同 not compulsory〉
例 At the end of every chapter in our science text, there is a group of optional questions, intended for students who wish to go more deeply into the subject. 在我们的科学教科书每一章的结尾，都有一些可自由选择回答的问题。这些问题针对的是愿意进一步深入了解这门课的学生。

oral
oral［'ɔ:rəl］
adj. 口头的〈同 spoken〉
例　Had I known this was an oral exam, I would not have brought pen and paper. 要是知道这是口试的话，我就不带笔和纸了。

orbit
orbit　［ˈɔːbɪt］
n. 轨道〈同 circle〉
例 Our planet is in orbit around the sun. 地球环绕太阳运行。
vt. 绕…轨道而行〈同 encircle〉
例 The earth orbits the sun every 365 days. 地球每365天环绕太阳一周。
联 orbital adj. 轨道的

orchard
orchard［'ɔ:tʃəd］
n. 果园〈同　garden〉
例　My grandfather has a large vegetable garden and an apple orchard behind his house. 我爷爷在房子后面有一大片菜园和一个苹果园。

orchestra
orchestra　［ˈɔːkɪstrə］
n. 管弦乐队〈同 band〉
例 Orchestras play symphonies and the music for operas and dance. 管弦乐队演奏交响乐和歌剧与舞蹈中的音乐。

orchid
orchid［'ɔ:kɪd］
n. 兰花
例　His favorite flower was the orchid. 他最喜欢的花是兰花。

ordeal
ordeal［ɔ:'di:l］
n. 严峻考验，痛苦的经历〈同　trying experience, hardship〉
例　The hostages' ordeal came to an end when soldiers stormed the building. 士兵们突袭大楼之后，人质们的痛苦经历终于结束了。

orderly
orderly［'ɔ:dəli］
adj. 有秩序的；整洁的〈同 disciplined, ordered〉
例　The books were aligned on the shelves in an orderly fashion. 书整齐地摆放在书架上。

ordinance
ordinance［'ɔ:dɪnəns］
n. 法令，条例〈同　law, decree〉
例　Passing a red light is a violation of a city's ordinance. 闯红灯是违反城市法令的行为。

organism
organism　［ˈɔːgənɪzəm］
n. 生物体，有机体；微生物〈同 living being〉
例 The sea is full of organisms used as food by fish. 大海里充满了生物，鱼类以此为食。
联 microorganism n. 微生物

orient
orient［'ɔ:rɪənt］
v. ① 确定方向 ② 使熟悉情况 adj. 东方的
解　v. ① to set in a definite position ② to make familiar with or adjusted to facts, principles, or a situation adj. eastern; oriental
例　The Smith family decided to go to the orient country for summer vacation and see the Great Wall. 史密斯一家决定去中国过暑假，还要参观长城。
同　orientation n. 定向；熟悉环境

orientation
orientation［ˌɔ:rɪən'teɪʃən］
n. 定向；介绍性指导〈同 direction, adjustment to surroundings〉
例　Freshman orientation provides the incoming students with an opportunity to learn about their new environment and their place in it. 新生指导为新生提供一个机会来了解新的环境以及他们的角色。

origin
origin　［ˈɒrɪʤɪn］
n. 起源，由来；出身，血统
例 AIDS has its origin in Africa. 艾滋病起源于非洲。

origin
origin［'ɒrɪʤɪn］
n. ① 起源，由来 ② 出身，血统
解　① the fact of originating; rise or derivation ② ancestry
例　The English language has Latin origins. 英语部分起源于拉丁文。

original
original　［əˈrɪʤənəl］
adj. ① 最初的，原始的〈同 first〉
例 This is the original map before the forest was cut down. 这是森林被砍伐之前的原始地图。
例 The students had to write an original short story for class. 学生们得为班级写一部原创短篇小说。
联 originality n. 创意，新奇；originally adv. 本来；最初；originate v. 开始，起源；发明

original
original［ə'rɪʤɪnəl］
n. 原物，原作 adj. ① 最初的，原始的 ② 独创的，新颖的
解　n. a first form from which other forms are made or developed adj. ① preceding all others in time; first ② being or productive of something fresh and unusual
例　The board members decided to discard the original plan in light of the new circumstances. 因为有新的情况发生，董事会成员决定放弃原先的计划。
同　originality n. 创造性，独特性

originality
originality［əˌrɪʤə'næləti］
n. 创意，新奇〈同　novelty, creativity〉
例　Playing the trumpet with dazzling originality, Louis Armstrong dominated jazz for 20 years. 路易斯·阿姆斯特朗以令人眼花缭乱的创意演奏小号，在爵士乐坛独领风骚20年。

originate
originate［ə'rɪʤɪneɪt］
v. 产生；发起，创办〈同 begin, initiate〉
例　Some bad habits originate in adolescence and continue throughout a person's life. 一些坏习惯在青春期形成，伴随整个人生。

originate
originate［ə'rɪʤɪneɪt］
v. 发起，创办
解　to cause or bring into existence
例　The long river originated from one ocean and ended in another. 这条长河发源于一片大海，最后注入另一片大海。

ornament
ornament［'ɔ:nəmənt］
n. 装饰，装饰物〈同 decoration〉
例　A lack of ornament made the room appear quite drab. 房屋缺少装饰物，显得很单调。

orthodox
orthodox［'ɔ:θədɒks］
adj. 正统的；传统的〈同 traditional〉
例　She is a cancer sufferer who has rejected orthodox medicine and turned instead to acupuncture and other forms of alternative medicine. 她是一个癌症患者，她拒绝正统医疗，求助于针灸等其他形式的替代疗法。

ostensible
ostensible［ɒs'tensəbəl; -sɪbəl］
adj. 表面上的，伪装的
解　according to appearances; apparent; pretended
例　My ostensible purpose for going to the library was to study, but I was really reading magazines. 我去图书馆表面上是为了学习，但实际上是看杂志。

ostentatious
ostentatious［ˌɒsten'teiʃəs］
adj. 做作的，虚荣的，炫耀的
解　done for unnecessary display; liking to attract notice; showy
例　The real hero is modest, never ostentatious. 真正的英雄很谦逊，从来不炫耀。
同　ostentation n. 夸示，炫耀

otherwise
otherwise　［ˈʌðəwaɪz］
adv./conj. 另外，否则〈同 under different conditions〉
例 Come early; otherwise you may not get a seat. 早点来，否则你可能找不到座位。

oust
oust［aʊst］
vt. 驱逐；赶走〈同　eject, expel〉
例　The police moved with alacrity to oust the disorderly mobs. 警察迅速赶来驱逐骚乱的暴民。

outbreak
outbreak［'aʊtbreɪk］
n. 发作；爆发〈同 beginning, eruption〉
例　Doctors are warning us about a possible outbreak of the flu. 医生提醒我们可能会爆发流感。

outcast
outcast［'aʊtkɑ:st; (US)-kæst］
n. 被社会遗弃者
解　a person or animal cast out from home and friends
例　The criminal was an outcast from society. 这名罪犯是一个被社会遗弃的人。

outcome
outcome　［ˈaʊtkʌm］
n. 后果，成果〈同 result〉
例 The newspaper reported the outcome of the Board meeting. 报纸报道了董事会会议的成果。

outcry
outcry［'aʊtkraɪ］
n. 大声疾呼；强烈抗议〈同　protest, shout〉
例　An outcry for more practical instruction arose among the students and educators. 学生和教育工作者发出了要求更多实践教学的强烈呼声。

outdated
outdated［ˌaʊt'deɪtɪd］
adj. 过时的〈同　old, outmoded〉
例　Technology has moved so fast that new software tends to get outdated in only a couple of years. 技术变化得如此迅速，仅仅几年时间，新软件就会过时。

outermost
outermost［'aʊtəməʊst］
adj. 最外边的，离中心最远的〈同　farmost, utmost〉
例　The outermost part of this fruit is hard but once you take it off, the fruit is soft and sweet. 这种水果最外面的部分很硬，但剥去外面的部分后，里面的果肉软糯香甜。

outfit
outfit［'aʊtfɪt］
n. 服装〈同　costume, clothes〉
例　The model was wearing a cute outfit. 那名模特穿着一套非常可爱的服装。
vt. 配备，装备〈同　equip, furnish〉
例　He outfitted his jeep with rooflights. 他为自己的吉普车配备了车厢顶灯。

outgoing
outgoing［'aʊtgəʊɪŋ］
adj. 好交际的，外向的〈同　sociable, extroverted〉
例　Sales representatives need to be outgoing and dynamic. 销售代表需要外向而有活力。

outgoing
outgoing［'aʊtɡəʊɪŋ］
adj. ① 即将离职的 ② 对人友好的
解　① going out or away ② friendly and sociable; somewhat extroverted; at ease in talking to others
例　She was very outgoing and would always introduce herself to people she did not know. 她对人十分友好，总是向不认识的人介绍自己。

outgrow
outgrow［ˌaʊt'grəʊ］
vt. 生长速度超过，长得比…快〈同　grow beyond〉
例　By age 16, John had outgrown his elder brother. 约翰在16岁的时候，身高就超过了他哥哥。

outing
outing［'aʊtɪŋ］

例　The father took his two sons on an outing as a male bonding experience. 父亲带着两个儿子去郊游，这是一种兄弟情谊般的旅行经历。

outlandish
outlandish［aʊt'lændɪʃ］
adj. 异国风味的；奇怪的，古怪的
解　looking or sounding odd, strange or foreign
例　He was known for asking outlandish questions that raised everyone's eyebrows. 大家都知道他喜欢问一些让人瞠目的古怪问题。

outlast
outlast［ˌaʊt'lɑ:st; (US)-'læst］
vt. 比…长久，比…活得长〈同　outlive〉
例　Our company outlasted many others through the economic crisis. 我们公司平安渡过了经济危机，比其他公司存在的时间都要长。

outlet
outlet　［ˈaʊtlet］

例 A chimney is an outlet for smoke from a fireplace. 烟囱是壁炉向外排烟的出口。
记 out（出）+let（让）→让…排出→出口

outlet

例　This lake's outlet is a stream that flows into the ocean. 这个湖的出口是一条流入大海的小溪。

outline

例 The police outlined the shape of the murder victim on the street with chalk. 警方用粉笔在街道上画出谋杀案受害者的轮廓。

outline
outline［'aʊtlaɪn］
n. 大纲，轮廓 v. 画轮廓，打草图
解　n. a summary of the main points of an argument or theory v. to draw the outer line of
例　The English teacher told the students that they should write an outline before they wrote an essay in order to organize their thoughts and ideas clearly. 这位英语老师告诉学生，在写文章之前要先拟一个提纲，这样就能更清晰地组织思路和想法。

例　The crank telephone was outmoded long ago. 转动曲柄电话机很早以前就已经过时了。

outrage

例　The king was outraged by the man's insult and ordered that his head be cut off. 国王被那个人的辱骂激怒，于是下令砍掉他的脑袋。

例　A mortgage enables a person to buy property without paying for it outright; thus more people are able to enjoy owning a house. 抵押贷款使一个人无需支付全款便可购买房产；因此，越来越多的人可以拥有一套房子。

例　The economic reform overhauled the previous system and implanted a more open economy. 这次的经济改革全面审视了以前的制度，重新引入了一个更加开放的经济体系。

例　The judge overturned his decision with the introduction of new evidence. 由于出现了新证据，法官推翻了他的判决。

overturn
overturn［ˌəʊvə'tɜ:n］
v. ① 打翻；（使）翻过来；（使）倒转 ② 颠覆；打倒
解　① to cause to turn over or capsize; upset ② to cause the ruin or destruction of; overthrow
例　The high waves caused by the rainstorm overturned the small boat and the passengers had to swim to shore. 暴风雨引起的巨浪掀翻了小船，船上的乘客不得不游到岸边。

例　Government troops have overwhelmed the rebels. 政府军镇压了叛乱者。

overwhelm

例　The peak of the mountain is covered with snow. 山顶覆盖着雪。

pebble［'pebəl］

例　Steve used the hammer to smash the stone into pebbles. 史蒂夫用锤子把石头砸成石子。

peck
peck［pek］
v. 啄，啄食〈同　pick〉
例　Woodpeckers pecked wood looking for the pest. 啄木鸟啄木头来寻找害虫。

peculiar
peculiar　［pɪˈkjuːlɪə(r)］
adj. ①（人、地点、时间等）特有的，专有的〈同 special〉
例 I was longing to get home—a desire peculiar to all people who travel for quite a long time. 我盼望着回家——这是所有在外漂泊已久的人特有的一种渴望。
例 This peculiar behavior puzzles everyone who knows him. 他奇怪的行为让所有认识他的人迷惑不解。
记 pec（来自pecus，意为“牛”，牛是私有财产，所以是特有的)+uliar→特有的，专有的
联 peculiarity n. 特性；怪癖

peculiarity
peculiarity［pɪˌkju:lɪ'ærəti］
n. 特性，怪癖〈同　eccentricity, oddness〉
例　She could not handle his peculiarity of touching his nose in public. 她解决不了他在公众面前摸鼻子的怪癖。

pedagogy［'pedəgɒʤi］
n. 教育学，教学法〈同　education, teaching〉
例　The university evaluated the quality of its pedagogy and curriculum every year. 这所大学每年都会评估其教学法和课程安排的质量。

pedagogy
pedagogy［'pedəɡɒɡi］
n. 教育学，教学法
解　the profession of a teacher; activities that impart knowledge
例　The English teacher had published her doctoral thesis on the pedagogy of languages. 英语老师出版了她关于语言教学法的博士论文。
近　pediatrics n. 儿科学；pedantic adj. 迂腐的，学究气的；pedantry n. 假装学者，卖弄学问；pedant n. 书呆子，迂腐之人

例　The philanthropic association donated money to worthy causes. 慈善协会对值得捐助的事业捐助资金。

近　misanthrope n. 厌世者，愤世嫉俗者

philanthropy
philanthropy［fɪ'lænθrəpi］
n. 仁慈，博爱
解　love of humanity shown by practical kindness and helpfulness
例　Tom showed a great deal of philanthropy by volunteering to organize the charity event. 汤姆自愿组织慈善活动，展现了他的博爱之情。

philatelist
philatelist［fɪ'lætəlɪst］
n. 集邮家
解　stamp-collector
例　When she heard the value of the Penny Black stamp, Phyllis was inspired to become a philatelist. 菲莉斯听说了黑便士邮票（英国1840年发行的面值1便士的黑色邮票）的价值之后，受到激发成为了集邮爱好者。
同　philately n. 集邮

adj. ①【电】阳极的
例 An electric current can consist of charges that are positive, negative, or both. 电流中可能包含正电荷、负电荷，或两种电荷同时存在。
例 Nodding one's head is a positive response. 点头是表示肯定的回答。
记 posit（肯定）+ ive→肯定的

pretension［prɪ'ten∫ən］
n. 要求；自命；自称〈同　claim; assertion〉
例　His pretension that he was innocent did not fool any one. 他自称自己是无辜的，但这骗不了任何人。

pretentious
pretentious［prɪ'tenʃəs］
adj. 自负的，夸耀的；自抬身价的
解　making claims to excellence or importance
例　The pretentious artist claimed his paintings had made millions even when they had not earned him a single penny. 这位艺术家自抬身价，声称他的画作已经给他带来了数百万元的收入，而实际上它们没有为他赚来分文。
同　pretension n. 自命不凡；pretense n. 借口；虚假，自负
构　pre (=before) + tent (=to stretch) + ious

pretext［'pri:tekst］

propriety
propriety［prə'praɪəti］
n. ① （常用作复）礼节，礼貌 ② 适当
解　① the usages and customs of polite society ② the quality of proper; appropriateness
例　Generally speaking, British society has a greater sense of proprieties than American society. 总体来说，英国社会比美国社会更注重礼节。

prosecute［'prɒsɪkju:t］
vt. 对…起诉；告发〈同　sue, indict〉
例　The district attorney refused to prosecute the case because of a lack of evidence. 由于缺乏证据，地方检察官拒绝审理这个案子。

prosecute
prosecute［'prɒsɪkju:t］
v. 告发，检举

构　pro (=before) + secut (=to follow) + e

prospect　［prəˈspekt; (US)ˈprɒspekt］

例 He spends the summers prospecting in the mountains. 他每年夏天都在山中勘探。
