radioactive
radioactive　［ˌreɪdɪəʊˈæktɪv］
adj. 放射性的；有辐射能的
例 Radium, uranium, and thorium are radioactive metallic elements. 镭、铀和钍都属于放射性金属元素。

radioactive
radioactive［ˌreɪdɪəʊ'æktɪv］
adj. 放射性的，辐射性的
解　of or exhibiting radioactivity
例　Radium, uranium, and thorium are radioactive metallic elements. 镭、铀和钍都属于放射性金属元素。

radius
radius　［ˈreɪdɪəs］
n. 半径；范围
例 The explosion was heard within a radius of four miles. 在四英里的范围内都能听到这个爆炸声。

raft
raft［rɑ:ft; (US)ræft］
n. 筏，救生艇
例　We used a raft to cross the river because it was too dangerous to swim. 我们用筏子渡河，因为游泳过河太危险了。

rage
rage［reɪʤ］
n. ① 时尚，风靡一时的事物〈同 fashion, vogue〉
例　By the 1930's, jazz music was the rage. 到20世纪30年代，爵士乐风靡一时。
例　I was frightened because I had never seen him in such a rage before. 我从来都没有看到他这么愤怒过，这让我很害怕。

ragged
ragged［'rægɪd］
adj. 褴褛的，破烂的〈同　torn, worn〉
例　The dress became ragged after the dogs played with it. 小狗们拿那条裙子玩，结果那条裙子变得破烂不堪。

ragtime
ragtime［'rægtaɪm］
n. 拉格泰姆音乐（或舞蹈）（一种源于美国黑人音乐的早期爵士乐）
例　Ragtime is a style of jazz music notable for its rhythm and melody. 拉格泰姆音乐是爵士乐的一种，以其节奏和旋律而著名。

raid
raid［reɪd］
n. 袭击〈同 invasion, attack〉
例　Thousands were killed in the air raids on London. 伦敦遭到空袭，数千人死亡。

rail
rail　［reɪl］
n. 轨道；铁路
例 Rail passengers are complaining about the recent increase in rail fares. 铁路乘客在抱怨最近铁路票价上涨的事。
v. 责备；抱怨〈同 complain〉
例 He railed against the injustices of the system. 他抱怨体制的不公。
联 railroad n. 铁路；rail-motor adj. 铁路公路联运的；railbus n. 有轨（公共）汽车；railcar n. 铁路车；有轨车

rainfall
rainfall［'reɪnfɔ:l］
n. 降雨；降雨量
例　The constant rainfall created flooding in many parts of the city. 持续降雨在那座城市的许多地方造成了洪水。

raise
raise　［reɪz］
vt. ① 举起；增长〈同 lift up〉
例 Children in school raise their hands to answer a question. 在学校里，孩子们举手回答问题。
例 She was raised by her aunt in London. 她是由姑姑在伦敦养大的。
例 I raised a loan for my sister's wedding. 我为姐姐的婚礼借了一笔钱。

rally
rally［'ræli］
v. 召集，集合；恢复〈同 unite, combine〉
例　We rallied together to save our leader from prison. 我们团结起来，把首领从监狱里救出来。

rampant
rampant［'ræmpənt］
adj. 蔓生的，猖獗的〈同　uncontrolled, unruly〉
例　The rampant weeds in the garden killed all the flowers which had been planted in the spring. 花园内猖獗的杂草害死了所有春天种下的花。

rancher
rancher［'rɑ:ntʃə(r); 'ræn-］
n. 大农场经营者；牧场工人
例　The rancher raised horses for a living. 那位牧场主以养马为生。

random
random［'rændəm］
adj. 任意的，随便的〈同 haphazard〉
例　The police were stopping cars at random and checking their brakes. 警察随机拦下汽车，检查其刹车是否有问题。

range
range　［reɪnʤ］
n. 行列；范围〈同 limit〉
例 The temperature range was between eight and twelve degrees. 温度范围在8度至12度之间。

rare
rare　［rɛə(r)］
adj. 稀有的〈同 scarce〉
例 Many gardeners have become interested in the propagation of rare seeds, in order to keep old strains from disappearing. 为了避免古老植物品种的消失，许多园艺师开始对稀有种子的繁殖感兴趣。
联 rarefy vt. 使稀少，使稀薄；vi. 变得稀少；rarely adv. 很少地，罕有地

rather
rather　［ˈrɑːðə; (US)ˈræðər］
adv. ① 宁愿，宁可〈同 more readily〉
例 I would rather go today than tomorrow. 我更愿意今天去而不是明天去。
例 The dress was rather more expensive than I was expecting it would be, so I didn't buy it. 那条裙子的价格比我预期的高多了，所以我没买。

ratify
ratify［'rætɪfaɪ］
vt. 批准〈同　endorse, approve〉
例　All parties ratified the peace treaty. 各方均批准了和平条约。

ratio
ratio　［ˈreɪʃɪəʊ］
n. 比，比率
例 The ratio of 10 to 3 is written as 10:3. 10比3，写出来就是10:3。

ration
ration［'ræ∫ən］
n. 定量，配给量〈同　allotment, allowance〉
例　Virtually every Iraqi family receives a food ration, but it's hardly enough and malnutrition is spreading. 几乎每一个伊拉克家庭都得到了食物配给，但这根本不够，营养不良正在人群中蔓延。
vt. 定量配给〈同　allot, distribute〉
例　He only had one bottle of water for the next two days, so he had to ration it to a sip every couple of hours. 未来两天，他只有两瓶水，所以他不得不每几个小时定量喝一小口。

rational
rational　［ˈræʃənəl］
adj. 理性的；合理的〈同 logical〉
例 It isn't rational to walk barefoot in the snow. 光着脚在雪中走是不理性的。
记 ration（理性）+ al→理性的；合理的
联 rationale n. 基本原理；rationality n. 合理性；rationalize v.（使）合理化

rattle
rattle［'rætəl］
n. 拨浪鼓；格格声
例　The baby enjoyed making sounds with the rattle. 那个婴儿喜欢用拨浪鼓弄出声音。

raucous
raucous［'rɔ:kəs］
adj. 沙哑的；喧嚣的〈同　loud, boisterous〉
例　We went to a raucous party last night and were exhausted when we went back home. 我们昨晚去参加了一场喧嚣嘈杂的聚会，回到家的时候已经筋疲力尽了。

ravine
ravine［rə'vi:n］
n. 沟壑，峡谷〈同　gorge〉
例　The ravine's current was too dangerous to swim in. 这条溪谷的水流太危险了，不适合游泳。

raw
raw　［rɔː］
adj. 生的，未加工的〈同 uncooked〉
例 Raw milk has not been pasteurized. 生鲜牛奶没有经过巴氏灭菌。

ray
ray［reɪ］
n. 光线〈同 beam, light〉
例　A ray of light came in through the hole in the wall. 一缕光从墙洞里穿过。

raze
raze［reɪz］
vt. 夷为平地〈同　demolish, topple〉
例　The violent hurricane razed much of the coastal city. 强烈的飓风把这个滨海城市的大部分地区夷为平地。

razor
razor［'reɪzə(r)］
n. 剃刀
例　He used a razor to shave every morning. 他每天早上都用刮胡刀刮胡子。

react
react　［riːˈækt］
v.（使）起反应，（使）起作用〈同 take effect〉
例 Many people react badly to penicillin. 许多人注射青霉素会有不良反应。
联 reaction n. 反应；反作用

reactant
reactant［ri:'æktənt］
n. 反应剂，反应物
解　a chemical substance that is present at the start of a chemical reaction
例　The chemistry student added the reactant into the liquid to start the experiment. 学化学的学生把反应剂加入液体里，开始了实验。
同　react v. 反应；reaction n. 反应

reactionary
reactionary［ri: 'ækʃənəri］
n. 反动分子，保守分子 adj. 保守的，反动的
解　n. an opponent of progress or liberalism
adj. extremely conservative
例　The reactionaries colluded in a conspiracy to prevent the liberal candidate from being elected president. 反动分子串通一气，阴谋阻止自由党候选人被选为总统。

readily
readily［'redɪli］
adv. 容易地；欣然地，乐意地〈同 easily, willingly〉
例　These snakes can be readily identified. 这些蛇一眼就能辨别出来。

realistic
realistic［ˌrɪə'lɪstɪk］
adj. 现实（主义 ）的〈同 pragmatic〉
例　Set realistic goals and work hard to achieve them. 设定几个现实的目标，再努力去实现它们。

realization
realization［ˌrɪəlaɪ'zeɪʃən］
n. 实现；意识〈同 fulfillment, awareness〉
例　He finally bought his own house. That was the realization of his dream. 他终于买了一套属于自己的房子，这让他梦想成真。

realm
realm　［relm］
n. 王国；领域〈同 kingdom〉
例 Lu Xun is well-known worldwide in the realm of literature. 鲁迅在文学界全球知名。

reap
reap［ri:p］
vt. 收割，收获；获得〈同 harvest, gain〉
例　Farmers sow in the spring and reap in the fall. 农民在春天播种，秋天收割。

rear
rear　［rɪə(r)］
vt. 培养，饲养〈同 raise〉
例 The mother swallow reared her children until they could fly on their own. 燕子妈妈会一直抚养孩子，直到它们能够独立飞行。
n. 后面〈同 back〉
例 The rear of the bus is the most uncomfortable part. 公交车后排座位是最不舒服的地方。

reasonable
reasonable　［ˈriːzənəbəl］
adj. 合理的；讲道理的，通情达理的〈同 sensible〉
例 If you tell him what happened I'm sure he'll understand—he's a reasonable man. 如果你告诉他发生了什么，我敢肯定他会理解的——他是个通情达理的人。

rebel
rebel
例 The prime minister left the capital after learning that the rebels were planning an imminent attack. 首相在得知反叛者正在预谋发动的袭击即将来临之后，便离开了首都。
例 The people rebelled when bread prices tripled again. 当面包价格再次涨至三倍时，人们便开始造反。
联 rebellion n. 谋反，叛乱；rebellious adj. 造反的，反叛的

rebel
rebel［ri'bel］v. 造反，反抗［'rebəl］ n. 反叛者
解　v. to break with established customs
n. a person who takes part in a rebellion in the hopes of improving conditions
例　It is natural for teenagers to rebel against their parents. 反抗父母是青少年的天性。

rebellion
rebellion［rɪ'beljən］
n. 叛乱
解　organized opposition to authority; a conflict in which one faction tries to wrest control from another
例　The rebellion overthrew the king from his throne. 这场叛乱推翻了国王的统治。

rebuke
rebuke［rɪ'bju:k］
vt. 斥责，谴责〈同　admonish, scold〉
例　The mother rebuked the child for getting on the stranger's car. 那位妈妈因为孩子上了陌生人的车而责备了他。

recalcitrant
recalcitrant［rɪ'kælsɪtrənt］
adj. 固执的，顽抗的
解　marked by stubborn resistance to authority
例　The recalcitrant solider disobeyed his orders. 这名顽抗的士兵违抗了他的命令。
同　recalcitrance n. 固执，顽抗

recall
recall　［rɪˈkɔːl］
vt. 回忆起；记得〈同 remember〉
例 The victim was asked to recall what happened to him the day he was robbed. 受害者被要求回忆自己被抢当天都发生了什么。

recapitulation
recapitulation［ˌri:kəpɪtjʊ'leɪʃən］
n. 扼要重述
解　a summary that repeats the substance of a longer discussion
例　The official 100-page report ended with a one-page recapitulation of the key points. 这份100页的官方报告的最后一页是要点概括。

recede
recede［rɪ'si:d］
v. ① 倒退，后退 ② 撤回，撤退
解　① to move back and away from ② to retreat
例　We watched the harbor recede from view as our ship headed out to sea. 随着轮船驶入大海，码头渐渐从我们的视线中消失。
近　rescind v. 废除，取消
构　re (=back) + ced (=to go) + e

receipt
receipt　［rɪˈsiːt］
n. ① 收据
例 I need all your receipts so that I can verify the bill for the work. 我需要你的所有收据，这样我就可以核对公费账单了。
例 On receipt of the news he went home. 一收到这个消息，他就回家了。
记 来自receive（v. 收到）
联 receptive adj. 善于接受的，能接纳的；recipient n. 接受者

receptacle
receptacle［rɪ'septəkəl］
n. 容器；储藏所，仓库〈同　container, holder〉
例　The goods were placed in large receptacles before they were placed on the cargo ship. 货物被装上货轮之前，存放在巨大的仓库里。

reception
reception　［rɪˈsepʃən］
n. ① 接待；招待会；欢迎会
例 Our school gave a reception for our new principal. 我们学校为新任校长举办了一场欢迎会。
例 The reception was poor because we were so far from the transmitter. 信号接收不良，因为我们离发射机太远了。
联 receptionist n. 接待员

receptive
receptive［rɪ'septɪv］
adj. 善于接受的，能接纳的〈同　open-minded, accepting〉
例　I was confident that after Dad had eaten a good meal, he would be in a more receptive mood to my request for the use of the car. 我相信，爸爸在吃完一顿美餐之后，就更容易接受我用一下汽车的请求。

recess
recess［rɪ'ses］
n. ① 壁凹 （墙上装架子、柜子等凹处）② 休息；休息、停顿等持续的时间
解　① a space set back or indented ② a pause from doing something (as work) ; the period of such cessation
例　During school recess, the children like to go to the playground and play games. 课间休息时，孩子们喜欢去操场上玩耍。

recession
recession［rɪ'seʃən］
n. 萧条时期，（经济）衰退〈同 depression〉
例　Slow growth in the early 1900's, linked with rising unemployment, led many experts to declare a recession. 20世纪头十年，经济增长放缓，加上失业率上升，使许多专家宣布经济进入衰退期。

recipe
recipe［'resɪpi］
n. 食谱；处方〈同 formula, instructions〉
例　I have a book full of recipes for curry. 我有一本做咖喱饭菜的食谱。

reciprocal
reciprocal［rɪ'sɪprəkəl］
adj. 相应的；相互的〈同 in return, mutual〉
例　She gave me a present, but she expected no reciprocal gift from me. 她给了我一件礼物，但是她不期望我回赠她。

recital
recital［rɪ'saɪtəl］
n. ① 朗诵，背诵 ② 独奏会，独唱会
解　① a reciting ② a musical entertainment, given usually by a single performer
例　My music teacher will give a piano recital Tuesday afternoon. 周二下午，我的音乐老师将举办一场钢琴独奏会。
同　recite v. 背诵；recitation n. 背诵

reckless
reckless［'reklɪs］
adj. 轻率的，鲁莽的〈同 careless〉
例　Mark had his license suspended for reckless driving. 马克因为野蛮驾驶被吊销驾照。

reckon
reckon［'rekən］
vt. 约略地计算；估计，猜想〈同 compute, guess〉
例　John was absent for the first time, so the teacher reckoned he was sick. 约翰第一次缺勤，老师估计他是生病了。

reclaim
reclaim［rɪ'kleɪm］
vt. 开垦；要求归还，收回
例　The Netherlands has reclaimed large tracts of land from the sea. 荷兰收回了海上的大片领土。

recluse
recluse［rɪ'klu:s］
n. 隐士 adj. 隐居的
解　n. one who lives in solitude adj. withdrawn from society; seeking solitude
例　The recluse lived in the woods, eating the plants from his garden and the meat of animals he hunted. 这个隐士居住在森林里，以自己菜园中种植的植物和狩猎所得的肉类为食。
同　reclusive adj. 隐遁的，隐居的
构　re (=back) + clus (=to shut) + e

recognize
recognize［'rekəgnaɪz］

例　I'm sure I would recognize you in that disguise. 我确信你伪装成那样我也能认出你。
例　The scientist was recognized by the president for her outstanding achievements. 那位科学家做出了杰出的贡献，受到总统的表彰。

例　She recoiled when she heard the cost of the operation. 听到手术费用的数目之后，她退缩了。

recollection

例　After the brain surgery, his recollection was not very good. 经过脑部手术之后，他的记忆变得不是很好。

recommend

reconcile

例　Friends managed to reconcile him with his wife after years of estrangement. 他和妻子多年分居，朋友们想方设法让他们重归于好了。

reconstruct

例　Without the original designs, it was impossible to reconstruct the building exactly as before. 如果没有当初的设计图，要想完全按照以前的样子对这栋建筑进行重建是不可能的。

recount
recount［rɪ'kaʊnt］
vt. 叙述，描写〈同　narrate, depict〉
例　The father recounted a story to his child before saying good night. 爸爸在道晚安之前，给他的孩子讲了一个故事。

recreation
recreation［ˌrekrɪ'eɪʃən］
n. 消遣，娱乐〈同 pastime, amusement〉
例　For recreation, I like to go hiking and camping. 在娱乐方面，我喜欢徒步旅行和露营。

recriminate
recriminate［rɪ'krɪmɪneɪt］
v. 反责，反控
解　to return an accusation against someone
例　The company defended that it had not infringed on any trademarks and recriminated the newspaper of libel. 这家公司辩称没有侵犯任何商标权，并反责报纸诬陷。

recruit
recruit［rɪ'kru:t］
vt. 征兵，征募；补充〈同 enlist, enroll〉
例　We have to recruit seven more people to start the work. 我们还需要招募七个人来启动这个工作。

rectify
rectify［'rektɪfaɪ］

例　Before you hand in your homework, you should rectify all the mistakes. 交家庭作业之前，你应该好好检查错误。

recur
recur［rɪ'kɜ:(r)］
vi. 重现，再来；复发〈同 reappear〉
例　Memories of my first meeting with her recur on and off. 我第一次和她相遇的回忆不断重现。

recurrent
recurrent［rɪ'kʌrənt］
adj. 反复出现的
解　occurring again and again
例　We brought the car to a mechanic because the overheating engine was a recurrent problem. 由于发动机过热的毛病反复出现，于是我们把车送到机械师那里修理。

例　Bill had already bought paper plates, so our purchase of paper plates was redundant. 比尔已经买了纸板，所以我们再买纸板就多余了。

reel

n. 卷轴
例　The fish was so big that his fishing rod and reel broke. 那条鱼太大了，他的鱼竿和卷轴都断了。

refer

例 Let's refer the dispute to the manager. 我们把争议提交给经理吧。

refined
refined　［rɪˈfaɪnd］
adj. ① 优雅的〈同 elegant〉
例 A photographer encouraged her to become a model because of her slim figure and refined features. 一位摄影师鼓励她成为一名模特，因为她身材苗条，气质优雅。
例 To obtain pure lead, the lead ore is mined, then smelted, and finally refined. 为了获得纯铅，需要对铅矿进行开采，接着是冶炼，并在最后进行精炼。
记 来自refine（vt. 提纯，精炼）；re（再）+ fin（完成）+ ed→做完后还反复做→精制的
联 refinement n.（言谈、举止等的）文雅，精巧；refinery n. 精炼厂

reflect
reflect［rɪ'flekt］
v. ① 反射 ② 仔细考虑
解　① to turn back or throw back (light, heat, sound, etc. ) ② to think carefully
例　Take time to reflect before making a decision. 在作决定之前，花点时间思考一下。
同　reflection n. 反射；思考；reflective adj. 深思熟虑的；反射的

reflection
reflection　［rɪˈflekʃən］
n. 反映〈同 expression〉
例 Your tone of voice is a reflection of your attitude. 你的语调反映了你的态度。
记 re（反）+ flect（弯曲）+ ion→弯曲反射回来→反映

refraction［rɪ'fræk∫ən］
n. 折光，折射〈同　deflection〉
例　When you look at a stick inserted in water, it looks bent because of the refraction of the light by the water. 当你看一根插在水里的棍子时，它看起来像是弯的，这是因为水对光的折射。

refractory
refractory［rɪ'fræktəri］
adj. ① 倔强的，难驾驭的 ② （病）难治的
解　① resisting control, discipline, etc., willful; stubborn ② not yielding to treatment
例　The refractory child would not sit still and drove his babysitter crazy. 这个不听话的小孩不愿安静地坐着，都快把保姆逼疯了。
构　re (=again) + fract (=to break) + ory

例 The teacher was very rigid in his ideas about class attendance. 这位老师在课堂出勤率的问题上非常严格。
联 rigidly adv. 坚硬地；严格地

rigidity
rigidity［rə'ʤɪdəti］
n. 僵化，死板〈同　stiffness〉
例　The drawback of institutionalization is that it can turn into a kind of organizational rigidity that produces paralysis. 制度化的缺点是，它可能变成某种组织僵化，进而造成瘫痪。

rigorous
rigorous［'rɪgərəs］
adj. 严格的〈同 stringent, strict〉
例　Along with the other physical sciences, meteorology has developed in the past three centuries from myth and folklore to rigorous observation, computation, and analysis. 同其他物理科学一起，气象学在过去的三个世纪中，从神话和民间传说发展到严密的观察、计算和分析。

rim
rim［rɪm］
n. 边缘〈同 edge〉
例　The rim of my coffee cup is chipped. 我的咖啡杯的边缘破了。

rinse［rɪns］

例　The cook rinsed the vegetables before cutting them to make the salad. 厨师先清洗蔬菜，然后把它们切碎来制作沙拉。

例 The time is ripe to invest in new technology. 投资新技术的时机已经成熟。

例　They go through the ritual of locking all doors and windows before going to bed. 睡觉之前，他们按照惯例把所有的门窗都锁好。

rival　［ˈraɪvəl］
vt. 比得上，与…相匹敌
例 Thomas Jefferson's achievements as an architect rival his contributions as a politician. 托马斯·杰斐逊作为一名建筑师所取得的成就，与作为一名政治家所作的贡献不相上下。
adj. 竞争的〈同 competitive〉
例 The rival supermarkets both cut their prices to attract customers. 两家相互竞争的超市均通过降价来吸引顾客。
n. 竞争者；匹敌者〈同 competitor〉
例 The two managers were rivals for the same position. 两位经理是争夺同一个职位的竞争者。
联 rivalry n. 竞争；敌对状态

例 Chromium is a comparatively scarce element, occurring in nature only in compounds. 铬是一种相对稀有的元素，在自然状态下只会出现在化合物中。
记 注意不要和scare（惊恐）相混
联 scarcely adv. 几乎不，简直没有；scarcity n. 缺乏，不足

shed
shed　［ʃed］
vt. ① 脱落，蜕〈同 fall off〉
例 Deciduous trees shed all or nearly all of their leaves each year. 每年，落叶阔木的所有叶子或者几乎所有叶子都会掉光。
例 She shed a few tears at her daughter's wedding. 她在女儿的婚礼上流下了眼泪。

sheer
sheer［ʃɪə(r)］
adj. ① 陡峭的〈同 steep〉
例　From the top of the wall it was a sheer drop of 100 feet to the water below. 从墙顶到水面有100英尺的垂直落差。
例　Don't believe him; his words are sheer nonsense. 别相信他，他的话都是一派胡言。

sheet
sheet　［ʃiːt］
n. ①（一）片，（一）张，薄片〈同 piece, layer〉
例 The application form has several sheets of paper. 申请表有几页纸。
例 One of the things I like about staying in hotels is that they put clean sheets on the bed every day. 关于住酒店，我比较喜欢的一件事就是他们每天都会换干净的床单。

shell
shell　［ʃel］
n. 壳〈同 husk〉
例 Oysters, turtles, and beetles all have shells. 牡蛎、乌龟和甲虫都有壳。
联 eggshell n. 蛋壳；shellfish n. 贝类水生动物

shelter
shelter　［ˈʃeltə(r)］
n. 掩蔽处；庇护所〈同 asylum〉
例 Everyone looked for shelter from the blazing sun. 每个人都在寻找阴凉儿以躲避炎炎烈日。
vt. 掩蔽〈同 protect〉
例 The mother bird sheltered her chicks from the cold. 鸟妈妈保护幼鸟不受寒冷的侵袭。
联 sheltered adj. 遮蔽的

shepherd
shepherd［'ʃepəd］
n. 牧羊人；牧羊犬
例　The shepherd led the sheep back home. 牧羊人赶着羊回家了。

shield
shield　［ʃiːld］
v. 庇护，保护〈同 protect〉
例 Politicians often shield criminals for their self-interest. 政客们经常出于自身利益包庇罪犯。
n. 盾；保护物
例 The shield protects your eyes from damage. 这个护眼罩可以保护你的眼睛不受伤害。
记 要牢记shield的原始意义是“盾”，其他意义都由此引申而来
联 windshield n. 挡风玻璃

shift
shift　［ʃɪft］
v. 移动，改变位置或方向〈同 change〉
例 When the wind shifted from south to north, it began to get cold. 当南风变成北风时，天气就开始变冷了。
n. ① 轮班〈同 turn〉
例 She is on the night shift this week. 她这周上夜班。
例 The shift in the wind was helpful to the sailors. 风向的变化对水手们很有帮助。
联 shifting adj. 变动的；运动的；shifty adj. 诡诈的，不老实的

shipment
shipment［'ʃɪpmənt］
n. 装运；装载的货物
例　The company sent the shipment of furniture directly to my house. 公司直接装上家具，送到我家。

shiver
shiver［'∫ɪvə(r)］
n./v. 颤抖〈同　quiver, tremble〉
例　She shivered in the cold air. 她在寒风中瑟瑟发抖。

shock
shock　［ʃɒk］
n. 震动，震惊；打击〈同 tremble〉
例 Her mother's death was a great shock. It was so unexpected. 母亲的离世对她是个沉重的打击。一切来得太突然了。
vt. 震惊，激怒〈同 stun〉
例 The news of Anne's accident shocked me. 安妮出车祸的消息让我震惊。
联 shocking adj. 骇人听闻的；shocked adj. 震惊的，震撼的

shortcut
shortcut［'∫ɔ:tkʌt］
n. 捷径〈同　a direct route〉
例　They took a shortcut to get to the airport faster. 为了更快地到达机场，他们抄了一条近路。

shot
shot［ʃɒt］
n. ① 照相，相片〈同 photograph〉
例　The photographer took many shots of the actor arriving at the event. 摄影师拍摄了许多演员到达现场的照片。
例　The hunter's shot was too high and the rabbit escaped. 猎人射击位置过高，兔子跑了。

shower
shower　［ˈʃaʊə(r)］
n. 阵雨；淋浴
例 Mary turned off the shower and dried herself with a towel. 玛丽关上淋浴，用毛巾把身上擦干。

shrewd
shrewd［ʃru:d］
adj. 精明的〈同 clever, sharp〉
例　The shrewd student received the highest score in the class. 这个聪明的学生得到了全班最高分。

shriek
shriek［∫ri:k］
v. 尖声叫喊〈同　scream〉
例　She shrieked at the sight of the mouse. 她一看到老鼠便尖叫起来。
n. 尖叫，尖声
例　We heard the shrieks from next door and called the police. 我们听到了隔壁的尖叫声，然后报了警。

shrink
shrink　［ʃrɪŋk］
vi. 收缩，缩小〈同 contract〉
例 Because my shirt had shrunk, I gave it to my younger cousin. 我的衬衣缩水了，所以我把它送给了我堂弟。
联 shrinkage n. 收缩

shrivel
shrivel［'∫rɪvəl］
v.（使）枯萎〈同　wither, shrink〉
例　She ought to pick the lettuce before it shrivels and dies. 她应该在莴苣枯死之前把它摘走。

shrub
shrub［∫rʌb］
n. 灌木；灌木丛〈同　bush〉
例　Shrubs can make a cute border around the lawn but they do not provide any privacy because of their low height. 灌木可以沿草坪形成一个可爱的边界，但它们无法保证任何私密性，因为它们太矮了。

shrug
shrug［ʃrʌg］
n./v. 耸肩
例　She did not care what brand toothpaste they bought and shrugged her shoulders. 她不在乎他们买了什么牌子的牙膏，只是耸了耸肩。

shuffle
shuffle［'∫ʌfəl］
vt. 洗牌〈同　disorder, jumble〉
例　She shuffled the deck at the beginning of every new card game. 每一局扑克牌开始之前，她都要洗牌。

shutter
shutter［'ʃʌtə(r)］
n. 百叶窗
例　Put the windows down and close the shutters before the storm comes. 暴风雨来临之前把窗户放下来，百叶窗关上。

shuttle
shuttle［'ʃʌtəl］
n. 往返汽车、列车等（穿梭往返固定线路的运输工具）
例　The student took a shuttle from school to the train station. 学生从学校坐穿梭公交去火车站。

sidestep
sidestep［'saɪdstep］
v. 横跨一步躲闪；回避（困难）〈同　avoid, evade〉
例　The player sidestepped his opponent and kicked the ball into the net. 那名球员晃开了对手，把球踢进了球门。

sideways
sideways　［ˈsaɪdweɪz］
adv. 向一旁，向侧面
例 If you would move sideways to the left, I can get everyone in the picture. 如果你往左边移一下，我就能把所有人拍到画面里。

sigh
sigh　［saɪ］
vi. 叹息，叹气
例 James sighed when Ann told him that she would not go to the dance with him. 当安拒绝跟他参加舞会时，詹姆斯叹了一口气。
n. 叹息声
例 The student let out a sigh of relief when he finished the examination. 那个学生考完试之后，松了一口气。

sightseeing
sightseeing　［ˈsaɪtsiːɪŋ］
n. 观光
例 He went on a sightseeing trip to Rome. 他去罗马观光旅游。

sign
sign　［saɪn］
n. 标志；符号〈同 indication〉
例 Ancient people viewed comets as signs of evil. 古代人将彗星视为灾难的标志。
v. 签署；签名〈同 write the name〉
例 He signed at the end of the letter. 他在信的结尾署上自己的名字。

signal
signal　［ˈsɪɡnəl］
n. 信号〈同 sign〉
例 A red light is a signal of danger. 红灯是危险的信号。

signature
signature　［ˈsɪɡnətʃə(r)］
n. 签名，署名
例 The doctor's signature was difficult to read. 医生写的字很难认。

significant
significant　［sɪɡˈnɪfɪkənt］
adj. 有意义的；重要的，重大的〈同 noteworthy〉
例 Proper exercise plays a significant role in the rehabilitation of patients with various back ailments. 对于各种背部疾病的患者来说，适当的锻炼对于康复有着至关重要的作用。
记 sign（记号，信号）+ific（带来）+ant→带有信号的→有意义的
联 significantly adv. 意味深长地；值得注目地；significance n. 意义，含义；重要性；insignificant adj. 无关紧要的，可忽略的

signify
signify［'sɪgnɪfaɪ］
vt. 表示，意味〈同 denote, mean〉
例　The poor results from the test trials signify that the shuttle is not ready for launch. 测试的糟糕结果意味着航天器还无法发射。

silly
silly［'sɪli］
adj. 愚蠢的；糊涂的；傻的〈同　foolish, stupid〉
例　The circus clown was very silly. 那个马戏团的小丑非常可笑。

silt
silt［sɪlt］
n. 淤泥
例　The harbor channel must be dredged annually to remove the silt. 必须每年对海港航道进行疏浚，以清除航道中的淤泥。

similar
similar　［ˈsɪmələ(r)］
adj. 相似的，类似的〈同 comparable〉
例 I bought some new shoes which are very similar to a pair I had had before. 我买了几双新鞋，与我之前的一双鞋非常类似。

simplicity
simplicity［sɪm'plɪsɪti］
n. ①简单〈同　easiness〉
例　The simplicity of that book makes it suitable for children. 那本书简单易懂，适合孩子阅读。
例　A room in a hospital should be furnished with simplicity. 医院里的房间必须简单装修。

simplify
simplify　［ˈsɪmplɪfaɪ］
vt. 单一化，简单化〈同 make easier〉
例 The college simplified its complex entry requirements. 学院简化了复杂的入学要求。
联 simplicity n. 简易

simultaneous
simultaneous［ˌsɪməl'teɪnɪəs; (US)ˌsaɪməl'teɪnɪəs］
adj. 同时的，同时发生的〈同 concurrent〉
例　The network made a simultaneous broadcast by radio and television. 联播网使得广播和电视可以同时播出同一节目。

sin
sin［sɪn］
n. 罪〈同 wrongdoing〉
例　The priest told the children that since they committed sins, they would go to hell. 牧师告诫小孩，如果他们犯下罪孽，就会下地狱。

sincere
sincere　［sɪnˈsɪə(r)］
adj. 诚挚的，真诚的〈同 honest〉
例 He offered a sincere apology for his behavior. 他为自己的行为表达了诚挚的歉意。

single
single　［ˈsɪŋɡəl］
adj. 单一的；单身的〈同 only one〉
例 The sisters share one room with two single beds in it. 俩姐妹共用一个放着两张单人床的房间。

singular
singular　［ˈsɪŋɡjʊlə(r)］
adj. ① 单数的
例 The singular form of “children” is “child”. “children”的单数形式是“child”。
例 John developed a singular manner for dealing with angry people tactfully. 约翰想出来一种巧妙应对生气的人的奇妙方法。

sink
sink　［sɪŋk］
v. 沉下，（使）下沉〈同 go down〉
例 The storm sank two fishing boats. 暴风雨造成两艘渔船沉没。
n. 水槽，水池
例 David's dirty dishes piled up in the kitchen sink. 戴维的脏盘子都堆在厨房的水槽里。

sinuous
sinuous［'sɪnjʊəs］
adj. 蜿蜒的，迂回的〈同　curving, twisting〉
例　Snakes move by the sinuous motion of the muscles in their bodies. 蛇通过身体肌肉的弯曲动作向前移动。

site
site　［saɪt］
n. 地点，地方〈同 place〉
例 The ambulance rushed to the accident site. 急救车迅速赶往事故现场。

skeleton
skeleton［'skelɪtən］
n. 骨架；梗概〈同 framework〉
例　The students studied the skeleton in their biology class. 学生们在生物课上研究骨骼模型。

skeptical
skeptical［'skeptɪkəl］
adj. 怀疑的；多疑的〈同 suspicious〉
例　I am skeptical of his methods; they do not seem very scientific to me. 我对他的方法持怀疑态度，我认为这些方法不太科学。

sketch
sketch　［sketʃ］
n. 草图；素描〈同 outline〉
例 My mother made a pencil sketch of my brother reading a book. 我妈妈画了一幅弟弟读书的铅笔素描。
v. 打草稿；素描〈同 draw, delineate〉
例 He sketched out a plan for his inferiors to execute. 他草拟了一个方案，交给下属去执行。
联 sketchy adj. 粗略的

skim
skim　［skɪm］
v. ① 撇去
例 We made a contest to see who could skim a flat stone over the water the farthest. 我们进行打水漂比赛，看谁的扁平石头在水面上飞的距离最远。
例 I've only skimmed over his letter. I haven't read it carefully yet. 我只是粗略地浏览了一下他的信。我还没有仔细读。

skimp
skimp［skɪmp］
v. 节省，节俭；吝啬〈同　stint, spare〉
例　They were forced to skimp on necessities in order to make their limited supplies last the winter. 为了使他们有限的物资能够维持一个冬天，他们不得不节约使用生活必需品。

skip
skip［skɪp］
v. ① 跳〈同 jump, hop〉
例　He skipped from rock to rock. 他从一块岩石上跳到另一块岩石上。
例　He got into trouble after he skipped class. 他逃课之后遇到麻烦了。

skyrocket
skyrocket［skaɪ'rɒkɪt］
vi. 猛涨，突增〈同　rise quickly, soar〉
例　Sales skyrocketed after the release of the new advertisements. 新广告推出之后，商品销量暴涨。

skyscraper
skyscraper［'skaɪskreɪpə(r)］
n. 摩天大楼〈同 edifice〉
例　Skyscrapers were the tallest buildings in the city. 摩天大楼曾是这个城市最高的建筑。

slab
slab［slæb］
n.（四边形的厚物质）板，片〈同　a broad〉
例　Talc, a soft mineral with a variety of uses, is sold in slabs or in powdered form. 云母是一种用途广泛的软矿石，通常以板或粉末的形式出售。

slack
slack［slæk］
adj. ① 疏忽的〈同 negligent〉
例　The manager criticized them for being slack at their jobs; they omitted many details and incurred a lot of mistakes. 经理批评他们工作马虎；他们遗漏了很多细节，导致发生了许多错误。
例　The slack rope needed to be tightened to make it more secure. 需要把松弛的绳索系紧，这样会更安全。

slam
slam　［slæm］
v. ① 砰地关上
例 She slammed the window down. 她“砰”的一声把窗户关上了。
例 That car slammed into a truck. 那辆小汽车猛地撞在一辆卡车上。

slander
slander［'slɑ:ndə(r); (US)'slændər］
n./v. 诽谤〈同　defamation; malign〉
例　Unless you can prove your allegations, your remarks constitute slander. 除非你能证明你的主张，否则你的话就构成了诽谤。

slap
slap［slæp］

例　She slapped him in the face after he made that impolite comment. 他说了那些无礼的话之后，她扇了他一耳光。

slash
slash［slæ∫］

例　Prices have been slashed by 50%. 价格大幅下跌了50%。

slaughter
slaughter［'slɔ:tə(r)］

例　Thousands of cattle are slaughtered every year to make hamburgers. 为了制作汉堡，每年都要宰杀数以千计的牛。

sleeve
sleeve［sli:v］
n. 袖子
例　Johnson rolled up his sleeves before he washed the dishes. 约翰逊卷起袖子，开始洗碗。

slender
slender　［ˈslendə(r)］
adj. 苗条的；纤细的〈同 slim〉
例 Silkworms digested mulberry leaves and then formed slender threads. 蚕消化桑树叶后吐出蚕丝。

slice
slice　［slaɪs］

slight
slight　［slaɪt］
adj. 轻微的；微小的，微不足道的〈同 subtle; tiny〉
例 Since an owl's ears are widely separated, there is usually a slight difference in the time it takes for a sound to reach each ear. 由于猫头鹰的耳朵分开的距离很大，因此一个声音传入它两个耳朵的时间通常存在细微的差异。
记 s+litht（轻微的，不重要的)→微小的
联 slightly adv. 轻微地

slim
slim［slɪm］

例　She went on a diet to become slim. 为了减肥，她开始节食。

slime

例　Please take your shoes off before you come in so you don't get any slime on the carpet. 进门之前请脱鞋，以免在地毯上留下泥巴。

slip
slip　［slɪp］
n. 滑倒；事故
例 John's slip on the floor resulted in a broken leg. 约翰在地板上滑倒了，结果摔断了腿。
v. 滑动；滑倒〈同 slide〉
例 The knife slipped and he cut his finger. 刀子滑了一下，他割伤了自己的手指。
联 slipper n. 拖鞋；slippery adj. 滑的，滑溜的

slippery
slippery［'slɪpəri］

例　Drive carefully, the roads are wet and slippery. 小心开车，因为道路又湿又滑。

slit
slit　［slɪt］

slogan

slot
slot［slɒt］

sloth
sloth［sləʊθ］

例　The sloth is a creature commonly found on trees in Central and South American jungles. 树懒是中南美洲丛林里的一种常见动物，它们一般生活在树上。

sluggish
sluggish［'slʌgɪ∫］

例　It was a sluggish day at the office and no one wanted to work. 办公室里一整天都死气沉沉，没有人想工作。

slum
slum［slʌm］

sly

例　She was sly in card games and never lost. 在玩扑克牌的时候，她非常狡猾，从来没输过。

smart

例 If you are a smart man, women will like you, even if you are not good-looking. 如果你是个聪明的男人，女人就会喜欢你，即便你长得不帅。

smash

例　The baby liked to splash water when taking a bath. 这个婴儿在洗澡的时候，喜欢戏水玩耍。

例 The coronation of a new king or queen is a splendid affair, with much elaborate and brilliant ceremony. 新国王或女王的加冕仪式是一件非常精彩的盛事，有许多精心准备的华丽仪式。
联 splendor n. 壮丽；辉煌

例 The teacher split the children into three groups. 老师把孩子们分成了三个组。

例 When milk spoils, it smells very bad. 牛奶一旦变质，会非常难闻。

联 spoilage n.（食物等）变质；损坏；unspoiled adj. 未损坏的

sponsor　［ˈspɒnsə(r)］

例 All the major theatres now have sponsors, especially for high-cost productions. 现在所有大型剧院都有赞助商，尤其是高成本的作品。

例 The team is sponsored by JVC, so the players wear the letters “JVC” on their shirts. 这个团队得到了JVC公司的赞助，所以演员们都穿着印有JVC字母的衬衫。

sprawl［sprɔ:l］

例 John sprayed insect poison on the plants. 约翰往植物上喷洒杀虫剂。

spring　［sprɪŋ］

spur　［spɜː(r)］

例 James is content with his success, but his wife keeps spurring him onto something “higher” or “better”. 詹姆斯满足于自己的成功，而他的妻子却不断激励他要追求“更高”或“更好”。

例　In Japan and elsewhere, the trees are planted to stabilize the soil on steep mountain slopes. 在日本以及其他一些地区，人们在陡峭的山坡上种植植物以防止土壤流失。

例 They have been working together for over five years and they have both become a little stale. 他们在一起合作超过五年了，两人都感觉有些乏味了。

stipulate
stipulate［'stɪpjʊleɪt］
vt. 约定，规定〈同　detail, specify〉
例　If the contract was framed by a good lawyer, it will stipulate exactly when, where, and how payment is to be made. 如果合同是由一名出色的律师草拟的，里面会明确规定付款的时间、地点和方式。

stir
stir［stɜ:(r)］
v. 激起，引起；搅动〈同 churn〉
例　If you stir your tea, the sugar will melt more quickly. 如果你搅一搅茶，糖就会融化得更快。

stitch
stitch［stɪtʃ］
v. 缝〈同 sew, knit〉
例　She stitched the hole in her husband's shirt. 她将丈夫衬衫上的破洞缝补好了。

stock
stock　［stɒk］
n. ① 库存〈同 storage〉
例 It is now halfway through winter and food stocks are already low. 冬天才过去一半，食物库存量就已经很少了。
例 She buys and sells stocks and shares. 她买卖股票和股份。
adj. 普通的〈同 usual〉
例

stocky
stocky［'stɒki］
adj.（人或动物）矮而结实的，粗壮的〈同　strong, stout〉
例　The stocky construction worker lifted the lumber with ease. 那名健壮的建筑工人轻松地搬起了那块木材。

stoop
stoop　［stuːp］
v. 弯腰，屈背〈同 bend down〉
例 Bob stooped so he wouldn't bump his head on the low eaves. 鲍勃俯下身，这样才不会被低矮的屋檐撞到头。

stout
stout［staʊt］
adj. 结实的，勇敢坚定的〈同　stocky, sturdy〉
例　The stout man liked to eat. 那个肥胖的人就喜欢吃。

stouthearted
stouthearted［ˌstaʊt'hɑ:tɪd］
adj. 勇敢的
解　having courage; brave
例　Armed with a stouthearted spirit, the little boy was able to knock the giant down. 小男孩用刚毅的精神鼓舞自己，然后把巨人打倒了。

straightforward
straightforward［streɪt'fɔ:wəd］
adj. ①（指人、态度等）坦率的，老实的〈同 honest〉
例　Her criticism of any paper was straightforward and painful. 她针对每篇论文提出的批评都很直接，让人不快。
例　The negotiator gave a very straightforward explanation as to why he would not assume any risks. 谈判者简单解释了为什么他不会承担任何风险。

strain
strain　［streɪn］
n. ① 紧张；压力〈同 tension〉
例 The strain of meeting a daily deadline made the columnist very anxious. 每天都会遇到最后期限的压力，这让专栏作家非常紧张。
例 Scientists have discovered a new strain of virus which may be responsible for the disease. 科学家们发现了一种新的病毒，它可能是造成这种病的罪魁祸首。
vt. 过滤〈同 filter〉
例 Janet strained the particles from the chemical solution. 珍妮特从化学溶液中滤除微粒。

strand
strand［strænd］
n.（绳、线之）一股〈同　thread〉
例　The strands of thread were twisted together to make rope. 几股线被拧在一起做成一根绳子。

strap
strap　［stræp］
n. 带，皮带〈同 belt〉
例 Could you help me fasten the strap around my suitcase? 你能帮我系上手提箱上的皮带吗？

strata
strata［'strɑ:tə］
n. 地层〈同　layer〉
例　The different strata of the Earth tell a history of their own. 地球的不同地层各自代表了一段历史。

strategy
strategy　［ˈstrætəʤi］
n. 策略，战略〈同 policy〉
例 The company will spend $6 million on the development of new products and sales strategies. 公司将投入600万美元，用于开发新产品和制定销售策略。
联 strategic adj. 战略的，战略上的

streamline
streamline［'stri:mlaɪn］
vt. ① 使成流线型 ② 改善…的表面或效率；使现代化
解　① to construct or design in a form that offers the least resistance to fluid flow ② to improve the appearance or efficiency of; to modernize
例　Through evolution, fish were streamlined in order to swim faster, to catch prey and avoid predators. 通过进化，鱼类的身体变成了流线型，这样可以游得更快，从而可以捕捉到猎物并躲避猎食者。
同　stream n. 溪流，水流，河流

streamlined
streamlined［'stri:mlaɪnd］
adj. 流线型的
例　Fish developed their streamlined shape to swim faster. 鱼类进化成了流线型是为了游得更快。

strengthen
strengthen　［ˈstreŋθən］
vt. 加强，巩固〈同 reinforce〉
例 The new constitution will further strengthen the powers of the president. 新章程将进一步加强总裁的权力。

strenuous［'strenjʊəs］
adj. 费力的；艰辛的〈同　arduous, laborious〉
例　After a strenuous day of work, Bill slept for 12 hours. 一天的紧张工作之后，比尔睡了12个小时。

stress
stress　［stres］
n. 重压，压力〈同 tension〉
例 Many heavy trucks put a lot of stress on the old bridge. 许多辆重型卡车给这座古老的大桥带来了许多压力。
vt. 着重，强调；重读〈同 emphasize〉
例 She has repeatedly stressed that the laboratory's safety standards are the best in the country. 她不断强调，实验室的安全标准在全国是最高的。

例 Anne stretched her arms wide and yawned. 安妮伸了伸胳膊，然后打了个哈欠。

例　The child could not keep up with his father's stride. 小孩无法跟上父亲的脚步。

strike
strike　［straɪk］

例 The union settled the strike when the management offered a fair contract. 在管理层提出签订一份公平的契约后，工会才平息了罢工。

例 The ball struck me in the back. 球打在了我的后背上。
联 striking adj. 显著的，惊人的

striking

例　We must strive to finish this report before we leave because it is due tomorrow morning. 我们必须在离开之前完成这份报告，因为截止日期是明天上午。

stroke
stroke　［strəʊk］

例　This tree is not as large as the others; something must have stunted its growth. 这棵树没有其他树长得那么高大；肯定有什么原因妨碍了它的成长。

subject　［ˈsʌbʤekt］

adj. 受…影响的；以…为条件的（to)〈同 depending on〉
例 Moving all the books should not take long, subject to there being enough helpers. 搬走所有的书应该用不了多长时间，因为给我们帮忙的人足够多。

submerge

记 sub（下面）+ merge（合并；吞没)→吞没下去→淹没

submerge
submerge［səb'mɜ:ʤ］
v. 潜入水中；沉没；淹没
解　to place or plunge under water
例　The submarine submerged to escape attack. 潜艇潜入水中躲避攻击。
构　sub (=below) + merg (=to sink) + e

例 The fishermen set out at sunset for a night's fishing. 渔民们在日落时出发，进行夜间捕鱼。

superb
superb［su:'pɜ:b; sju:'pɜ:b］
adj. 极好的，超级的〈同 excellent, wonderful〉
例　This excellent restaurant serves superb steaks. 这家高档的餐厅有优质牛排。

superficial
superficial　［ˌsuːpəˈfɪʃəl; ˌsjuːpəˈfɪʃəl］
adj. 肤浅的，表面（上）的〈同 shallow〉
例 His kindness was all superficial. Janet exposed him for what he really was. 他的仁慈都是表面现象。珍妮特揭露了他的真实面目。
记 super（超过）+ fic（做）+ ial→在上面做→表面（上)的
联 superficially adv. 表面上地

superficial
superficial［ˌsju:pə'fɪʃəl］
adj. 表面的，肤浅的
解　not deep or penetrating emotionally or intellectually
例　This essay will only give you a superficial understanding of the subject; several years of research are necessary to really understand it. 这篇文章只能让你对这个主题有个肤浅的了解，要想真正理解它，你还需要花费几年的时间进行好好研究。
构　super (=above, over) + fic (=to make, to do) + ial

superfluous
superfluous［ˌsju:'pɜ:flʊəs］
adj. 多余的〈同　unnecessary, excess〉
例　After I was full, the extra food she offered was superfluous. 我吃饱了之后，她额外上的那些食物便多余了。

superfluous
superfluous［ˌsju:'pɜ:flʊəs］
adj. 多余的，过剩的
解　more than is needed, desired, or required; unnecessary
例　The writing professor assigned a word limit to his essay assignment so students would be less likely to use superfluous words. 写作课教授对给学生布置的写作作业设置了字数限制，这样学生们就不太可能出现字数过多的情况。
同　superfluity n. 多余，累赘

例　The picture superimposed the picture of the Democrat on a donkey as a political joke. 这幅图片把民主党的照片叠合在一头驴上当做一个政治笑话。

adj. 较高的，上级的；较好的；优秀的

例　The cashier tagged a surcharge onto the bill. 出纳在账单上添上了一笔附加费。
n. 标签，货签〈同　label〉
例　The tag on the shirt says it costs 20 dollars. 衬衫的标签上写着其价格是20美元。

taint
taint［teɪnt］
n. 污点〈同　stain, blot〉
例　The one incident was a permanent taint on his reputation. 那件事是他名誉上永久的污点。
vt. 污染；玷污〈同　contaminate; blemish〉
例　The water was tainted with waste from the factory. 水被工厂排放的废物污染了。

talent
talent　［ˈtælənt］
n. 才能；天才〈同 skill; gift〉
例 She is a young dancer of great talent. 她是一位很有天赋的年轻舞者。
联 talented adj. 有才能的

talkative
talkative［'tɔ:kətɪv］
adj. 多话的〈同　garrulous, loquacious〉
例　He was very shy as a boy, but became more talkative as he got older. 他小的时候非常腼腆，但长大后变得健谈多了。

tally
tally［'tæli］
v.（使）符合〈同　agree, correspond〉
例　The two statements do not tally at all. 这两份声明根本不一致。
n. 记录；记账〈同　count〉
例　The final tally of the votes indicated that the incumbent won. 选举的最终票数显示，现任者获得选举的胜利。

tame
tame　［teɪm］
vt. 驯养，驯服〈同 domesticate〉
例 It is quite difficult to tame wild animals. 驯服野生动物很难。
adj.（指动物）驯服的，温顺的〈同 domesticated, meek〉
例 The monkeys born at the zoo are tame. 在动物园出生的猴子非常温顺。
记 发音像北京话“忒没”→忒没脾气了→驯服的
联 untamed adj. 未驯服的；tameless adj. 无法驯服的

tangle
tangle［'tæŋg(ə)l］

例　The insect was tangled up in the spider's web and could not escape. 昆虫被蜘蛛网缠住了，没法逃跑。

tap
tap　［tæp］

tar［tɑ:(r)］

例　This cigarette with lower tar is probably less harmful. 吸这种焦油含量低的香烟可能对健康的损害少一点。

例　The accident tarnished John's driving record. 那次事故破坏了约翰良好的驾驶记录。

technocracy［tek'nɒkrəsi］
n. 技术统治
解　a form of government in which scientists and technical experts are in control
例　A group of computer engineers dreamed of creating a technocracy based on the Internet. 一些电脑工程师梦想创建一个基于互联网的技术统治政府。

tectonics［tek'tɒnɪks］
n.【地】构造学
例　Tectonics is the scientific study of the deformation of the rocks that make up the Earth's crust and the forces that produce such deformation. 构造地质学是关于构成地壳的岩石的变化以及造成这种变化的力的科学研究。

tedious
tedious　［ˈtiːdɪəs］
adj. 单调乏味的，沉闷的〈同 tiresome〉
例 The tedious lecture bored most of the audience. 沉闷乏味的演讲让大多数听众感到厌烦。
记 ted（厌倦）+ious→让人厌倦的→单调乏味的
联 tedium n. 乏味

tedium［'ti:dɪəm］

例　We hope this radio will help overcome the tedium of your stay in the hospital. 我们希望这台收音机能够帮助你消除住院期间的无聊。

例 Anne's harsh words were tempered with a kind smile. 安妮的话语严厉，脸上却带着和蔼的微笑，缓和了气氛。

temperate
temperate［'tempərɪt］

例　The United States is mostly in the North Temperate Zone. 美国大部分都处在北温带。
例　Noted for his temperate appetite, he seldom gains weight. 他以适度饮食而出名，体重很少会增加。

tempo
tempo［'tempəʊ］

例　As the music reached a frenetic tempo the audience lost all decorum and broke into impromptu dancing. 随着音乐节奏变得狂热，观众们也丢掉矜持，即兴跳起舞来。

tempo
tempo［'tempəʊ］
n. （音乐）速度，拍子
解　the speed at which a composition is to be played
例　Professional dancers can naturally move to the rhythm and tempo of the music. 专业舞蹈家会自然地跟着音乐的节拍和旋律起舞。

temporary

temporary
temporary［'tempərəri］

例　Although bad times may seem never-ending, they are temporary just like everything else. 虽然糟糕的境遇似乎无休无止，但是它们和所有事情一样，都是暂时的。

trespass
trespass［'trespəs］
v. ① 侵犯，闯入私人领地 ② 侵占另一个人的时间、隐私或注意力
解　① to go on to privately owned land without right or permission ② to take too much of someone's time, privacy, attention, etc.
例　The boys trespassed into the private property out of curiosity, and were chased away by two big dogs. 男孩们出于好奇闯入了这个私人住宅，然后被两只大狗追赶了出来。

trial　［treɪl］
n. ① 实验〈同 experiment〉
例 Over a very large number of trials, the probability of an event occurring is equal to the probability that it will not occur. 经过大量测试，一个事件发生的概率与其不发生的概率是相等的。
例 The scandal put the President on trial. 丑闻使总统面临审讯。

tribe
tribe［traɪb］
n. 部落，部族
例　Everyone in the tribe participates in a weekly ritual. 部落里的每个人都参加每周一次的仪式。

tributary
tributary［'trɪbjʊtəri; (US)-teri］
adj. 辅助的，支流的
例　Some of the first settlers of America refused to be considered part of a tributary colony of England and fought for their freedom. 美洲第一批移民中，有些人拒绝被视为英国的附属殖民地的一部分，并为了自由而进行了抗争。
n. 支流〈同　branch〉
例　The Ohio River is a tributary of the Mississippi River. 俄亥俄河是密西西比河的支流。

tribute
tribute［'trɪbju:t］
n. ① 贡品；贡税〈同 tax, levy〉
例　The defeated country was forced to pay a tribute to the victor. 战败国被迫向战胜国交纳贡品。
例　The actress gave tribute to her director when she accepted her Oscar. 在接受奥斯卡金像奖的时候，这位女演员向导演表达了感激之情。

trick
trick　［trɪk］
n. 诡计；恶作剧
例 Somebody played a trick on me by hiding my shoes. 有人把我的鞋子藏了起来捉弄我。

trickle
trickle［'trɪkəl］
vi. 滴；流出〈同　dribble, drip〉
例　Blood trickled down her face. 血顺着她的脸往下滴。

trifle
trifle［'traɪfəl］
n. 琐事；少量〈同 little〉
例　The cheap picture cost only a trifle. 只花了一点钱就买了这幅便宜的画。

trigger
trigger［'trɪgə(r)］
vt. 引发，引起，触发〈同 set off, initiate〉
例　The attack triggered a full-scale war. 这次攻击引发了全面的战争。

trilogy
trilogy［'trɪləʤi］
n. 三部剧，三部曲〈同　three-part novel〉
例　The Star Wars trilogy has become a classic story. 《星球大战》三部曲已经成为经典故事。

trim
trim　［trɪm］
vt. 修剪，整饰〈同 clip〉
例 The barber trimmed my hair. 理发师给我理发。

triple
triple［'trɪpəl］
n./adj. 三倍数（的）
例　Nine is the triple of three. 9是3的三倍。

triumph
triumph　［ˈtraɪəmf］
n. 胜利〈同 victory〉
例 His career was characterized by one triumph after another. 他做事的特点就是接二连三的胜利。
vi. 获得胜利，成功〈同 win〉
例 The lucky patient triumphed over cancer. 那名幸运的患者战胜了癌症。
联 triumphant adj. 胜利的

trivial
trivial［'trɪvɪəl］
adj. 微不足道的，琐碎的〈同 insignificant, trifling〉
例　The new textbook is quite good, though it does contain a few trivial errors. 尽管里面有点小错误，这本新教科书还是不错的。

tropical
tropical　［ˈtrɒpɪkəl］
adj. 热带的
例 Most bananas are grown on tropical plantations. 大部分香蕉都被种在热带种植园里。

troublesome
troublesome　［ˈtrʌbəlsəm］
adj. 讨厌的，麻烦的〈同 annoying〉
例 Her hip has been troublesome for quite a while, and she'll probably need surgery on it. 她的臀部让她烦恼了很久，她可能需要给它做个手术。
联 troubling adj. 令人不安的，令人忧虑的

troupe
troupe［tru:p］
n. 剧团；群，队
例　The troupe of actors will present six different plays during the season. 在演出季，这群演员将带来六部不同的剧目。

trustworthy
trustworthy［'trʌstwɜ:ði］
adj. 可信赖的〈同　dependable, reliable〉
例　The boss could always tell his secrets to his trustworthy assistant. 老板经常把他的秘密告诉自己信任的助理。

tuck
tuck［tʌk］
vt. 把…塞进（一个狭小容器或空洞等）
例　All the boys in this class are required to tuck their shirts into their pants. 这个班里的所有男孩被要求把衬衫下摆塞到裤子里。

tug
tug［tʌg］
v. 用力拖，吃力地搬运〈同 pull〉
例　They tugged on the rope to pull the truck out of the mud. 他们用力拽着绳子，想把卡车从泥里拉出来。

tuition
tuition［tju:'ɪʃən; (US)'tu:'ɪʃn］
n. 学费
例　He had to pay the school tuition before he could attend class. 他必须交了学费，然后才能上课。

tumble
tumble［'tʌmbəl］
vi. 跌倒〈同 topple, fall〉
例　He tumbled off his horse. 他从马上摔了下来。

turbulent
turbulent［'tɜ:bjʊlənt］
adj. 吵闹的；狂暴的，（空气等）流动得剧烈而不稳定的〈同 disorderly, violent〉
例　Since the 1930s, aircraft manufacturers have tried to build airplanes with frictionless wings so that the air passing over them would not become turbulent. 从20世纪30年代起，飞机制造者就开始尝试建造一种有平滑机翼的飞机，这样飞机在穿过气流时就不会产生强烈的震荡。

turnover
turnover［'tɜ:nəʊvə(r)］
n. 营业额；人员更替率
例　This department has the highest turnover rate in the company. 这个部门是公司人员流动率最高的部门。

turnpike
turnpike［'tɜ:npaɪk］
n. 公路，收费高速公路〈同　toll highway〉
例　You should be sure you have money to pay for the tolls if you take the turnpike. 如果你选择走收费高速公路，你得确保自己有足够的钱支付通行费。

tutor
tutor［'tju:tə(r); (US)'tu:tər］
vt. 辅导；当…的家庭教师〈同 guide, direct〉
例　Ted wants someone to tutor him before the exam. 泰德希望有人能在考前辅导他。
n. 家庭教师〈同 coach〉
例　The tutor would explain his mistakes to him. 家庭教师会对他犯错的地方进行讲解。

twig
twig［twɪg］
n. 细枝，嫩枝
例　Some insects will mimic a twig when in danger. 有些昆虫在面临危险时会伪装成树枝的样子。

twine
twine［twaɪn］
v. 搓；编织；（使）缠绕〈同　twist, intertwine〉
例　The python is a snake that twines around its prey before swallowing it. 巨蟒是一种蛇，它会先缠绕猎物，然后再将其吞下。

twinkle
twinkle［'twɪŋkəl］
v. 闪烁；（使）闪光〈同 glitter〉
例　You could stay up all night trying to count all the stars that twinkle in the sky. 你可以整夜不睡，试着数清天上所有闪烁的星星。

twist
twist　［twɪst］
v. 扭弯，扭曲，缠绕〈同 bend〉
例 The visitor twisted his neck to look at the photograph on the wall behind him. 参观者扭过头看他身后墙上的照片。

tycoon
tycoon［taɪ'ku:n］
n. 大企业家，大亨〈同　magnate, entrepreneur〉
例　John D. Rockefeller was a prominent tycoon. 约翰·D. 洛克菲勒是一位杰出的企业界大亨。

typical
typical　［ˈtɪpɪkəl］
adj. 典型的；有代表性的〈同 classic; representative〉
例 This sort of hot and spicy food is very typical of the food in the south of the country. 这种辛辣食品是这个国家南方的典型食品。
记 typ（看作type，类型）+ical→经典的类型→典型的
联 atypical adj. 非典型的；typically adv. 有特色地

tyrannical
tyrannical［tɪ'rænɪkəl］
adj. 暴虐的，残暴的〈同　dictatorial, domineering, authoritarian〉
例　The tyrannical king was merciless and let no one stand in his way. 那个残暴的国王非常冷酷无情，绝不允许任何人阻挡他的道路。

ugly
ugly　［ˈʌɡli］
adj. 丑陋的，难看的
例 She's got one of those really ugly dogs with a squashed face. 她有一只那种非常丑陋的狗，狗脸看上去像是被压扁了。

ultimate
ultimate　［ˈʌltɪmət］
adj. 最后的，最终的〈同 final〉
例 The ultimate results were not really foreseeable, but we prepared for them as best we could. 最终结果是不可预测的，但我们已经尽可能为此做好了准备。
记 ultim（最远，落后）+ate→最后的
联 ultimately adv. 最后，最终；ultimatum n. 最后通牒

ultimatum
ultimatum［ˌʌltɪ'meɪtəm］
n. 最后通牒〈同　last offer〉
例　Since they have ignored our ultimatum, our only recourse is to declare war. 既然他们对我们的最后通牒视而不见，我们唯一的手段就是宣战。

ultrasonic
ultrasonic［ˌʌltrə'sɒnɪk］
adj. 超音速的，超声（波）的〈同　supersonic〉
例　Bats use ultrasonic waves to locate flying insects at night. 蝙蝠利用超声波在夜间定位飞行的昆虫。

ultraviolet
ultraviolet［ˌʌltrə'vaɪələt］
adj. 紫外线的
例　We cannot see ultraviolet light in our atmosphere. 我们看不到空气中的紫外线。

unanimity
unanimity［ˌju:nə'nɪməti］
n. 全体一致，一致同意〈同　concord, consensus, harmony〉
例　We were surprised by the unanimity with which our proposals were accepted by the different groups. 我们的提案竟然被不同群体一致同意接受，这令我们很是吃惊。

unanimous
unanimous［ˌju:'nænɪməs］
adj. 全体意见一致的〈同 uniform, agreed〉
例　Janet was elected chairwoman by a unanimous decision of the board. 经董事会一致同意，珍妮特当选为主席。

unanimous
unanimous［ju:'nænɪməs］
adj. 全体意见一致的
解　in complete agreement
例　The board came to the unanimous decision to elect Olin as president. 董事会一致决定推选奥林为主席。
同　unanimity n. 全体一致，一致同意

unbiased
unbiased［ʌn'baɪəst］
adj. 没有偏见的〈同　impartial, fair〉
例　The unbiased mediator helped solve the contract dispute. 那名公正的调停者帮助解决了合同纠纷。

unbridgeable
unbridgeable［ʌn'brɪʤbəl］
adj. 不能架桥的；不可逾越的〈同　impassable, insurmountable〉
例　The differences between the wife and husband were unbridgeable, so they decided to file for divorce. 这对夫妻之间有无法逾越的分歧，所以他们决定申请离婚。

unbridled
unbridled［ʌn'braɪdəld］
adj. 放纵的，无约束的〈同　uncontrolled, wild〉
例　His unbridled anger eventually drove his wife away. 他无法抑制的愤怒最终逼走了他的妻子。

unbroken
unbroken［ʌn'brəʊkən］
adj. 完整的；持续的〈同　uninterrupted, intact〉
例　The longest unbroken border in the world is that between Canada and the United States. 世界上最长的连续边界线在加拿大与美国之间。

unconscious
unconscious　［ʌnˈkɒnʃəs］
adj. 不省人事的；无意识的〈同 senseless〉
例 The doctor tried to revive the unconscious crash victim. 医生努力让那名失去意识的车祸受害者苏醒过来。
记 un（不）+conscious（清醒的）→不省人事的
联 unconsciously adv. 无意中，不知不觉

uncover
uncover［ˌʌn'kʌvə(r)］

例　The newspaper article uncovered the truth behind the scandal. 报纸上的这篇文章揭示了丑闻背后的真相。

underdeveloped

例　The value of our house was underestimated by at least two thousand dollars. 我们房子的价值被低估了至少两千美元。

undergo
undergo　［ˌʌndəˈɡəʊ］

例 Mary told me of the ordeal she underwent during the robbery. 玛丽跟我讲了她在抢劫发生期间所经受的折磨。

undergraduate

underline
underline　［ˌʌndəˈlaɪn］
vt. ① 在…下面划线
例 Students prefer to underline important points, and it seemed to be just as useful as note-taking. 学生们喜欢划出要点，这似乎与记笔记一样有用。
例 To underline their disgust, the crowd started throwing bottles at the stage. 为了强调他们的厌恶，人们开始向舞台扔瓶子。

underlying
underlying［ˌʌndə'laɪɪŋ］

例　Lack of money was the underlying reason that I didn't go on vacation. 我没去度假的根本原因是没钱。

undermine［ˌʌndə'maɪn］

例　The recent corruption scandals have undermined many people's faith in the city government. 最近的腐败丑闻使很多人对市政府失去了信心。

underscore［ˌʌndə'skɔ:(r)］

例　When we take notes, our teacher wants us to underscore items that are especially important. 我们在记笔记的时候，老师希望我们在特别重要的条目下画线。

例 The overall task looks forbidding, but the stakes are too high not to undertake it. 从表面上看，整个任务让人望而生畏，但不接受这个任务的风险太大了。

undertaking
undertaking［ˌʌndə'teɪkɪŋ］

例　He undid his shoelaces and took his shoes off before walking inside. 他解开鞋带，脱下鞋，然后走了进去。
例　lt will take months to undo the damage caused by the disgruntled employee. 要挽回心怀不满的员工造成的损失，需要几个月的时间。

uniform
uniform　［ˈjuːnɪfɔːm］

例　She unpacked her clothes from her suitcase when she arrived at the hotel room. 她到了酒店房间后，便从行李箱里取出自己的衣服。

unprecedented
unprecedented［ʌn'presɪdentɪd］

例　George's consumption of 10,677 hot dogs was unprecedented; no one had ever eaten so many before. 乔治吃掉了10,677个热狗，真是史无前例；之前从没有人能吃这么多。

unravel

例　Anne unraveled the old sweater because she needed the yarn. 安妮拆了那件旧毛衣，因为她需要纱线。

unrestrained

unscrupulous

untie

unwieldy
unwieldy［ʌn'wi:ldi］

例　The unwieldy package was expensive to mail overseas. 向海外邮寄这个笨重的包裹，价格非常昂贵。

update

up-front
up-front［ʌp'frʌnt］
adj. ① 提前的 （指支付工资）② 坦率的
解　① paid or due in advance ② straightforward; frank
例　He would do the work only if he was paid up-front. 只有预先支付了薪水，他才愿意做这份工作。

upgrade
upgrade［ˌʌp'greɪd］
vt. 使升级，提升〈同 improve, advance〉
例　The manufacturer has done everything possible to upgrade his product, with the result that it is now of excellent quality. 制造商想尽一切办法升级产品，如今产品质量已非常上乘。

upheaval
upheaval［ʌp'hi:vəl］
n. 剧变，动乱〈同　disturbance, explosion〉
例　The recent layoffs have caused a great upheaval within the corporation. 最近的裁员在公司内造成了动荡。

uphold
uphold［ʌp'həʊld］
vt. 维护，支持（决定等）〈同 support, maintain〉
例　The Supreme Court upheld the lower court's ruling. 最高法院维持了下级法院的判决。

upright
upright［'ʌpraɪt］
adj. ①垂直的；直立的〈同　vertical; erect〉
例　He was sitting upright in his hospital bed, propped up by pillows. 他用枕头支撑着身体，直直地坐在医院的病床上。
例　The upright politician refused to accept the bribe. 那名正直的政治家拒绝接受贿赂。

uproar
uproar［'ʌprɔ:(r)］
n. 喧嚣，骚动〈同　commotion, turmoil〉
例　The car crash caused an uproar throughout the neighborhood. 车祸在整个社区造成了骚动。

uproot
uproot［ˌʌp'ru:t］
v. ①连根拔起，拔除〈同　pull up, displace〉
例　It is easier to destroy weeds with a chemical than to uproot them by hand. 用化学药品除去杂草，比用手拔草要容易得多。
例　After a year of unsuccessful business, the manager uprooted the company and moved the offices to another city. 经过一年不成功的经营，公司负责人对公司进行了彻底重建，并将办公室搬到了另外一个城市。

upset
upset　［ʌpˈset］
v. 颠覆，推翻；扰乱〈同 overturn; disturb〉
例 Any mechanical problems would upset our plans of driving across the desert. 任何机械问题都会扰乱我们驾车穿越沙漠的计划。
adj. 心烦意乱的〈同 worried〉
例 Mary was upset because we were going to be late. 玛丽很心烦，因为我们要迟到了。

upside-down
upside-down［ˌʌpsaɪd'daʊn］
adj. 颠倒的〈同　inverted〉
例　Bats like to sleep upside-down. 蝙蝠喜欢倒挂着睡觉。

urban　［ˈɜːbən］
adj. 城市的〈同 metropolitan〉
例 Urban problems often stretch beyond city limits into suburbs. 都市问题通常会从市区扩展到郊区。
联 urbanism n. 都市生活，都市化；urbanite n. 都市人；suburbanite n. 郊区居民

urge　［ɜːʤ］

例 The teacher urged us to work harder to achieve high scores. 老师督促我们更加努力地学习，以取得好成绩。

urgent　［ˈɜːʤənt］

记 来自urge（v. 驱策，催促）+ent→催促着做的→紧急的
联 urgently adv. 迫切地，急切地；urgency n. 紧急情况

utilitarian
utilitarian［ˌjʊtɪlɪ'teərɪən］
adj. 功利的；实利的〈同　practical, useful〉
例　She was not a utilitarian shopper and always wasted money on things that were unnecessary or worthless. 她并不是实用主义的购物者，经常把钱浪费在不需要或没有价值的东西上。

utility
utility　［juːˈtɪləti］
n. ① 运用；效用〈同 function, usefulness〉
例 The utility of the rescue equipment still has to be assessed in a real emergency. 这种救生设备的功用还有待在真正的紧急情况中评定。
例 The cost of utilities in this building is included in my monthly rent. 这栋大楼的公用事业费用包含在我每月的租金当中。
联 utilitarian adj. 功利的，实利的；utilitarianism n. 功利主义

violence
violence［'vaɪələns］
n. 暴力；强烈〈同 force〉
例　The violence of the storm terrified the sailors. 凶猛的风暴吓坏了水手们。

violent
violent　［ˈvaɪələnt］
adj. ① 暴力引起的；暴力的〈同 turbulent〉
例 A violent crime is committed in the United States about every 22 seconds. 美国大约每22秒钟就会发生一起暴力犯罪。
例 The violent winds tore down many tall trees. 强风吹倒了许多大树。
记 viol（冒犯）+ ent→用暴力冒犯别人→暴力的
联 violence n. 暴力

virgin
virgin［'vɜ:ʤɪn］
n. 处女
例　Mary was a virgin until she got married. 玛丽结婚之前是处女。
adj. 未经使用的，处于原来状态的；初榨的〈同 unused〉
例　Virgin olive oil is very popular in Italy. 初榨橄榄油在意大利很受欢迎。

virtual
virtual［'vɜ:tjʊəl; 'vɜ:tʃʊəl］
adj. 实质上的
例　Pollution will cause the virtual destruction of the planet. 污染能导致星球真正毁灭。

virtually
virtually　［ˈvɜːtjʊəli］
adv. 事实上，实质上；几乎〈同 almost completely〉
例 It used to be virtually impossible to find vegetarian restaurants outside the major cities, but it's much easier now. 以前要在大城市以外的地方找到素食餐厅几乎是不可能的，但现在却容易了许多。

virtue
virtue［'vɜ:tju:］
n. 美德〈同　merit, goodness〉
例　Mr. Bao is the incarnation of virtue; he has never done anything wrong since he was born. 鲍先生就是美德的化身；他自从出生以来，从未做过任何错事。

virus
virus［'vaɪərəs］
n. 病毒〈同 germ〉
例　The virus was killed with antibiotics. 抗生素杀死了病毒。

viscosity
viscosity［vɪs'kɒsəti］
n. 黏度，黏性〈同　viscidity, stickiness〉
例　The mechanic's hands were always dirty, mostly because of the viscosity of oil. 那名技工的双手总是很脏，这很大程度上是由于油的黏性。

visible
visible　［ˈvɪzəbəl］
adj. 看得见的，明显的〈同 able to be seen〉
例 Employees must wear their badges so they are visible. 员工必须佩戴徽章，以使他们易于辨认。
联 visibility n. 可见度

vision
vision　［ˈvɪʒən］
n. 视觉〈同 sight〉
例 Surgery restored the blind woman's vision. 手术恢复了那位盲人女子的视力。

vista
vista［'vɪstə］
n. 景色〈同　outlook, view〉
例　The vista from the top of the mountain is majestic. 从山顶看到的景色非常雄伟壮丽。

visual
visual　［ˈvɪʒjʊəl］
adj. 视觉的
例 Special glasses corrected David's visual problem. 特殊的眼镜矫正了戴维的视力。

visualize
visualize［'vɪzjʊəlaɪz; 'vɪʒʊəlaɪz］
v. 使可见；想像，设想〈同 imagine〉
例　The inventor of the Internet visualized a world networked together. 互联网的发明者使世界联网为一体成为现实。

vital
vital　［ˈvaɪtəl］
adj. 极重要的；与生命有关的；充满活力的〈同 essential〉
例 We learned in our biology class that all living things, no matter how large or small, carry on the same vital functions. 我们在生物课上学到过，所有生物，不论大小，均有同样的生命机能。
联 vitalism n. 活力论，生机说；vitalist n. 活力论者；vitality n. 活力，生命力

vitality
vitality［vaɪ'tæləti］
n. 活力，生命力，体力
解　vital force; power to live
例　One's vitality can be lessened by illness. 生病会削弱人的体力。

vitalize
vitalize［'vaɪtəlaɪz］
v. ① 赋予…生命 ② 给予…活力 ③ 鼓舞
解　① to give life to ② to put vitality into
例　The cartoonist vitalized the drawing of a mouse called Mickey into one of the most famous icons in the world. 这位漫画家将一只名叫米奇的老鼠画得栩栩如生，使它成为了世界上最著名的漫画形象之一。

vitiate
vitiate［'vɪʃɪeɪt］
v. ① 削弱，损害，使无效 ② 使（在道德方面）败坏
解　① to reduce the value or impair the quality of ② to corrupt morally
例　Fraud will vitiate the contract. 欺诈会使合同失效。

vivid
vivid　［ˈvɪvɪd］
adj. ①（光线、色彩）鲜艳的；强烈的〈同 bright〉
例 David's tie was a vivid green. 戴维的领带是鲜艳的绿色。
例 The author's vivid description aided my visualization of the story's setting. 作者鲜明生动的描述，帮助我更形象地了解了故事的背景。
记 viv（生命）+ id→生动的
联 vivify vt. 使生动；vivisection n. 活体解剖

vocal
vocal［'vəʊkəl］
adj. 嗓音的；歌唱的
例　Her vocal skills as a child were evidence that she would become a great singer. 作为一个小孩，她的歌唱技巧可以证明她将成为一个伟大的歌唱家。

vocation
vocation［vəʊ'keɪʃən］
n. 职业〈同 career, profession〉
例　He chose medicine as his vocation and committed himself to curing diseases. 他选择进入医药行业工作，致力于治病救人。

void
void［vɔɪd］
n. 空白，空虚〈同 emptiness, space〉
例　Her death left a void in her husband's life. 她去世后她丈夫的生活很空虚。
adj. 无效的〈同 canceled, invalid〉
例　The student's report was void of any reason and he failed. 学生的报告缺少理由，未被准许。

volatile
volatile［'vɒlətaɪl; (US)-təl］
adj. ①挥发性的〈同　evaporable〉
例　Alcohol is an example of a volatile liquid. 酒精是一种典型的挥发性液体。
例　The boss was very volatile in the morning and all his employees would avoid him then. 老板在早上的时候情绪非常不稳定，所以所有员工在那个时间都避开他。

volume
volume　［ˈvɒljuːm］
n. 体积，容积；量〈同 capacity; amount〉
例 The volume of information that a computer diskette can hold is astounding. 计算机磁盘可存储的信息量是惊人的。
联 voluminous adj. 长篇的；大量的

voluntary
voluntary　［ˈvɒləntəri; (US)ˈvɒlənteri］
adj. 自愿的；志愿的〈同 willing〉
例 The charity relied solely on voluntary support. 慈善团体完全依靠自愿支持。
记 volunt（意志，意愿）+ ary→自愿的
联 involuntary adj. 自然而然的，无意的；volunteer n. 自愿者

volunteer
volunteer［ˌvɒlən'tɪə(r)］
n. 自愿者，志愿者
例　The volunteers cleaned up the street without getting paid. 志愿者们无偿清扫街道。
v. 自愿（做…）〈同 offer〉
例　People who volunteer their services to the army were called volunteers. 志愿在军队服役的人称为志愿兵。

voracious
voracious［və'reɪ∫əs］
adj. 狼吞虎咽的，贪婪的〈同　greedy, insatiable〉
例　The wolf is a voracious animal; its hunger is never satisfied. 狼是一种贪婪的动物；它的饥饿永远得不到满足。

vote
vote　［vəʊt］
n./vt. 投票〈同 cast one's ballot〉
例 In India everyone eighteen or over gets the right to vote in political elections. 在印度，凡年满18岁者，均有权在政治选举中投票。
联 voter n. 投票者，选举人

voyage
voyage　［ˈvɔɪɪʤ］
n. 航行；旅行，航程〈同 journey〉
例 The voyage to America used to take many months. 以前，去往美国的航程需要花数月时间。
联 voyager n. 航海者

vulgar
vulgar［'vʌlgə(r)］
adj. 粗鲁的，庸俗的；下流的〈同 rude, indecent〉
例　His vulgar words were very impolite to say in front of guests. 他在客人面前说粗话是很不礼貌的。

vulnerable
vulnerable［'vʌlnərəbəl］
adj. 易受攻击的；易受伤害的〈同 defenseless, susceptible〉
例　Small animals are often vulnerable to attack. 小型动物通常易受攻击。

wage
wage　［weɪʤ］
n. 工资〈同 payment〉
例 Susan gets paid a good wage for her work. 苏珊的工资很高。
v. 发动〈同 carry on〉
例 Pakistan waged a war with India in 1965. 1965年，巴基斯坦发动了对印度的战争。

walkout
walkout［'wɔ:kaʊt］
n. 罢工〈同　strike〉
例　After the walkout, the workers and the company officials held negotiations to resolve the situation. 罢工结束后，工人们和公司领导进行了谈判，以解决当前的问题。

wallet
wallet［'wɒlɪt］
n. 皮夹，钱夹
例　He kept all his money in his wallet. 他把所有的钱都放在钱包里。
n. 仓库，货栈〈同 depot, storehouse〉
例　The warehouse stored rice and grain. 仓库存储米和粮食。

wander
wander　［ˈwɒndə(r)］
vi. 徘徊，漫步〈同 roam〉
例 Early man used to wander from one place to another in search of food and shelter. 早期人类经常四处漂泊，寻找食物和住所。

wane
wane［weɪn］
vi. 减少；衰落〈同　decline, dwindle〉
例　The fame of celebrities often starts to wane. 名人的名气经常会开始减弱。

warfare
warfare［'wɔ:fə(r)］
n. 战争；斗争
例　The Art of War is a book on warfare.《孙子兵法》是一部关于战争的书籍。

warrant
warrant［'wɒrənt; (US)'wɔ:rənt］
n. 授权书，委托书；许可证
例　The police had a warrant to enter their house and search for the missing people. 警察带着搜查证进入他们的房子，搜查失踪的人。

warrior
warrior［'wɒrɪə(r); (US)'wɔ:rɪər］
n. 战士，勇士〈同　fighter, combatant〉
例　The warrior fought bravely on the battleground. 那位战士在战场上英勇奋战。

wary
wary［'weəri］
adj. 小心翼翼的，机警小心的〈同　cautious, discreet〉
例　Marilyn's mother told her to be wary of strangers. 玛丽莲的妈妈告诉她要提防陌生人。

wasteland
wasteland［'weɪstlənd］
n. 荒地
解　an uninhabited wilderness that is worthless for cultivation
例　The desert wasteland was uninhabitable for humans. 这片被遗弃的荒地不适合人类居住。

waterfall
waterfall［'wɔ:təfɔ:l］
n. 瀑布〈同 falls〉
例　The large waterfall was exploited to make electricity. 巨大的瀑布被利用起来发电。

waterproof
waterproof［'wɔ:təpru:f］
adj. 防水的〈同 impermeable, tight〉
例　She put her camera in a waterproof bag so it wouldn't get wet. 她把相机放进防水包里防止被打湿。

wax
wax　［wæks］
n. 蜂蜡；蜡状物
例 She watched the wax as it dripped down the side of the candle. 她看着蜡从蜡烛的一侧往下滴。
v. 上蜡于〈同 polish〉
例 I waxed the floor so I'm afraid it's a bit slippery. 我给地板打了蜡，所以恐怕地板有点滑。
联 waxy adj. 苍白的；光滑的

weapon
weapon　［ˈwepən］
n. 武器〈同 arms〉
例 No weapons are permitted in school. 校园内禁止携带任何武器。

weary
weary［'wɪəri］
adj. 疲倦的；厌倦的〈同 tired, exhausted〉
例　The weary workers walked slowly toward the train station after work. 下班后，疲倦的工人们步履缓慢地朝火车站走去。

weave
weave［wi:v］
vt. 编织，组合〈同 braid, knit〉
例　A loom is used to weave cloth. 织布机用是来织布的。

wed
wed［wed］
v. 娶，嫁，（与…）结婚〈同 marry〉
例　He put one knee on the ground and asked her to wed him. 他单膝跪地，向她求婚。

wedge
wedge［weʤ］
n. 楔；使分裂的东西
例　The quarrel drove a wedge between him and his relatives. 吵架使他和他的亲人之间产生了裂痕。
v. 楔入，挤进
例　He wedged himself through the crowd to get a glimpse of the movie star. 他挤进人群瞥见了那位电影明星。

weed
weed　［wiːd］
n. 杂草
例 The farmer killed the weeds with poison. 农民用农药除去了杂草。
联 locoweed n.【植】疯草（牲畜食后会患上疯草病)；seaweed n. 海草，海藻；weed killer 除草剂

weep
weep　［wiːp］
vi. 哭泣〈同 cry〉
例 The movie Titanic was so sad that many people wept when they saw it. 电影《泰坦尼克号》太悲伤了，许多人边看边哭。

weird
weird［wɪəd］
adj. 怪诞的，奇异的〈同　queer, strange〉
例　She looked weird with that horrible makeup on her face. 她脸上糟糕的妆容让她看起来非常奇怪。

weld
weld　［weld］
vt. ① 焊接
例 The cell door was sheet metal welded onto a frame of iron. 牢房的门是把金属板焊在铁框架上制成的。
例 He is a born leader, who welded a collection of gifted individualists into a real team. 他是个天生的领袖。他吸引了一批有才华的人，组成了一个真正的团队。

welfare
welfare　［ˈwelfeə(r)］
n. 福利〈同 well-being〉
例 These organizations have fought very hard for the rights and welfare of immigrants. 这些组织为了移民的权利和福利进行了艰苦的斗争。

well-being
well-being［'welbi:ɪŋ］
n. 安宁；福利〈同　welfare, benefit〉
例　The many foreign investments improved the well-being of the country's economy. 众多国外投资促进了该国经济的健康发展。

whim
whim［wɪm; (US)hwɪm］
n. 随意，冲动〈同 fancy, caprice, impulse〉
例　He has a whim for reading suddenly. 他突然心血来潮想看书。

whim
whim［wɪm; (US)hwɪm］
n. 心血来潮；怪念头〈同　impulse, caprice〉
例　People were uncertain about her whim to marry that rich old fellow. 人们无法确信她要嫁给那个有钱老男人的怪念头。

whip
whip　［wɪp; (US)hwɪp］
n. 鞭子
例 The cowboy bought a long, slender whip at the leather shop. 牛仔在皮革店里买了一条细长的鞭子。
v. 鞭打，抽打〈同 strike〉
例 The rider whipped the horse to make it go faster. 骑手用鞭子抽打马匹，让它跑得更快。

whisper
whisper　［ˈwɪspə(r)］
v. 低声说；耳语
例 You should whisper when you're in the library. 在图书馆的时候，你应该小声说话。
n. 低语
例 The librarian spoke in a whisper. 图书管理员小声地说话。

whittle
whittle　［ˈwɪtəl; (US)ˈhwɪtəl］
v. 削；削减〈同 cut〉
例 Susan whittled a stick with a knife to pass the time. 苏珊用刀子削着一根木棍，以此来打发时间。

wholesale
wholesale［'həʊlseɪl］
adj. ①批发的
例　A rise in the wholesale prices precedes a sharp increase in the retail level. 批发价格上涨之后，零售价格也开始大幅上涨。
例　Many people were angered by the wholesale slaughter of birds. 许多人被大批捕杀鸟类的行为激怒了。

wholesome
wholesome［'həʊlsəm］
例　The food we got at school was simple but wholesome. 我们在学校买的食物虽然简单，但是有益健康。

wholesome
wholesome［'həʊlsəm］
adj. 身心健康的；朝气蓬勃的〈同　healthful, beneficial〉
例　Janet is not really pretty, but her sparkling personality and wholesome charm make her very attractive. 珍妮特其实并不漂亮，但她活泼的个性和朝气蓬勃的魅力让她非常迷人。

wicked
wicked　［ˈwɪkɪd］
adj. 坏的，邪恶的〈同 evil〉
例 The wicked owner treated the employees badly. 那个邪恶的老板对员工态度非常恶劣。

widespread
widespread　［ˈwaɪdspred］
adj. 分布广的，普遍的〈同 extensive〉
例 The earthquake caused widespread damage. 地震造成了大范围的破坏。

wildlife
wildlife［'waɪldlaɪf］
n. 野生动植物〈同 animal〉
例　The conservation research project will concentrate on the wildlife habitats in the forest.（动物）保护研究项目将关注森林野生动物的习性。

wildlife
wildlife［'waɪldlaɪf］
n. 野生动植物〈同　wilding〉
例　The forest was preserved as a national park for the sake of the rare wildlife in it. 那片森林被评为国家公园，以保护里面的稀有野生动植物。

wisdom
wisdom　［ˈwɪzdəm］
n. 智慧〈同 intelligence〉
例 It is often said that wisdom is the product of experience. 人们经常说，智慧是经验的产物。

withdraw
withdraw　［wɪðˈdrɔː］
v. ① 撤退〈同 retreat〉
例 There's been a lot of debate about whether the UN should withdraw its troops from the country. 关于联合国是否应该从这个国家撤军的问题，仍存在许多争议。
例 Once in court, he withdrew the statement he'd made to the police. 一到法庭上，他却收回了向警方所做的供述。
联 withdrawal n. 收回；撤退，退回

wither
wither［'wɪðə(r)］

例　I forgot to water my plant and it withered. 我忘给植物浇水，它都枯萎了。

withhold
withhold［wɪð'həʊld］
v. 保留，抑制〈同 hold, keep〉
例　The bank withheld the deposit until he paid back his debt. 银行冻结了他的财产，直到他偿还完借款。

withstand
withstand　［wɪðˈstænd］
vt. 承受，抵住〈同 tolerate, resist〉
例 The training that astronauts receive teaches them how to withstand the hazards of space exploration. 宇航员所接受的培训，让他们学会了如何抵御太空探测的危险。

witness
witness　［ˈwɪtnəs］

例 The lady witnessed the murder. 那位女士目击了凶杀案。
n. 证人
例 John and Anne served as witnesses to the signing of the contract. 约翰和安妮担任了签署合同的见证人。
联 eyewitness n. 目击者，见证人

witty
witty［'wɪti］
adj. 机智的；风趣的〈同　clever; humorous〉
例　The politician always started his speeches with a witty joke in order to get the audience smiling. 为了引观众发笑，那个政治家的演讲总会以一个诙谐的笑话开场。

wonder
wonder　［ˈwʌndə(r)］
n. 奇迹；惊奇
例 Mount Everest is one of the natural wonders of the world. 珠穆朗玛峰是世界上的自然奇观之一。
vt. 对…感到惊奇，想知道〈同 be curious about〉
例 I wondered how he could finish so much work during a short period. 我想知道，他是如何在这么短时间内完成这么多工作的。
联 wonderful adj. 令人惊奇的，奇妙的，极好的

woods
woods［wʊdz］
n. 森林，树林〈同　forest, woodland〉
例　The man liked to go to the woods on the weekends to hunt for deer. 那个男人喜欢周末去树林里猎鹿。

worship
worship　［ˈwɜːʃɪp］
n./v. 崇拜，膜拜〈同 adore〉
例 He was the hero worshipped by the younger children. 他是孩子们崇拜的英雄。
v. 敬神
例 Tom worships at the temple every Sunday morning. 汤姆每周日上午都去寺庙拜神。

worthwhile
worthwhile　［ˌwɜːθˈwaɪl］
adj. 值得的，值得花时间、金钱或精力的〈同 rewarding〉
例 It may someday be worthwhile to try to recover uranium from seawater, but at present this process is prohibitively expensive. 或许有一天值得尝试从海水中回收铀，但目前这种工艺的成本还是太过高昂。
记 worth（价值）+ while→有价值的→值得的

wrap
wrap　［ræp］
vt. 裹，包，捆〈同 enclose〉
例 He wrapped his handkerchief round his bleeding finger. 他用手绢把流血的手指包了起来。
联 wrap up 胜利完成；包起来

wreath
wreath［ri:θ］
n. 花圈，花环
例　The bride wore a wreath on her head at the wedding. 婚礼上，新娘头戴花环。

wreck
wreck　［rek］
n. 失事；失事的残骸〈同 destruction〉
例 The divers found a wreck on the seabed. 潜水员在海床上发现了一艘沉船的残骸。
vt. 失事〈同 sink, destroy〉
例 The ship was wrecked when it hit the rocks in a storm. 船在暴风雨中撞上了岩石，结果失事了。
联 shipwreck n. 船只失事，海难

wrench
wrench［rentʃ］
n./v. 猛扭，猛拉〈同 twist〉
例　With a powerful wrench, I removed the lid from the pickle jar. 我用了个强有力的扳手，打开了泡菜坛上的盖子。

wring
wring［rɪŋ］
vt. 绞，拧，扭〈同　twist, squeeze〉
例　I wrung the water out of the sponge and wiped the counter. 我拧出海绵里的水，然后用它擦柜台。

wrinkle
wrinkle［'rɪŋkəl］
n. 皱纹，褶皱〈同 crease, furrow〉
例　The shirt has many wrinkles and should be ironed. 衬衫上有许多褶皱，应该熨一下。

yardstick
yardstick［'jɑ:dstɪk］
n. 码尺；准绳〈同　standard〉
例　He used a yardstick to measure the size of the room. 他用码尺来测量房间的大小。

yawn
yawn　［jɔːn］
n. 哈欠 vi. 打哈欠
例 He yawned and fell asleep. 他打了个哈欠，然后睡着了。

yell
yell［jel］
n./v. 大叫，呼喊〈同 shout〉
例　The patient let out a yell of pain when the doctor touched his broken bone. 当医生碰到病人的骨折处时，病人发出了痛苦的叫声。

yield
yield　［jiːld］
v. ① 生产；产生〈同 produce; bear〉
例 The cow won't yield much milk. 奶牛不怎么产奶了。
例 The child pleaded, but the parents wouldn't yield. 孩子不断恳求，但家长就是不让步。
n. 产量；收益〈同 output〉
例 An experienced farmer can estimate the annual yield of his acres with surprising accuracy. 一个有经验的农民可以估算出自己农田的年产量，而且准确度高得惊人。
联 yield to 屈服于

youngster
youngster［'jʌŋstə(r)］
n. 年轻人，少年〈同 youth〉
例　The youngster listened respectfully to his grandfather's stories. 年轻人恭敬地听着祖父的故事。

zenith
zenith［'zenɪθ; (US)'zɪ:nɪθ］
n. 顶点，顶峰〈同 pinnacle, peak〉
例　Bill Clinton reached the zenith of his career in 1992. 1992年，比尔·克林顿到达了事业的顶峰。

zenith
zenith［'zenɪθ］
n. 顶点，顶峰〈同　pinnacle, peak〉
例　Bill Clinton reached the zenith of his career in 1992. 1992年，比尔·克林顿达到了职业的巅峰。

zigzag
zigzag［'zɪgzæg］
adj. ①曲折的〈同　sinuous〉
例　Life today is nervous, sharp, and zigzag. 如今的生活紧张、快速、曲折。
例　Our journey lay through the zigzag path through the woods. 我们的行程是沿一条蜿蜒的小路穿过树林。

zone
zone［zəʊn］
n. 区域；地带〈同 region, district〉
例　The factory was built in an industrial zone. 那座工厂建在工业园区。

zoology
zoology［zəu'ɒləʤi］
n. 动物学
解　the science of animals
例　The diversity of species in the rainforest provides a wealth of knowledge for zoology. 热带雨林的物种多样性为动物学的研究提供了大量的知识。
同　zoologist n. 动物学家
